Freeing One of Two Slaves: Effect of Sale, Death, or Tadbir
Ruling on which slave becomes free when one is sold, dies, or made mudabbar, including intra-Hanafi dispute on intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which slave becomes free when one is sold, dies, or made mudabbar, and explain the Hanafi disagreement on whether intercourse with one female slave specifies the other as free.

Core Idea
Actions that remove ownership (sale, death, tadbir) specify the other slave; intercourse does not, according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a scenario where a master declares 'one of you is free' to two slaves. Subsequent events like sale or death determine which slave actually attains freedom. The ruling is extended to tadbir and umm walad. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the master has intercourse with one of two female slaves after such a declaration: does that action specify the other? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, and the mufta bihi is the opinion of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
When a master says 'one of you is free' to two slaves, then sells one, that one dies, or makes one a mudabbar, the other slave becomes free. Note the three triggers: sale, death, tadbir.
The text also applies to making one an umm walad.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Each trigger removes the possibility of freedom from that slave: death absolutely, sale removes freedom from the master's side, tadbir makes the slave already destined for future freedom. Hence only the other remains for immediate freedom.
The reasoning is based on conflict of objectives: sale aims at price, tadbir at deferred benefit, both incompatible with immediate freedom.
3
Extend to analogous cases
Gift with delivery and charity with delivery are like sale since they transfer ownership. Presenting for sale is annexed per Abu Yusuf.
The text also mentions that invalid sales (fasid) and sales with option are included due to the generality of the ruling.
4
Examine the dispute on intercourse
The Sahibayn argue that intercourse with one female slave shows the master retains ownership in her, so the other becomes free, analogous to divorce. Abu Hanifa disagrees, saying intercourse does not specify because the declaration was indefinite and the slave was specific.
This is the core intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states that Abu Hanifa's view is not given for fatwa ('لا يفتى به'), so the operative ruling is that of Sahibayn: the other becomes free after intercourse.
Understand the distinction: in marriage, intercourse indicates intent for offspring; with a slave, only desire, so no implication of retention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَبْدَيْهِ أَحَدُكُمَا حُرٌّ فَبَاعَ أَحَدَهُمَا أَوْ مَاتَ أَوْ قَالَ لَهُ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ بَعْدَ مَوْتِي عَتَقَ الْآخَرُ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَبْقَ مَحَلَّا لِلْعِتْقِ أَصْلًا بِالْمَوْتِ وَلِلْعِتْقِ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ بِالْبَيْعِ وَلِلْعِتْقِ مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهٍ بِالتَّدْبِيرِ فَتَعَيَّنَ الْآخَرُ وَلِأَنَّهُ بِالْبَيْعِ قَصَدَ الْوُصُولَ إِلَى الثَّمَنِ وَبِالتَّدْبِيرِ إِبْقَاءَ الِانْتِفَاعِ إِلَى مَوْتِهِ وَالْمَقْصُودَانِ يُنَافِيَانِ الْعِتْقَ الْمُلْتَزَمَ فَتَعَيَّنَ لَهُ الْآخَرُ دَلَالَةً وَكَذَا إِذَا اسْتَوْلَدَ أَحَدَهُمَا لِلْمَعْنَيَيْنِ وَلَا فَرْقَ بَيْنَ الْبَيْعِ الصَّحِيحِ وَالْفَاسِدِ مَعَ الْقَبْضِ وَبِدُونِهِ وَالْمُطْلَقِ وَبِشَرْطِ الْخِيَارِ لِأَحَدِ الْمُتَعَاقِدَيْنِ لِإِطْلَاقِ جَوَابِ الْكِتَابِ وَالْمَعْنَى مَا قُلْنَا وَالْعَرْضُ عَلَى الْبَيْعِ مُلْحَقٌ بِهِ فِي الْمَحْفُوظِ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَالْهِبَةُ وَالتَّسْلِيمُ وَالصَّدَقَةُ وَالتَّسْلِيمُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْبَيْعِ لِأَنَّهُ تَمْلِيكٌ وَكَذَلِكَ لَوْ قَالَ لِامْرَأَتَيْهِ إِحْدَاكُمَا طَالِقٌ ثُمَّ مَاتَتْ إِحْدَاهُمَا لِمَا قُلْنَا وَكَذَا لَوْ وَطِئَ إِحْدَاهُمَا لِمَا نُبَيِّنُ وَلَوْ قَالَ لِأَمَتَيْهِ إِحْدَاكُمَا حُرَّةٌ ثُمَّ جَامَعَ إِحْدَاهُمَا لَمْ يَعْتِقِ الْأُخْرَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا يَعْتِقُ لِأَنَّ الْوَطْءَ لَا يَحِلُّ إِلَّا فِي الْمِلْكِ حُرَّةً فَكَانَ بِالْوَطْءِ مُسْتَبْقِيًا الْمِلْكَ فِي الْمَوْطُوءَةِ فَتَعَيَّنَتِ الْأُخْرَى لِزَوَالِهِ بِالْعِتْقِ كَمَا فِي الطَّلَاقِ وَلَهُ أَنَّ الْمِلْكَ قَائِمٌ فِي الْمَوْطُوءَةِ لِأَنَّ الْإِنْقَاعَ فِي الْمُنْكَرَةِ وَهِيَ مُعَيَّنَةٌ فَكَانَ وَطْؤُهَا حَلَالًا فَلَا يُجْعَلُ بَيَانًا وَلِهَذَا حَلَّ وَطْؤُهُمَا عَلَى مَذْهَبِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يُفْتَى بِهِ ثُمَّ يُقَالُ الْعِتْقُ غَيْرُ نَازِلٍ قَبْلَ الْبَيَانِ لِتَعَلُّقِهِ بِهِ أَوْ يُقَالُ نَازِلٌ فِي الْمُنْكَرَةِ فَيَظْهَرُ فِي حَقِّ حُكْمٍ تَقْبَلُهُ وَالْوَطْءُ يُصَادِقُ الْمُعَيَّنَةَ بِخِلَافِ الطَّلَاقِ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ الْأَصْلِيَّ مِنَ النِّكَاحِ الْوَلَدُ وَقَصْدُ الْوَلَدِ بِالْوَطْءِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى اسْتِبْقَاءِ الْمِلْكِ فِي الْمَوْطُوءَةِ صِيَانَةً لِلْوَلَدِ أَمَّا الْأَمَةُ فَالْمَقْصُودُ مِنْ وَطْئِهَا قَضَاءُ الشَّهْوَةِ دُونَ الْوَلَدِ فَلَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى الِاسْتِبْقَاءِ
And whoever says to his two slaves, 'One of you is free,' then sells one of them, or one dies, or says to him, 'You are free after my death,' the other becomes free, because no place for freedom remains at all by death, and freedom from his side by sale, and freedom from every aspect by tadbir, so the other becomes specific. And because by sale he intended to obtain the price, and by tadbir to preserve benefit until his death, and the two objectives conflict with the committed freedom, so the other becomes specific by implication. Similarly, if he makes one of them an umm walad (by impregnating), due to the two meanings. And there is no difference between a valid sale and an invalid one with or without possession, and absolute or with a condition of option for one of the two contracting parties, due to the generality of the answer of the book and the meaning we stated. And presenting for sale is annexed to it in what is preserved from Abu Yusuf. And gift with delivery and charity with delivery are like sale because it is a transfer of ownership. Similarly, if he says to his two wives, 'One of you is divorced,' then one of them dies, (the other becomes specific) due to what we said. Similarly, if he has intercourse with one of them, for what we will explain. And if he says to his two female slaves, 'One of you is free,' then he has intercourse with one of them, the other does not become free according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: She becomes free, because intercourse is not lawful except in ownership of a free woman, so by intercourse he is preserving ownership in the one he had intercourse with, so the other becomes specific due to its removal by freedom, as in divorce. And for him (Abu Hanifa) that ownership remains in the one with whom he had intercourse because the declaration of freedom is in the indefinite, and she is specific, so his intercourse with her was lawful, so it is not made a specification. For this reason, intercourse with both is lawful according to his school, except that it is not given for fatwa. Then it is said: Freedom does not descend before specification due to its attachment to it, or it is said: It descends in the indefinite, so it appears in terms of a ruling that accepts it, and intercourse affirms the specific one, unlike divorce because the original purpose of marriage is offspring, and the intention of offspring by intercourse indicates preservation of ownership in the one with whom intercourse occurred for the protection of the child. As for the female slave, the purpose of intercourse is fulfillment of desire without offspring, so it does not indicate preservation.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on manumission of one of two slaves. It begins by stating the general rule: if a master says to two slaves 'one of you is free,' then subsequently sells one, that one dies, or the master makes him a mudabbar (freed upon the master's death), then the other slave becomes free. The reasoning is that death removes the possibility of freedom entirely; sale removes freedom from the master's side; and tadbir removes freedom from every aspect since the slave is already designated for future freedom. Thus only the other slave remains as a candidate for the immediate freedom. The author then extends the rule to cases where one slave is made an umm walad (by impregnating her), and clarifies that all types of sale—valid or invalid with or without possession, absolute or with option—are the same because the ruling is general. Abu Yusuf adds that presenting for sale is included. Gifts and charities with delivery are analogous to sale. The same principle applies to wives (divorce) and to female slaves with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. Sahibayn argue that intercourse with one female slave indicates the master considers her his property (instead of free), so the other becomes free. Abu Hanifa counters that the act of declaring freedom was in the indefinite, while the intercourse was with a specific slave; it does not specify which slave was meant. Therefore, intercourse with both is lawful in his view, though the fatwa is on the opinion of Sahibayn. The difference between marriage and slavery is that marriage aims at offspring, so intercourse shows intent to keep the wife in ownership for the child's sake; with a slave, only desire is sought, so intercourse does not indicate preservation of ownership.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A type of manumission where a slave is freed upon the master's death.
استيلاد (istilaad): Making a female slave an umm walad by impregnating her, which eventually leads to her freedom upon the master's death.
بيان (bayan): Specification or clarification of an ambiguous statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master tells two slaves 'one of you is free' and then sells one of them, which slave becomes free?
A) The one who was sold
B) The one who remains
C) Both become free
D) Neither becomes free

Key Takeaway
When a master ambiguously declares freedom for one of two slaves, subsequent actions that remove ownership (sale, death, tadbir) specify the other slave; intercourse, per the mufta bihi, also serves as specification for the other slave in the case of female slaves.

Freeing a Slave if First Child is a Boy: Ambiguous Birth of Twins
Ruling on ambiguous firstborn with conditional manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave gives birth to twins of opposite sexes with unknown order and explain the reasoning based on probability and dependency.

Core Idea
Half-free mother, half-free daughter, fully enslaved son — ambiguity in condition splits ownership.

This passage addresses a conditional manumission where the condition depends on the order of birth, but the order is unknown. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling balancing both possible outcomes, demonstrating the use of probability and the principle that a child's status follows the mother (taba).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the ambiguity
The master's statement makes the mother's freedom conditional on the firstborn being a boy. The ambiguity arises because she gives birth to twins, a boy and a girl, and the order is unknown.
2
List the two possible orders
Two scenarios: (1) boy born first, (2) girl born first. Each leads to different legal outcomes for the mother and children.
3
Determine status in each scenario
If boy first: condition met, mother becomes free; daughter born after free mother is free; son is born free (though not mentioned, he would be free). If girl first: condition not met, mother remains slave; daughter and son are slaves as they follow mother's status.
In Hanafi law, a child's status is determined by the mother's status at the time of birth.
4
Apply the principle of equal probability
Since both orders are equally possible, we take an average: mother is half free, half slave; daughter's status mirrors the mother's because she is a dependent (taba); son is a slave because in one scenario he is free and in the other a slave, but the text rules him a slave (some accounts say he remains a slave due to original status or other principles).
The son's enslavement is a specific Hanafi ruling; the text states 'the boy is a slave'.
5
Conclude the final ruling
Thus, half of the mother and half of the daughter become free, and the son remains entirely a slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِأَمَتِهِ إِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ وَلَدٍ تَلِدِينَ غُلَامًا فَأَنْتِ حُرَّةٌ فَوَلَدَتْ غُلَامًا وَجَارِيَةً وَلَا يُدْرَى أَيُّهُمَا وَلَدَ أَوَّلًا عَتَقَ نِصْفُ الْأَمَةِ وَنِصْفُ الْجَارِيَةِ وَالْغُلَامُ عَبْدٌ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا تَعْتِقُ فِي حَالٍ وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا وَلَدَتِ الْغُلَامَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ الْأَمَةُ بِالشَّرْطِ وَالْجَارِيَةُ لِكَوْنِهَا تَبَعًا لَهَا إِذِ الْأَمَةُ حُرَّةٌ حِينَ وَلَدَتْهَا وَتُرَقُ فِي حَالٍ وَهُوَ مَا إِذَا وَلَدَتِ الْجَارِيَةَ أَوَّلًا
And whoever says to his female slave, 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, then you are free,' and she gives birth to a boy and a girl, and it is not known which of them was born first, half of the female slave and half of the female child become free, and the boy is a slave. Because each one of them (the mother and the daughter) becomes free in one circumstance: that is, when she gives birth to the boy first, the mother (becomes free) by the condition, and the daughter because she is a dependent of her, as the mother is free when she gave birth to her; and she (the mother) remains a slave in another circumstance: that is, when she gives birth to the girl first.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on a conditional manumission case. A master says to his female slave: 'If the first child you give birth to is a boy, you are free.' She gives birth to twins, a boy and a girl, but it is unknown which was born first. The ruling is that half of the mother and half of the daughter become free, while the son remains a slave. The reasoning is based on considering both possible scenarios: if the boy was born first, then the condition is fulfilled and the mother becomes free; the daughter, being born after the mother is free, is born free as well. If the girl was born first, then the condition is not fulfilled, so the mother remains a slave; the daughter follows her mother's status and is also a slave. Since both scenarios are equally possible, the mother's status is half free and half slave; the same applies to the daughter. The son is a slave in both scenarios because he is born first in one scenario (making him free) but in the other scenario he is born after the girl (making him a slave); but the text says he is a slave, implying that in the scenario where he is born first, the mother is free and he is free? Wait: The text says 'the boy is a slave.' That is because if the boy was born first, the mother becomes free by condition, and the boy being the firstborn male is not subject to the condition (the condition only applies to the mother's freedom). Actually in the Hanafi school, if a slave gives birth to a child, the child follows the status of the mother at the time of birth. So if the boy is born first while the mother is still a slave (since the condition is about the first child being a boy, but the mother is only freed upon that birth, so at the moment of birth she is still a slave? There is a subtlety: The condition is 'If the first child is a boy, you are free.' At the instant of the boy's birth, the condition is met, so the mother becomes free from that instant. Thus the boy would be born free? But the text says the boy is a slave. This requires clarification: According to Hanafi fiqh, the condition is suspensive (ta'liq), so the freedom occurs upon fulfillment of the condition. When the boy is born, the condition is fulfilled and the mother becomes free at that moment. However, the child's status is determined at the moment of birth, and if the mother becomes free at that moment, the child is born free. But the text here says the boy is a slave. This suggests that the boy is a slave because in the scenario where the boy is born first, the mother becomes free but the boy himself? Actually, the condition only applies to the mother; the boy is not being freed by the condition. The boy's status is based on the mother's status at the time of his birth. If the mother becomes free at the moment of his birth, then he is born free. So why is he a slave? The answer is that the text's ruling considers the uncertainty: because we don't know which was born first, we treat the boy as a slave in all scenarios? The text says: 'the boy is a slave' without qualification. This is the Hanafi ruling: in case of ambiguity, the boy is considered a slave. This is because in the scenario where the girl is born first, the boy is born after and the mother is a slave, so he is a slave. In the scenario where the boy is born first, he would be born free but the mother free as well; however, since we cannot determine, we take the more cautious approach? Or perhaps the Hanafi rule is that the child's status is determined by the mother's status at the time of conception? Let's check standard Hanafi texts: In Al-Hidayah, the ruling is that half of the mother and half of the daughter are free, and the son is a slave. The reasoning is that in one scenario the son is born when the mother is a slave (if daughter first), and in the other scenario he is born when the mother is free (if son first). But then why is he a slave? Actually, the correct ruling from the Hanafi school is that the son is a slave. This is because in the case where the son is born first, the mother becomes free upon his birth, but the son himself is not freed by the condition; he is born to a free mother? That would make him free. So there is inconsistency. I recall that the Hanafi position is that the son is a slave because the mother's freedom is contingent on the first child being a boy; when the boy is born first, the condition is fulfilled and the mother becomes free, but the boy himself remains a slave because he was conceived while the mother was a slave? Or because the condition only applies to the mother. Actually, in Hanafi law, a child born to a slave woman is a slave unless the mother is freed before or at the time of birth. If the mother becomes free at the exact time of birth, the child is free. So if the boy is born first, he would be free. But the text says he is a slave, implying that in both possible orders, he ends up a slave. This suggests a different interpretation: Perhaps the condition is interpreted as 'if the first child (i.e., the one born first) is a boy, then you are free.' So if the boy is born first, then the mother is free from that instant, and the boy, being the first child, is not himself freed by this statement; he remains a slave because he was born to a slave mother at the moment of his birth? But if she becomes free simultaneously with his birth, he is born free. This is a nuanced point. For the purpose of this lesson, we will explain the ruling as given: half of mother and daughter free, son slave, because in one scenario the mother is free and daughter dependent, in the other the mother is slave and daughter dependent; the son is slave in both scenarios? Actually the son is slave in one scenario (if daughter first, mother slave, son slave) and free in the other (if son first, mother free, son free). So why is he considered a slave? The answer is that the text says 'the boy is a slave' because the probability is that he is a slave in one scenario and free in another, but the Hanafi ruling gives him the status of slavery due to the original state (istishab) or because of a principle. The commentary should follow the text exactly: the boy is a slave. We will not go beyond the text. For the teacher's commentary, we can say: The ruling is based on the two probabilities. The mother is half free because she could be free (if boy first) or slave (if girl first). The daughter is half free because she could be free (born after free mother) or slave (born after slave mother). The boy is a slave because in the scenario where he is born first, the mother becomes free but he is not freed by the statement; he remains a slave? Actually, in standard Hanafi fiqh, if a pregnant slave woman is freed, her fetus is also freed if born after the freedom. But here the freedom occurs at the moment of birth. The difference might be that the condition is suspensive, so the freedom occurs after the boy's birth? The text says العتق غير نازل قبل البيان? No that's from another context. For simplicity, we'll state the ruling as given.

Key Terms
تبع (taba): Dependent; the child follows the mother's status in slavery or freedom.

Key Takeaway
When a conditional manumission depends on an unknown order of birth, the mother and daughter become half-free, and the son remains a slave.

Ambiguous Manumission After Intercourse: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous manumission after intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi positions on ambiguous manumission after intercourse and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When a master says 'one of you is free' to two slave-girls and then has intercourse with one, the Sahibayn hold the other is freed; Abu Hanifa disagrees, but the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning a master's ambiguous statement freeing one of two slave-girls, followed by intercourse with one. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on whether the other slave-girl is automatically freed. The passage also draws analogies from divorce and sale to illustrate the underlying principles of intention and specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the positions
State the scenario: master says 'one of you is free' to two slave-girls, then has intercourse with one. Identify that Abu Hanifa holds the other is not freed, while Sahibayn hold the other is freed.
This is the central factual situation for the dispute.
2
Explain Sahibayn's proof
Sahibayn argue that intercourse with one slave-girl indicates retention of ownership over her, so the other must be the one freed, similar to the divorce analogy where intercourse with one wife specifies her as undivorced.
The illa (effective cause) is that the act of intercourse shows which slave-girl the master intended to keep.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa contends that the ambiguous statement (nakirah) remains unresolved because intercourse is not a clear expression of specification; the master could intend mere pleasure, not procreation, so the act does not clarify the manumission.
The key distinction is that in divorce, the purpose is to dissolve marriage, while in manumission, the purpose of intercourse matters.
4
Analyze the author's response to objections
The author addresses a potential contradiction: if the statement did not effect freedom, it becomes meaningless; but if it did, both slave-girls would be free since the statement was ambiguous. The response is that freedom does not occur until specification, or that freedom occurred in an indefinite sense, which does not specify the actual freed individual.
This clarifies that the master's statement is not void but suspended until clarification.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author states that Abu Hanifa's opinion is not given as fatwa; the relied-upon position is that of Sahibayn. Thus, in practice, the other slave-girl is freed.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلق ہے اور تمام صورتوں کو شامل ہے۔ ان سے مراد وہی دو صورتیں ہیں جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں یعنی وہی دو جہیں جو اوپر ذکر کی گئی ہیں۔ پھر امام ابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ سے یہ روایت موجود ہے کہ اگر دونوں میں سے ایک کو غلاموں کی منڈی یا بازار میں بیچنے کی غرض سے لے گئے تو یہ بھی بیچنے کے حکم میں ہے۔ یعنی دوسرا غلام آزادی کے لئے متعین ہو گیا اور ہبہ کر کے حوالہ کر دینا یا صدقہ میں دے کر حوالہ کر دینا بھی بیچنے کے ہی حکم میں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک ایسا بھی کرتا ہے۔ ( یعنی جس غلام کو دوسرے کی ملکیت میں دے دیا تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہوگی کہ اسے آزاد نہیں کیا ہے۔ اسلئے لامحالہ ان دونوں میں سے اس کے علاوہ وہ دوسرا غلام ہی آزاد ہوگا)۔ اور اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنی دو بیویوں کو کہا کہ تم میں سے ایک کو طلاق ہے اور اس کے بعد ان دونوں میں ایک مرگئی۔ تو طلاق کے لئے دوسری (زندہ) متعین ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ مردہ اب محل طلاق باقی نہیں رہی۔ اسی دلیل کی بناء پر جو ہم نے پہلے بیان کر دی ہے۔ اسی طرح اس صورت میں بھی کہ اگر دو میں سے کسی ایک کے ساتھ اس نے ہمبستری کر لی ہو۔ تو بھی یہی دوسری طلاق کے لئے متعین ہو جائے گی۔ جس کی وجہ ہم آئندہ بیان کریں گے اور اگر کسی نے اپنی دو باندیوں سے کہا کہ تم دونوں میں سے ایک آزاد ہے۔ پھر ان میں سے ایک سے ہمبستری کر لی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دوسری آزاد نہ ہوگی اور صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما نے کہا ہے کہ دوسری آزاد ہو جائیگی۔ کیونکہ ولی تو صرف اپنی مملوکہ عورت سے ہی حلال ہوتی ہے۔ جب ان دونوں میں سے ایک آزاد ہے تو وہ اب اس کے لئے حرام ہو چکی ہے اور جس سے اس نے ولی کر لی ہے اس میں اس نے اپنی مملکیت باقی رکھی ہے اور وہی اس کے لئے حلال رہی ہے اور دوسری آزادی کے لئے متعین ہو گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ آزاد ہو جانے کی وجہ سے اس کی ملکیت ختم ہوگئی ہے۔ جیسے طلاق میں ہوتا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس باندی سے ولی کی اس میں ملکیت باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ آزادی کا واقع کرنا ایک نکرہ یعنی غیر معین میں ہے اور جس سے وطی کی وہ معین ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی وطی حلال تھی پس ایسا کرنا اس کے مبہم قول کا بیان نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق دونوں سے ولی حلال ہے۔ لیکن اس قول پر فتوی نہیں دیا جائے گا ( اب اگر یہ سوال کیا جائے کہ اگر مولی کے کلام سے آزادی واقع نہیں ہوئی تو وہ کلام ہی مہمل ہو گیا اور اگر آزادی ہوگئی تو دونوں سے ولی کس طرح حلال ہوئی ۔ تو مصنف نے اس کے جواب میں کہا) پھر یوں کہا جائے کہ جب تک اس کی وضاحت نہ کر دے آزادی واقع نہیں ہوئی۔ کیونکہ آزادی کا واقع ہونا بیان پر ہی وقوف ہے۔ یا یوں جواب دیا جائے کہ غیر معین میں آزادی واقع ہوئی ہے۔ اس لئے ایسا حکم اس میں ظاہر ہو گا جس کو نکرہ قبول کرتا ہو۔ حالانکہ یہاں ایک معینہ باندی سے وطی ہوئی ہے۔ یعنی جس سے وطی کرے وہی معینہ ہو جائینگی۔ مگر طلاق میں یہ بات نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نکاح سے مقصود اصلی ، اولاد کا پیدا ہونا ہے اور وطی سے اولاد کا ارادہ کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس نے جس باندی سے ولی کی ہے اسے اپنی ملکیت میں باقی رکھا ہے۔ تا کہ بچہ کی حفاظت ہوتی رہے اور اس بات کے بغیر اگر باندی سے ولی کرے تو اس سے صرف اپنی خواہش نفسانی پوری کرنی ہوگی اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہونا مقصود نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے ایسی وطی اس بات کی دلیل بالکل نہیں ہوگی کہ اس نے ملکیت باقی رکھی ہے۔
It is absolute and includes all cases. By them is meant the two cases we have already explained, i.e., the two aspects mentioned above. Then there is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that if one of the two is taken to the slave market or bazaar for the purpose of selling, this is also in the ruling of selling. That is, the other slave is designated for freedom. And giving as a gift and handing over, or giving as charity and handing over, are also in the ruling of selling, because the owner also does this. (i.e., giving a slave into the ownership of another is evidence that he has not freed him. Therefore, inevitably, of the two, the other slave is the one freed). Similarly, if a man tells his two wives, 'One of you is divorced,' and then one of them dies, the other (living) is designated for divorce, because the dead one is no longer a valid subject for divorce. Based on the same reasoning we have already stated. Similarly, in the case where he has intercourse with one of the two, the other is still designated for divorce, for a reason we will explain later. And if someone tells his two slave-girls, 'One of you is free,' then has intercourse with one of them, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the other is not freed, but the Sahibayn have said that the other is freed. Because intercourse is only halal with one's own slave-girl. When one of the two is free, she becomes haram for him, and the one with whom he had intercourse, he has retained ownership over her, so she remains halal for him, and the other is designated for freedom, because due to being free, ownership over her has ended. As happens in divorce. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the slave-girl with whom he had intercourse, ownership remains, because the occurrence of freedom is in a nakirah (indefinite) and the one with whom he had intercourse is definite. Therefore, intercourse with her was halal, so this action cannot be an expression of his ambiguous statement. Thus, according to Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab, intercourse with both is halal, but this opinion is not given as a fatwa. (Now if it is asked that if freedom does not occur by the master's statement, then the statement becomes meaningless, and if freedom does occur, then how can intercourse with both be halal? The author answers:) Then it is said that freedom does not occur until he clarifies it, because the occurrence of freedom depends on expression. Or it is answered that freedom occurred in an indefinite sense, so the ruling that appears in it is that which the indefinite accepts, although here intercourse occurred with a specific slave-girl. That is, the one with whom he has intercourse becomes specified. But this is not the case in divorce, because the primary purpose of marriage is procreation, and intending offspring from intercourse is evidence that he has retained ownership of the slave-girl with whom he had intercourse, so that the child may be protected. Without this, if he has intercourse with the slave-girl, it is only to fulfill his carnal desire, and procreation is not intended. Therefore, such intercourse is absolutely not evidence that he retained ownership.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the issue of ambiguous manumission when one of two slave-girls has been freed in an unspecified manner. The discussion begins by establishing that if the master takes one of the two slaves to market for sale, that action indicates he did not intend to free that one, so the other is designated as the freed one. Similarly, gifting or giving in charity also designates the other as freed. The analogy of divorce is then drawn: if a man says 'one of you is divorced' to his two wives, and one dies, the living one is divorced; if he has intercourse with one, the other is divorced. This principle is extended to slave-girls. The core dispute is when a master says 'one of you is free' to two slave-girls, then has intercourse with one. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the slave-girl with whom he had intercourse is the one he retained ownership of, and the other is freed, similar to the divorce case where intercourse specifies the wife not divorced. Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that the ambiguous statement remains unresolved, and intercourse with one does not specify the other as freed, because the statement is indefinite and intercourse is not a clear expression of intention. However, Abu Hanifa's opinion is not relied upon for fatwa; the position of Sahibayn is considered stronger. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if the statement did not effect freedom, it becomes meaningless, but if it did, how can intercourse with both be halal? The response is that freedom is not realized until specification, or that the freedom occurred in an indefinite sense and the intercourse specifies only the action, not the statement. The distinction from divorce is that in divorce, the purpose is to dissolve marriage, while in manumission, retaining ownership for procreation is a key consideration. Thus, intercourse with intent for offspring indicates continued ownership, but not all intercourse has that intent.

Key Terms
مبہم (mubham): Ambiguous; a statement that does not specify which individual is intended.
نکرہ (nakirah): Indefinite noun; in context, the freedom was expressed as 'one' without specifying which.
معین (mu'ayyan): Specified; the slave-girl with whom intercourse occurred becomes definite.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a master says to two slave-girls 'one of you is free' and then has intercourse with one, what is the ruling?
A) Both remain enslaved until specification.
B) The one with whom he had intercourse is freed.
C) The other slave-girl is freed.
D) The master must free both.

Key Takeaway
In ambiguous manumission followed by intercourse, the Hanafi fatwa (following Sahibayn) holds that the other slave-girl is freed because intercourse indicates retained ownership of the one copulated with.

Conditional Manumission and Unknown Birth Order
Ruling on ambiguous birth order in conditional manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave-girl gives birth to a boy and a girl with unknown order, apply the rules of nukool (refusal of oath) to claims of freedom, and distinguish the status of the son from the mother and daughter.

Core Idea
When birth order is unknown, partial freedom is ruled; the master's oath or refusal decides actual freedom.

A master conditions freedom on the first child being male. The slave-girl then delivers twins – a boy and a girl – but the order is unknown. How does Hanafi law resolve this? The answer involves a blend of freedom and slavery for the mother and daughter, while the son remains fully enslaved. The passage also details the procedural role of oaths and refusal (nukool) when claims are made. This lesson unpacks the logic and the practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the event
The master said: 'If your first child is a boy, you are free.' The slave-girl gives birth to a boy and a girl; the first-born is unknown.
2
Determine the legal status of each person
Analyze the three possibilities (boy first, girl first, unknown) and note that the son is born before any freedom, so he remains a slave. The mother and daughter are half-free because of the two scenarios.
Half-free means each must work to compensate half their value.
3
Understand the claim and oath procedure
When the mother claims the boy was first, the master denies. The master's word is accepted with an oath. If he swears, no freedom; if he refuses (nukool), the mother and a minor daughter are freed.
Nukool is effective because freedom is a pure benefit for the slave.
4
Distinguish the adult daughter scenario
If the daughter is adult and does not claim, only the mother is freed by nukool. If the adult daughter claims on her own, she is freed but not the mother.
The claim must come from the one who benefits.
5
Note the oath on knowledge
The master is sworn 'on his knowledge' because it concerns the action of another (the slave-girl).
This is a Hanafi rule for oaths on another's act.

وَ مَنْ قَالَ لِاَمَتِهِ إِنْ كَانَ اَوَّلُ وَلَدِتَلِدِينَ غُلَامًا فَانْتِ حُرَّةٌ فَوَلَدَتْ غُلَامًا وَجَارِيَةً وَلَا يُدْرَى أَيُّهُمَا وَلَدُاَوَّلٍ عَتَقَ نِصْفُ الْامَ وَ نِصْفُ الْجَارِيَةِ وَالْغُلَامُ عَبْدَلاَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا تَعْتِقُ فِي حَالٍ وَهُوَمَا إِذَا وَلَدَتِ الْغُلَامَ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ الأم بِالشَّرْطِ وَالْجَارِيَةُ لِكَوْنِهَا تَبْعًا لَهَا إِذِ الْامُ حُرَّةٌ حِيْنَ وَلَدَتْهَا وَتُرَقُ فِي حَالٍ وَهُوَمَا إِذَا وَلَدَتِ الْجَارِيَةَ أَوَّلًا
باب عتق احد العبدين. ۲۲ اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم لِعَدْمِ الشَّرْطِ فَيَعْتِقُ نِصْفُ كُلَّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا وَيَسْعَى فِي النِّصْفِ أَمَّا الْغُلَامُ يَرِقُ فِي الْحَالَيْنِ فَلِهَذَا يَكُونُ عَبْدَاوَانِ ادَّعَتِ الْاُمُّ اَنَّ الْغُلَامَ هُوَ الْمَوْلُودُ أَوَّلًا وَ انْكَرَ الْمَوْلَى وَالْجَارِيَةُ صَغِيرَةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ مَعَ الْيَمِينِ لِإِنْكَارِهِ شَرْطَ الْعِتْقِ فَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمْ وَإِنْ نَكَلَ عَتَقَتِ الْأُمُّ وَالْجَارِيَةُ لَانَّ دَعْوَى الْأُمِّ حُرِّيَّةَ الصَّغِيرَةِ مُعْتَبَرَةٌ لِكَوْنِهَا نَفْعًا مَحْضَافَاعْتُبِرَ النُّكُولُ فِي حَقِّ حُرِّيَّتِهِمَا فَعَتَقَتَا وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ كَبِيرَةً وَلَمْ تَدْعِ شَيْئًا وَالْمَسْأَلَة بِحَالِهَا عَتَقَتِ الأمُّ بِنُكُولِ الْمَوْلَى خَاصَّةٌ دُونَ الْجَارِيَةِ لِاَنَّ دَعْوَى الْامَ غَيْرَ مُعْتَبَرَةٍ فِي حَقِ الْجَارِيَةِ الْكَبِيرَةِ وَصِحَّةُ النُّكُول عَلَى الدَّعْوَى فَلَمْ يَظْهَرْ فِي حَقِ الْجَارِيَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ الْكَبِيرَةُ هِيَ الْمُدَّعِيَةُ لِسَبْقِ وِلَادَةِ الْغُلَامِ وَالامُ سَاكِنَةٌ يَثْبُتُ عِشقُ الْجَارِيَةِ بِنكُولِ الْمَوْلَى دُونَ الْامَ لِمَاقُلْنَا وَالتَّحْلِيْفَ عَلَى الْعِلْمِ فِيمَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّهُ اسْتِحْلَاتٌ عَلَى فِعْلِ الْغَيْرِ وَ بِهَدَ الْقَدْرِ يُعْرَفُ مَاذَكَرْ نَامِنَ الْوُجُوهِ فِي كِفَايَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى

آزاد ہونے سے پہلے ہی پیدا ہو چکا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ غلام ہی رہے گا اور اگر باندی نے یہ دعوی کیا کہ پہلے لڑکا پیدا ہوا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے مولی نے اس کا انکار کیا اور وہ لڑکی ابھی چھوٹی ہے تو قسم کے ساتھ موٹی کی بات مقبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس مولی نے باندی کی آزادی کی شرط کے پائے جانے سے انکار کیا ہے۔ البتہ اس کے ساتھ اس سے قسم بھی لی جائے گی ۔ اگر اس نے قسم کھائی تو ان تینوں میں سے کوئی بھی آزاد نہ ہو گا اور اگر مولی نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کیا تو ماں اور اس کی لڑکی آزاد ہو گی ۔ کیونکہ لڑکی کے متعلق اس کی ماں اس دعوئی کا کہ یہ لڑ کی آزاد پیدا ہوئی ہے اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ صرف نفع کی بات ہے۔ اس لئے مولی کا قسم سے انکار کرنا ماں اور لڑکی دونوں کے حق میں معتبر ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں آزاد ہو جائیں گی اور اگر یہ لڑکی بالغہ ہو اور اس نے اپنی آزادی کا خود دعوئی نہ کیا ہو اور باقی مسئلہ اسی حال پر ہو یعنی باندی نے پہلے لڑکے کے پیدا ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا ہومگر مولی نے نہیں مانا اور قسم سے بھی انکار کیا تو مولی کے قسم کے انکار سے فقط ماں آزاد ہوگی مگر لڑ کی آزاد نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بالغہ لڑکی کے بارے میں ماں کا دعویٰ کرنا کہ یہ آزاد ہے اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قسم کے انکار سے اسی صورت میں اقرار مانا جاتا ہے۔ جب کہ اس نے خود ہی کسی بات کا دعویٰ کیا ہو اور موجودہ مسئلہ میں چونکہ بالغہ لڑکی کی طرف سے کوئی دعوی نہیں ہے تو اس کے بارے میں قسم سے انکار کا بھی اثر نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ اگر بالغہ لڑکی خود ہی دعویٰ کرے کہ پہلے لڑکا پیدا ہوا تھا اور اس کی ماں اس وقت خاموش رہی تو موٹی کے قسم کے انکار سے یہ لڑ کی آزاد ہو جائے گی مگر ماں آزاد نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ ماں کا دعویٰ لڑکی کے حق میں معتبر نہ ہوگا اور جن صورتوں میں مولی سے قسم لینے کی ضرورت ہو ان میں اس سے اس کے علم کی بنا پر قسم لی جائے گی کہ واقعہ میں نہیں جانتا ہوں کہ پہلے لڑکا پیدا ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہاں پر غیر کے فعل و عمل پر اس سے قسم لی جائے گی
Explanation: It is clear from the translation. The master said to his slave-girl, 'If you first give birth to a child, then you are free.' She gave birth to a boy and a girl, and it is not known whether the boy or the girl was born first. So the mother and her daughter are each half free, but the boy remains entirely a slave. Because each of the two (mother and girl) is free in one scenario: when the boy is born first, the mother becomes free by the condition, and the girl follows her since the mother was free when she gave birth to her; and they are enslaved in another scenario: when the girl is born first, due to the condition not being met. So half of each of them is freed, and they must work to pay half their value. As for the boy, he remains a slave in both scenarios, because he was born before the mother's freedom, so he is a slave. If the mother claims that the boy was born first, but the master denies it, and the daughter is a minor, then the statement of the master is accepted with an oath, because he denies the condition of freedom. If he swears, none of them are freed. If he refuses to take the oath, the mother and the daughter are freed, because the mother's claim of freedom for the minor daughter is considered, as it is purely beneficial. So the refusal to take the oath is considered in respect of both their freedoms, so they are freed. If the daughter is an adult and does not claim anything, and the case is the same, then only the mother is freed by the master's refusal to take the oath, not the daughter, because the mother's claim is not considered regarding the adult daughter, and the validity of the refusal based on a claim applies only to the claimant. So it does not affect the daughter. If the adult daughter herself claims that the boy was born first, and the mother is silent, then the daughter's freedom is established by the master's refusal to take the oath, but not the mother's, for the reason we stated. And in cases where an oath is required from the master, he is made to swear based on his knowledge, because it is an oath regarding the action of another. By this much, what we have mentioned is known from the various aspects in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed ruling on conditional manumission when the order of birth is unknown. The core case: a master tells his slave-girl that if her first child is a boy, she is free. She then gives birth to a boy and a girl, but it is unknown which was born first. The ruling is that both the mother and the daughter are half-free, meaning half of each is freed, and they must work to compensate the master for half their value. The son remains a full slave because he was born before any freeing occurred. The reasoning is based on probability: if the boy was born first, the mother becomes free at that moment, and the daughter, born afterwards, is free because she was born to a free mother. If the girl was born first, the condition is not met, so the mother remains a slave, and the daughter is also a slave. Since the actual order is unknown, the legal status is a blend: half freedom for both mother and daughter. The son, however, was born in either case while the mother was still a slave, so he remains a slave. The passage then discusses procedural scenarios regarding claims and oaths: if the mother claims the boy was first and the master denies, the master's word is taken with an oath. If the master refuses the oath (nukool), the mother and a minor daughter are freed, but not an adult daughter who does not claim. An adult daughter can claim on her own behalf. These rules show how Hanafi fiqh handles uncertainty in conditional manumission, balancing the master's rights and the slave's potential freedom.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Condition; here, the condition is that the first child must be male for freedom to occur.
ولادت (wiladat): Birth; the event of childbirth.
نکول (nukool): Refusal to take an oath; legal consequence is that the opposing party's claim is accepted.
قسم (qasam): Oath; the master is made to swear by his knowledge of the birth order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a slave-girl gives birth to a boy and a girl and the order is unknown, what is the status of the son?
A) He is half-free like his mother.
B) He is fully free.
C) He remains a full slave.
D) His status is pending until the order is known.

Key Takeaway
Conditional manumission with unknown birth order results in half-freedom for the mother and daughter, while the son remains a full slave; procedural claims and oaths can alter the final status.

Conditional Emancipation with Unknown Birth Order
Ruling on conditional freedom when birth order of twins is unknown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional emancipation when the birth order of twins is unknown and apply it to scenarios with claims and oaths.

Core Idea
Uncertainty divides freedom: mother and daughter half-free, son fully enslaved.

This lesson examines a nuanced case from the Hanafi school: a master conditionally frees his slave woman upon the birth of a male child first, but she gives birth to twins of unknown order. The ruling hinges on legal uncertainty and the principle that freedom is partial when conditions are partly met. We'll also explore how claims and oaths affect the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statement
The master says: 'If your first child is a male, you are free.' This creates a conditional freedom tied to the first birth's gender.
The condition is attached to the first-born's gender, not the birth order itself.
2
Analyze the twin birth scenarios
Two possibilities: boy born first (condition met, mother free at moment of birth, daughter born later free) or girl born first (condition fails, both slaves). Since order is unknown, each is half-free.
Son is always a slave because in both scenarios he is born before mother's freedom.
3
Determine the son's status
In both possible orders, the son is born while the mother is still a slave. If boy is first, condition is met at his birth, but he is born before mother becomes free; if girl is first, condition fails entirely. So he remains a full slave.
This is a key point: the son never benefits from the condition.
4
Examine claim and oath scenarios
If the mother claims the boy was first and master denies, master's word with oath is accepted. If he refuses oath, mother and minor daughter become free. For an adult daughter, her own claim is needed.
Oath is on knowledge since it concerns another's action.
5
Synthesize the legal principles
The rulings apply the maxim that certainty (of slavery) is not removed by doubt, and that claims benefiting a minor are accepted. The son's slavery is certain; partial freedom arises from the unresolved ambiguity.
These principles are central to Hanafi jurisprudence on emancipation.

باب عتق احد العبدين. ۲۲ اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم لِعَدَمِ الشَّرْطِ فَيَعْتِقُ نِصْفُ كُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا وَيَسْعَى فِي النِّصْفِ أَمَّا الْغُلَامُ فَيَرِقُّ فِي الْحَالَيْنِ فَلِهَذَا يَكُونُ عَبْدًا وَإِنِ ادَّعَتِ الْأُمُّ أَنَّ الْغُلَامَ هُوَ الْمَوْلُودُ أَوَّلًا وَأَنْكَرَ الْمَوْلَى وَالْجَارِيَةُ صَغِيرَةٌ فَالْقَوْلُ قَوْلُهُ مَعَ الْيَمِينِ لِإِنْكَارِهِ شَرْطَ دُونَ الْجَارِيَةِ لِأَنَّ دَعْوَى الْأُمِّ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَرَةٍ فِي حَقِّ الْجَارِيَةِ الْكَبِيرَةِ وَصِحَّةُ النُّكُولِ عَلَى الدَّعْوَى فَلَمْ يَظْهَرْ فِي حَقِّ الْجَارِيَةِ وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ الْكَبِيرَةُ هِيَ الْمُدَّعِيَةُ لِسَبْقِ وِلَادَةِ الْغُلَامِ وَالْأُمُّ سَاكِنَةٌ يَثْبُتُ عِتْقُ الْجَارِيَةِ بِنُكُولِ الْمَوْلَى دُونَ الْأُمِّ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَالتَّحْلِيفُ عَلَى الْعِلْمِ فِيمَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّهُ اسْتِحْلَافٌ عَلَى فِعْلِ الْغَيْرِ وَبِهَذَا الْقَدْرِ يُعْرَفُ مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ مِنَ الْوُجُوهِ فِي كِفَايَةِ الْمُنْتَهَى ترجمہ اگر مولی نے اپنی باندی سے یہ کہا آدھی آدھی آزاد ہوں گی مگر لڑکا اپنی جگہ پورا غلام ہی رہے گا۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی یہ حالت ہے کہ ایک حالت میں آزاد ہو جاتی ہے جبکہ واقعتا پہلے لڑکا ہی پیدا ہوا ہو اور اس کے تابع ہو کر لڑکی بھی آزاد ہو جائیگی کیونکہ یہاں یہ بات لازم آتی ہے کہ یہ لڑ کی جس وقت پیدا ہوئی اس کی ماں آزاد ہو چکی تھی۔ یعنی جبکہ اسے لڑکا پیدا ہوا تھا اور جب ماں آزاد ہوئی تو اس کی بچی بھی آزاد ہوئی اور دوسری حالت میں ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں اپنی اپنی قیمت کا آدھا حصہ کما کر کے اپنے مولی کو دے کر آزاد ہو جائیں۔ لیکن وہ لڑ کا دونوں حالتوں میں غلام ہی رہے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ لڑکا اپنی ماں کے آزاد ہونے سے پہلے ہی پیدا ہو چکا ہے۔ دونوں کے حق میں معتبر ہوگا۔ اس لئے دونوں آزاد ہو جائیں گی اور اگر یہ لڑکی بالغہ ہو اور اس نے اپنی آزادی کا خود دعوئی نہ کیا ہو اور باقی مسئلہ اسی حال پر ہو یعنی باندی نے پہلے لڑکے کے پیدا ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا ہومگر مولی نے نہیں مانا اور قسم سے بھی انکار کیا تو مولی کے قسم کے انکار سے فقط ماں آزاد ہوگی مگر لڑ کی آزاد نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بالغہ لڑکی کے بارے میں ماں کا دعویٰ کرنا کہ یہ آزاد ہے اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قسم کے انکار سے اسی صورت میں اقرار مانا جاتا ہے۔ جب کہ اس نے خود ہی کسی بات کا دعویٰ کیا ہو اور موجودہ مسئلہ میں چونکہ بالغہ لڑکی کی طرف سے کوئی دعوی نہیں ہے تو اس کے بارے میں کیونکہ یہاں پر غیر کے فعل و عمل پر اس سے قسم لی جائے گی اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم . ۲۳ باب عتق احد العبدين اور ہماری بتائی ہوئی اس تفصیل سے وہ صورتیں بھی معلوم ہو جاتی ہیں جو ہم نے کفایتہ امنتہی میں ذکر کی ہیں۔ تشریح وَ مَنْ قَالَ لِاَمَتِهِ إِنْ كَانَ أَوّلُ وَلَدِتَلِدِينَ غُلَامًا فَانتِ حُرَّةً فَوَلَدَتْ غُلَامًا وَ جَارِيَةً وَلَايُدْري أَيُّها.... الخ ترجمه ت ......و مطلب واضح ہے۔ ( کتاب کفایہ انتہی اس زمانے میں بالکل نایاب ہے اور جامع صغیر کی شرحوں میں ان صورتوں کی تفصیل میں چھ صورتیں مذکور ہیں۔ ان میں سے چار صورتیں تو خود کتاب میں مصنف نے خود بیان فرمادی ہیں اور پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ باندی اور مولی اور لڑکی سھوں نے متفق ہو کر یہ کہا کہ پہلے لڑکی پیدا ہوئی ہے اور چھٹی صورت یہ ہے کہ سکھوں نے بالا تفاق یہ کہا کہ پہلے لڑکا پیدا ہوا ہے۔ تو اس کا حکم یہ ہوگا کہ ماں آزاد ہوگی اور اس کے ساتھ ہی یہی لڑکی بھی آزاد ہو جائے گی مگر لڑ کا غلام ہی رہے گا)۔
Chapter: Freeing one of two slaves. 22. Due to the absence of the condition, half of each of them becomes free, and she must work for the half. As for the boy, he remains a slave in both cases, so he is a slave. And if the mother claims that the boy was born first, and the master denies it, and the girl is a minor, then the master's word is taken with an oath because he denies the condition of freedom. If he swears, none of them become free. If he refuses to swear, the mother and the girl become free because the mother's claim of freedom for the minor is considered as it is purely beneficial. So the refusal is deemed in favor of their freedom, and they become free. And if the girl is an adult and does not claim anything, and the case remains as is, the mother becomes free by the master's refusal alone, not the girl, because the mother's claim is not considered for the adult girl, and the validity of refusal is tied to a claim, so it does not appear for the girl. And if the adult girl herself claims that the boy's birth was earlier, and the mother remains silent, the girl's freedom is established by the master's refusal, not the mother's, for what we said. And the oath is upon knowledge in what we mentioned, because it is an oath about another's action. By this much, the points we mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha are known. Translation: ... [Urdu commentary detailing scenarios]
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Hidayah discusses the ruling when a master conditionally frees his slave woman upon giving birth to a male child first, and she gives birth to twins (a boy and a girl) with the order unknown. The ruling: the mother and daughter each become half-free, while the son remains fully enslaved. This is because in one possibility (boy born first), the condition is met and the mother becomes free, so the daughter born after her freedom is free; in the other possibility (girl born first), the condition is not met, and both remain slaves. Due to uncertainty, each is deemed half-free. The son, whether born first or second, is always born before the mother's freedom (if the girl is first, condition fails; if the boy is first, he is born while mother is still enslaved until condition is fulfilled at his birth, but technically he is born before the freedom takes effect because the condition is fulfilled at his birth? Actually, the text says he remains a slave in both cases because he was born before the mother's freedom: if the boy is first, he is born while mother is still a slave (condition only fulfilled at his birth, so the mother becomes free after his birth, so he is born as a slave); if the girl is first, condition fails entirely, so he is born a slave. The son is never free. The passage then discusses scenarios involving claims and oaths: if the mother claims the boy was first and the master denies, the master's word with oath is accepted because he denies the condition. If he swears, none free; if he refuses, mother and minor daughter free. For an adult daughter, her own claim is needed. The oath is upon knowledge because it concerns another's action. The commentary adds that from this, the six scenarios mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha can be deduced.

Key Terms
عتق ('itq): Emancipation of a slave, making him/her free.
نكول (nukūl): Refusal to take an oath in legal proceedings; treated as an admission of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All three become half-free
B) Mother and daughter half-free, son full slave
C) Mother half-free, daughter and son full slaves
D) All three remain full slaves

Key Takeaway
When the condition for emancipation is partially met due to uncertainty, the mother and daughter become half-free, but the son remains fully enslaved.

Conditional Manumission: Future Ownership Fulfills Oath
Ruling on conditional manumission when the oath-taker owns no slaves at the time of the oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a conditional manumission oath when no slaves are owned at the time of the oath, and identify the key term that determines the outcome.

Core Idea
In a conditional manumission oath, 'at that time' refers to the future condition's fulfillment, not the oath's utterance.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter on oaths by manumission. The case involves a person who swears to free all his slaves if he enters a house, but at the time of the oath he owns no slaves. Later he buys a slave and then enters. The Hanafi ruling is that the slave becomes free. Understanding the precise wording of the oath is crucial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is an oath of manumission (ḥalif bil-ʿitq). The condition is entering the house. The result is that all slaves owned at the time of entry become free.
The condition is future: 'if I enter the house'.
2
Note the ownership timeline
At the time of the oath, the man owns no slaves. He later purchases a slave, then enters the house.
Ownership changes between the oath and the condition's fulfillment.
3
Analyze the key phrase 'yawma’idhin'
The phrase 'at that time' (yawma’idhin) refers to the time of entry, not the time of the oath. This is the critical point for the ruling.
The Arabic attaches the ownership to the moment of entry.
4
State the ruling
Since he owns a slave at the moment of entry, the condition is met and the slave becomes free. The ruling applies regardless of ownership at the time of the oath.
The manumission is valid and binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ مَنْ قَالَ إِذَا دَخَلْتُ الدَّارَ فَكُلُّ مَمْلُوكَ لِى يَوْمَئِذٍ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ مَمْلُوكَ فَاشْتَرَى مَمْلُوكًا ثُمَّ دَخَلَ عَتَقَ
And whoever said: When I enter the house, every slave I own at that time is free, and he does not own any slave, then he buys a slave and then enters, that slave becomes free.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on swearing by manumission. The matn presents a case: A man makes a conditional oath to free all his slaves if he enters a house, but at the time of the oath he does not own any slaves. Subsequently, he purchases a slave and then enters the house. The ruling is that the slave becomes free. This is because the phrase 'every slave I own at that time' (yawma'idhin) refers to the time of entering, not the time of the oath. Since he owns a slave at the time of entry, the condition is fulfilled and the manumission takes effect. The ruling applies even though he owned no slaves at the time of the oath; the condition is attached to the future time of entry.

Key Terms
حلف بالعتق (ḥalif bil-ʿitq): An oath involving the conditional manumission of a slave, often used to enforce or prohibit an action.
يَوْمَئِذٍ (yawmaʾidhin): At that time (referring to the future time of the condition's fulfillment, here entry into the house).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the oath was unconditional.
B) Because the phrase 'at that time' refers to the time of entering.
C) Because buying a slave automatically fulfills any previous oath.
D) Because the man's intention was to free future slaves.

Key Takeaway
A conditional manumission oath attaches ownership to the moment of the condition's fulfillment, not the oath itself.

Freeing One of Two Slaves in Terminal Illness: Testimony and the Requirement of a Claim
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony requirement for freeing slaves in marad al-mawt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the need for a slave's claim for testimony about his freedom, and apply the principle of istihsan to determine when testimony is accepted.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, testimony about freeing a slave may be accepted without a claim if the freeing spreads to both slaves, but Imam Abu Hanifa requires a claim for a specific opponent.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a nuanced legal scenario: a master frees one of two slaves in terminal illness, and after his death, witnesses testify. The central question is whether the slaves must first make a legal claim for their freedom before such testimony is accepted. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Understanding the reasons behind their positions—especially the use of istihsan and analogy with divorce—is key to mastering Hanafi jurisprudence on testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine the legal issue: does testimony about freeing one of two slaves require a claim by the slave? State Imam Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions clearly.
2
Trace the proof for the Sahibayn
Understand why the Sahibayn accept testimony without a claim: they rely on the principle that freeing in marad al-mawt spreads to both slaves, making each a specific opponent. Also, they analogize to divorce where no claim is needed.
Key principle: freeing in marad al-mawt is a will, and the executor/heir becomes the opponent.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's counter-argument
Note his distinction: freeing does not immediately make the slave's private parts forbidden to the master (unlike divorce), so analogy with divorce fails. Thus, a claim is still required.
This distinction applies specifically to female slaves; for male slaves, the same reasoning applies? Actually, the text focuses on female slaves.
4
Apply to different scenarios
Distinguish between freeing male vs female slaves, and freeing in health vs terminal illness. See how the ruling differs accordingly.
5
Understand the role of istihsan
Note that in terminal illness, the Hanafi school prefers the Sahibayn's view by istihsan, because the testator's executor or heir is a specific opponent, and the spread of freedom justifies acceptance.
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas here.

Source Text

Chapter on freeing one of two slaves. (Number 24) Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary volume 6. The freeing in terminal illness is a will. The opponent in a will is the testator, who is known. After him, there is a successor, which is the executor or heir. And the freeing in terminal illness spreads with death among them (the two slaves), so each of them becomes a specific opponent. If they (two witnesses) testify after his death that he said in his health 'one of you is free,' it has been said: it is not accepted because it is not a will, and it has been said: it is accepted due to the spread (of freedom). Urdu translation: The basis of this difference in the matter of freedom is that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, without the slave's own claim, testifying to his being free is not accepted. But according to the Sahibayn, it is accepted, and this issue is well-known. Then, when according to Imam A'zam the slave's claim is a condition, in the issue of Jami' al-Saghir which was explained above, the claim cannot be proven at that time, so the testimony will not be accepted. According to the Sahibayn, since making a claim is not a condition, the testimony will be accepted even if no claim was made. However, in the case of divorce, the absence of a claim does not affect the testimony because a claim is not a condition for testimony in divorce. If two witnesses testify that this man said to his two slave-girls, 'One of you is free,' then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this testimony is also not accepted, even though in such testimony a claim is not a condition. The reason is that the non-necessity of a claim is only based on the fact that by freeing, her private parts become forbidden to the master. Therefore, it resembles divorce. But according to Imam A'zam, by freeing, the prohibition of her private parts is not necessitated, as we have mentioned before. Therefore, testifying to freeing one of two female slaves is like testifying to freeing one of two slaves in health. If the witnesses testify that he freed one of them in his terminal illness, or that he made one of them mudabbar in health or illness, and this testimony was given during the master's terminal illness or after his death, then by istihsan this testimony will be accepted. Because making mudabbar in any state (illness or health) is effective. Similarly, freeing in terminal illness is in the ruling of a will. The person against whom the claim of will is made is called the testator, and he is known, and his successor is present, i.e., his executor or heir, so testimony against him will be accepted. And by the proof that the freedom that occurs in terminal illness spreads to both slaves upon the master's death, each of them becomes a specific defendant, so the testimony is accepted. If after the master's death the witnesses testify that he said in his health, 'One of you is free,' then there are two opinions: one that the testimony is not accepted because it is not a will, and the second that it is accepted because the freedom spreads among them. Benefit: The freedom spreads between them, so it becomes clear that each is a defendant against the other; thus the claim and testimony of each are valid.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on freeing one of two slaves addresses two main issues: the ruling on freeing a slave during terminal illness (marad al-mawt) and the acceptance of testimony after the owner's death. The Arabic matn establishes that freeing a slave in marad al-mawt is treated as a will (wasiyyah). In a will case, the opponent is the testator, who is known; after his death, his executor or heir takes his place. The key principle is that if a person frees one of two slaves in marad al-mawt, the freedom spreads to both upon death (yashiya'u bi'l-mawt fihima). Consequently, each slave becomes a specific opponent in a legal dispute. The matn then discusses testimony: if witnesses testify after the owner's death that he said in health 'one of you is free,' there are two views. One considers it unacceptable because it is not a will; the other accepts it due to the spread of freedom. The Urdu commentary delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the requirement of the slave's claim for testimony. Imam Abu Hanifa requires the slave to make a claim before testimony about his freedom is accepted, while the Sahibayn do not. This distinction is applied to cases of freeing male slaves versus female slaves, and to freeing during health versus terminal illness. The commentary explains that in terminal illness, freeing is like a will, so the executor or heir is the opponent, and testimony is accepted by istihsan. It also mentions that if the owner made one of them mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the owner's death), the same principle applies. The passage concludes with two opinions on testimony after death regarding a statement made in health: one rejects it, the other accepts it due to the spread of freedom, emphasizing that the spread makes each slave a defendant to the other, so their claims and testimonies are valid.

Key Terms
العِتق (al-'itq): The act of freeing a slave; in this context, it refers to the legal ruling of freeing one of two slaves.
وصية (wasiyyah): A will; here, freeing a slave in marad al-mawt is treated as a will, subject to the rules of wills.
خصم (khasm): Opponent or legal party; in testimony, the person against whom the testimony is directed.
شيع (shay'): To spread or circulate; here, freedom spreads to both slaves upon the owner's death.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a principle of Hanafi fiqh used to give a ruling based on fairness over strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the master's statement is a direct confession.
B) Because the freedom spreads to both slaves upon death, making each a specific opponent.
C) Because two witnesses are sufficient for any testimony.
D) Because the heirs have consented.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of testimony about freeing a slave depends on whether the freeing was in health or terminal illness, and whether a claim has been made; this intra-Hanafi dispute highlights the role of istihsan and the distinction between freeing and divorce.

intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Oath to Free Slaves When None Owned at Time of Oath
States the ruling on an oath to free all slaves upon entering a house when no slaves are owned at the oath, then later acquiring a slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a conditional oath to free slaves when the wording includes 'yawm idh' vs when it does not, and explain the reasoning based on the linguistic analysis.

Core Idea
The inclusion of 'yawm idh' in an oath extends the applicable slaves to those owned at entry.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on conditional oaths involving freeing slaves. The key distinction is whether the oath includes the phrase 'yawm idh' (that day). Understanding this linguistic nuance is crucial for determining which slaves become free upon the condition's fulfilment. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents two scenarios and the reasoning behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage carefully: one scenario includes the word 'yawm idh' and the other does not. Note the difference in the rulings.
The passage explicitly contrasts the two cases.
2
Analyse the linguistic contraction of 'yawm idh'
The passage explains that 'yawm idh' is a contraction of 'yawm idh dakhaltu' (the day when I entered). Understand how this makes ownership at the time of entry the relevant factor.
The substitution of nunation for the verb is a key linguistic point.
3
Apply the ruling to the scenario with 'yawm idh'
If the oath includes 'yawm idh', any slave owned at the time of entry becomes free, even if no slave was owned at the oath. Recognize the reasoning: the oath refers to the moment of entry.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario without 'yawm idh'
If the oath does not include 'yawm idh', the phrase 'every slave of mine' applies to the present moment of the oath. Only slaves owned at that time and still owned at entry become free.
Slaves purchased after the oath are not covered.

Source Text

باب الحلف بالعتق ترجمہ باب آزادی کی قسم کھانے کے بیان میں ایک شخص نے کہا اگر میں گھر میں داخل ہوا میرے تمام غلام آزاد اس وقت کسی غلام کا مالک نہیں پھر غلام خریدے اور گھر میں داخل ہو ا غلام آزاد ہو مطلب واضح ہے۔ اگر اپنی یمین میں یو مئذ کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہو تو غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا. وَ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَالَ فِي يَمِينِهِ يَوْمَئِذٍ لَمْ يَعْتِقْ لِاَنَّ قَوْلَهُ كُلُّ مَمْلُوكِ لِى لِلْحَالِ وَالْجَزَاءُ حُرِّيَّةُ الْمَمْلُوكِ فِي الْحَالِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَمَّا دَخَلَ الشَّرْطُ عَلَى الْجَزَاءِ تَأَخَّرَ إِلَى وُجُودِ الشَّرْطِ فَيَعْتِقُ إِذَابَقِيَ عَلَى مِلْكِهِ إِلَى وَقْتِ الدُّخُولِ وَلَا يَتَنَا وَلُ مَنِ اشْتَرَاهُ بَعْدَ الْيَمِيْنِ ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے قسم کے موقع پر لفظ اس روزانہ کہا ہوتو بعد میں خریدا ہواغلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کا یہ کہنا کہ میر وہ غلام ایسے ہی غلام کے واسطے کہنا صحیح ہے جو اس وقت اس کی ملکیت میں موجود ہو اور اس قسم (شرط) کی جزاء یہ تھی کہ جو فی الحال غلام ہے وہ آزاد ہو جائے۔ لیکن چونکہ جزاء پر شرط داخل ہے اس لئے تاخیر کے پائے جانے تک اس جزا میں تاخیر ہوئی۔ لہذا گھر میں داخل ہونے تک جو غلام فی الحال موجود ہے اگر اس کی ملکیت میں باقی نہ رہا تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور جو غلام اس شرط و قسم کے بعد خریدا گیا ہو وہ آزادی میں شامل نہیں ہو گا۔
Chapter on swearing by freeing. Urdu translation: Chapter on the explanation of swearing by freeing. A person said: If I enter the house, all my slaves are free. At that time he owned no slaves. Then he bought a slave and entered the house: the slave will be free. And whoever says, 'When I enter the house, then every slave of mine on that day is free,' and he has no slave, then he buys a slave and enters: the slave becomes free, because his saying 'yawm idh' (that day) is an abbreviation of 'the day when I entered,' except that he dropped the verb and substituted the nunation. So what is considered is the existence of ownership at the time of entry. Similarly, if at the time of his oath he owned a slave, and that slave remains in his ownership until he enters, then the slave becomes free, for the reason we have mentioned. Urdu translation: If someone said, 'When I enter this house, then every slave of mine on that day is free,' even though on the day of his saying he had no slave, but later he bought a slave and then entered the house, that slave will be free. Because his saying 'that day' is originally 'the day when I entered,' but he omitted the verb and replaced it with nunation. Thus, ownership at the time of entry is considered. Similarly, if at the time of the oath he had a slave, and that slave remains in his ownership until he enters, the slave will become free for the reason we have given: the slave is in his ownership at the time of entry. Clarification: The meaning is clear from the translation. If he did not use the word 'yawm idh' in his oath, the slave will not be free. And if he did not say in his oath 'yawm idh,' he (the slave) does not become free, because his statement 'every slave of mine' applies to the present, and the consequence is the freedom of the slave in the present. However, since the condition was attached to the consequence, it is delayed until the condition occurs. So if the present slave remains in his ownership until the time of entry, he becomes free; but it does not include one who was bought after the oath. Urdu translation: If he did not use the word 'that day' at the time of the oath, then a slave bought later will not be free. Because his saying 'my every slave' is correctly applied only to the slave that was present at that time. The consequence of this oath (condition) was that whoever is currently a slave becomes free. But since the condition (entry) is attached to the consequence, the consequence is delayed until the condition occurs. Therefore, if the slave currently present remains in his ownership until he enters the house, he becomes free, but the slave bought after the oath is not included in the freedom.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on swearing by freeing (al-hilf bi'l-'itq) explains the legal effect of an oath that includes the word 'yawm idh' (that day). The matn presents two cases: first, if a person says, 'When I enter the house, every slave of mine on that day (yawm idh) is free,' but at the time of the oath he owns no slaves, then later he buys a slave and enters the house, that slave becomes free. The reasoning is that 'yawm idh' is a contraction of 'the day when I enter,' so the ownership at the time of entry is considered. The same ruling applies if he owned a slave at the oath and that slave remains in his ownership until entry: the slave is freed. The second case: if the oath does not include 'yawm idh,' then the slave is not freed unless he was owned at the time of the oath and remained in ownership until entry. In this case, the phrase 'every slave of mine' refers to present slaves. The consequence (freedom) is suspended on the condition of entry, but only applies to slaves in existence at the time of the oath. Therefore, a slave purchased after the oath is not included. The Urdu commentary clarifies these rulings and emphasizes that the use of 'yawm idh' expands the scope to include slaves owned at entry, whereas without it, only slaves owned at the time of the oath are affected.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): Oath; here it refers to a conditional oath involving freeing slaves.
جزاء (jaza'): Consequence or result; in this context, the freeing of the slave is the consequence of the condition (entering the house).
شرط (shart): Condition; the act of entering the house is the condition that triggers the freeing.
يومئذ (yawma idh): That day; a contracted form meaning 'the day when' referring to the day of entry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man swears 'When I enter the house, every slave of mine is free' (without 'yawm idh') and at the time of the oath he owns a slave named Bakr. He later sells Bakr before entering. What happens when he enters?
A) Bakr becomes free despite being sold.
B) Bakr does not become free.
C) The oath is invalid because he sold the slave.
D) He must free another slave as expiation.

Key Takeaway
The inclusion of 'yawm idh' in a conditional oath expands the scope of the objects to the time of the condition, while its absence restricts it to the moment of the oath.

Ruling on Oath to Free Male Slaves: Effect on a Pregnant Slave
Determines whether a male child born to a pregnant slave is freed under an oath to free all male slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a male child born to a pregnant slave is freed under an oath to free all male slaves and explain the reasoning that the fetus is not an independent slave.

Core Idea
A fetus is not an independent slave—it is a limb of the mother, so an oath to free male slaves does not free a male child born later.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a master swears 'Every male slave of mine is free' while owning a pregnant female slave. Does the male child she later delivers become free? The Hanafi position is clear: the child is not freed. Understanding the legal principle that a fetus is owned dependently (taba'an) and considered like a limb (udw) is key to grasping this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and scenario
Read the passage to understand the exact wording of the oath: 'Every male slave of mine is free.' Note that the master owns a pregnant slave.
2
Determine the ruling
The passage states clearly: the male child is not freed (lam ya'tiq). This is the definitive Hanafi ruling.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The reasoning is that the fetus is not an independent slave (mamluk mustaqill) but is a dependent possession (mamluk taba'an) of the mother, likened to a limb (udw). The word 'mamluk' applies to independent persons, not limbs.
This principle prevents treating the fetus as an independent subject of ownership.
4
Consider the timing conditions
The passage discusses births after six months (presumed pregnancy at oath time) and before six months. In both cases, the child is not freed, reinforcing the principle.
Birth after six months confirms pregnancy at oath time, but the fetus was still not an independent slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Clarification: If he did not say in his oath 'yawm idh,' he does not free... the meaning is clear from the translation. The master said: 'Every male slave of mine is free.' He had a pregnant slave-girl who gave birth to a male child; will that child be freed? And whoever says, 'Every male slave of mine is free,' and he has a pregnant slave-girl, and she gives birth to a male child, the child is not freed. This applies if she gives birth after six months or more, because the wording applies to the present. And regarding the existence of the pregnancy at the time of the oath, there is a possibility of the minimum period of pregnancy occurring after it. Similarly, if she gives birth before six months, because the wording covers the absolute slave, and the fetus is a slave as a dependent of the mother, not as an intended object, and because it is a limb from one perspective. The name 'slave' applies to persons, not limbs. For this reason, one cannot sell it separately. Al-'Abd al-Da'if said: The benefit of restricting to the description of maleness is that if he said 'every slave of mine,' the pregnant mother would be included, and the fetus would be included as a dependent of her. Urdu translation: And if someone said, 'When I enter this house, then every slave of mine that is male is free,' and at that time he had...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage clarifies a specific scenario: a master swears 'Every male slave of mine is free' while owning a pregnant female slave. Does the male child she later delivers become free? The ruling is clear: the child is NOT freed. The reasoning is that the word 'mamluk' (slave) applies to independent persons, not to a fetus, which is considered a part of the mother (like a limb). The fetus is owned only dependently (taba'an) and not as a primary object of ownership. Therefore, it cannot be sold separately. The matn adds that if she gives birth after six months or more, it is clear she was pregnant at the time of the oath, but still the child is not freed because the wording is for present slaves. If she gives birth before six months, the child is also not freed for the same reason. The benefit of restricting the oath to 'male' is explained: if the master had said 'every slave of mine' without the restriction, the pregnant slave herself would be included, and then the fetus would be included as her dependent, so the fetus would be freed if the mother was freed. But with the restriction to male, the pregnant slave is excluded, so her child is not covered.

Key Terms
مملوك (mamluk): Slave; in this context, it denotes a legally recognized human being who is owned as property.
تبعا (taba'an): Dependently; the fetus is owned as a dependent of the mother, not as an independent slave.
عضو (udw): Limb; the fetus is likened to a limb of the mother, not a separate person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The child is freed only if the mother is also freed.
D) The child is freed because six months indicates pregnancy at time of oath.

Key Takeaway
A fetus is not an independent slave; it is a part of the mother, so an oath to free male slaves does not free the male child born later.
