Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Post-Oath Acquisitions in Tadbir
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of a conditional freeing upon death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether a tadbir statement covers later-acquired slaves, and evaluate the reasoning based on the combination of two legal causes.

Core Idea
A statement combining immediate freeing and bequest covers future slaves; a single cause cannot combine present and future.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of a declaratory freeing after death. When a master says 'Every slave I own is free after my death,' does this apply only to slaves owned at that moment, or also to those acquired later? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad argue for inclusion of future acquisitions by analyzing the statement as both an immediate obligation (making current slaves mudabbar) and a bequest (extending to future slaves). Imam Abu Yusuf restricts it to current ownership based on literal interpretation. Understanding this difference sharpens our appreciation of how Hanafi jurists combine textual interpretation with purposive reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the contested ruling
The master utters 'Every slave I own is free after my death' when he owns one slave, then later purchases another. The dispute is whether the later slave is included in the freeing.
Focus on the difference between the two slaves: the one owned at utterance vs. the one acquired later.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad and their dalil
They hold that the statement comprises two causes: an immediate obligation of freeing (ijab al-'itq) applying to the present slave, making him mudabbar, and a bequest (wasiyyah) applying to future slaves, freeing them from the third of the estate at death.
Their dalil uses analogy: in bequests of wealth, after-acquired property is included; similarly for bequests to offspring, after-born children are included.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf and his dalil
Abu Yusuf restricts the freeing to slaves owned at the time of utterance, because the literal wording 'every slave I own' refers to present ownership. The later slave is not owned at that moment, so not included.
His position is based on a strict reading of the wording as a single cause of freeing.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that the combination of present and future in one statement is permissible because it arises from two different causes (immediate freeing and bequest). This is unlike a statement like 'after tomorrow,' which is a single cause and cannot combine present and future.
The key is the duality of causes; the same principle would apply today in combined contracts.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi position
Under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, the later slave is freed from the third of the estate at death (not mudabbar). Under Abu Yusuf, the later slave is not freed at all. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it gives fuller effect to the testator's intent.
This shows how tarjih within the school resolves such disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِيجَابُ عِتْقٍ وَوَصِيَّةٍ حَتَّى اعْتُبِرَ مِنَ التَّلْثِ وَفِي الْوَصَايَا تُعْتَبَرُ الْحَالَةُ الْمُنْتَظَرَةُ وَالْحَالَةُ الرَّاهِنَةُ أَلَا يُرى أَنَّهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي الْوَصِيَّةِ بِالْمَالِ مَا يَسْتَفِيدُهُ بَعْدَ الْوَصِيَّةِ وَفِي الْوَصِيَّةِ لِأَوْلَادِ فُلَانٍ مَنْ يُولَدُ لَهُ بَعْدَهَا وَالْإِيجَابُ إِنَّمَا يَصِحُّ مُضَافًا إِلَى الْمِلْكِ أَوْ إِلَى سَبَبِهِ فَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ إِيجَابُ الْعِتْقِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْعَبْدَ الْمَمْلُوكَ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَالَةِ الرَّاهِنَةِ فَيَصِيرُ مُدَبَّرًا حَتَّى لَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُهُ وَمِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ وَصِيَّةٌ يَتَنَاوَلُ الَّذِي يَشْتَرِيهِ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْحَالَةِ الْمُتَرَقِّبَةِ وَهِيَ حَالَةُ الْمَوْتِ وَقَبْلَ الْمَوْتِ حَالَةُ التَّمَلُّكِ اسْتِقْبَالٌ مَحْضٌ فَلَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ اللَّفْظِ وَعِنْدَ الْمَوْتِ يَصِيرُ كَأَنَّهُ قَالَ كُلُّ مَمْلُوكٍ لِي أَوْ كُلُّ مَمْلُوكٍ أَمْلِكُهُ فَهُوَ حُرٌّ بِخِلَافِ قَوْلِهِ بَعْدَ غَدٍ عَلَى مَا تَقَدَّمَ لِأَنَّهُ تَصَرُّفٌ وَاحِدٌ وَهُوَ إِيجَابُ الْعِتْقِ وَلَيْسَ فِيهِ وَصِيَّةٌ وَالْحَالَةُ مَحْضُ اسْتِقْبَالٍ فَافْتَرَقَا وَلَا يُقَالُ إِنَّكُمْ جَمَعْتُمْ بَيْنَ الْحَالِ وَالِاسْتِقْبَالِ لِأَنَّا نَقُولُ نَعَمْ لَكِنْ بِسَبَبَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ إِيجَابِ عِتْقٍ وَوَصِيَّةٍ وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَجُوزُ ذَلِكَ بِسَبَبٍ وَاحِدٍ. ترجمہ: اگر کسی نے کہا کہ ہر وہ غلام جس کا میں مالک ہوں یا یوں کہا کہ میرے سارے غلام میری موت کے بعد آزاد ہیں اور اس کہنے کے وقت اس کا صرف ایک ہی غلام تھا۔ اس کے بعد اس نے دوسرے غلام بھی خرید لیا۔ تو وہ غلام جو اس کی قسم کھانے کے وقت اس کے پاس موجود تھا وہی مدبر ہو گا۔ یعنی بعد کا خریدا ہوا مدبر نہیں ہوگا اور مولی کے انتقال کے بعد اس کے وارث سے تہائی حصہ سے دونوں آزاد ہو جائیں گے۔ لیکن ابو یوسف نے یوں فرمایا ہے کہ اس قسم کھانے کے وقت جو غلام بھی اس کی ملکیت میں ہو گا وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور وہ غلام جسے مولیٰ نے اس قسم کے بعد خریدا ہے وہ آزاد نہیں ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر اس نے یوں کہا جتنے بھی میرے غلام ہیں وہ جب میں مر جاؤں تو وہ آزاد ہیں تو یہی حکم ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظاہری لفظ حقیقت میں موجود اور فی الحال پائے جانے والے کے لئے ہے جیسا کہ ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ اس لئے وہ غلام جو قسم کھانے کے بعد جس کا وہ مالک ہوا ہو آزاد نہ ہو گا۔ اسی لئے وہی قسم کے وقت مدبر ہو گیا اور دوسرا مدبر نہیں ہوا اور طرفین یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام سے آزادی کو واجب کرنا اور وصیت کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ مردہ کے تہائی مال سے اس کا اعتبار کیا جاتا ہے اور وصیتوں میں آئندہ موت تک کی حالت اور موجودہ حالت کا بھی اعتبار ہوتا ہے کیا یہ نہیں دیکھتا کہ اپنے تہائی مال کی وصیت کرنے کی صورت میں اس مال کا بھی حساب کیا جاتا ہے جو وصیت کرنے کے بعد موت آنے تک میں حاصل ہوتا ہے اور فلاں شخص (مثلاً زید) کی اولاد کے لئے وصیت کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی موجودہ اولاد کے علاوہ اس وصیت کے بعد پیدا ہونے والی اولاد بھی اس وصیت میں داخل ہوتی ہے اور وصیت کا قول اسی وقت صحیح ہوتا ہے جبکہ آزاد کرنا ملک یا سبب ملک کی طرف سے منسوب کیا جائے تو اس اعتبار سے کہ اس میں آزادی کی بات ہے اس مملوک غلام کو شامل ہوگا جو موجودہ حالت کے اعتبار سے ہو۔ اس لئے فی الحال جو غلام بھی اس کی ملکیت میں ہوگا وہ مدبر ہو جائے گا۔ اسی وجہ سے اس کو بیچنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا اور اس اعتبار سے کہ وہ وصیت ہے وہ ایسے غلام کو بھی شامل ہوگا جسے اس کے بعد خریدے گا تاکہ آئندہ کو بھی شامل ہو۔ یعنی اس کی آخری زندگی تک جو غلام بھی کسی طرح اس کی ملکیت میں آئے گا وہ اس حکم میں شامل ہو جائے گا اور اس کی موت سے پہلے کی حالت محض استقبالی ہے یعنی آئندہ ایسا ہونا ممکن ہے کہ اس کی ملکیت میں کچھ اور بھی غلام آئیں اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ نہ آئیں۔ تو یہ بات لفظ کے تحت میں داخل نہیں ہو سکتی اور مولیٰ کے مرنے کے وقت یہ سمجھا جائے گا کہ گویا اس نے یوں کہا ہے کہ میرے تمام غلام یا وہ سارے غلام جن کا میں مالک ہوں وہ آزاد ہیں بخلاف اس قول کے کہ ہر وہ غلام جس کا میں مالک ہوں وہ کل کے بعد آزاد ہے۔ جیسا کہ اس سے پہلے بیان ہو چکا ہے۔ اس فرق کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ قول صرف ایک ہی بات اور ایک ہی تصرف ہے یعنی آزاد کرنے کی بات ہے۔ اس میں وصیت کرنے کا کوئی بیان نہیں ہے اسی طرح ملکیت حاصل کرنے کی حالت بھی فقط آئندہ زمانے پر معلق ہے۔ اس طرح دونوں قولوں میں فرق ظاہر ہو گیا۔ یہاں اگر یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ اس بیان سے زمانہ حال اور استقبال دونوں کا اکھٹا کر دیا گیا ہے تو یہ اعتراض درست نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اگر چہ دونوں کا اجتماع ہوتا ہے مگر ایک سبب سے نہیں ہے بلکہ دو سببوں سے جمع کیا ہے۔ یعنی ایک کلام کو آزادی کا کلام اور دوسرے کو وصیت سے شامل کیا ہے اور دونوں زمانوں کو جمع کرنا اس صورت میں جائز نہیں ہوتا ہے جب کہ ایک ہی سبب سے دونوں کو جمع کیا گیا ہو۔ تشریح وَلَوْ قَالَ كُلُّ مَمْلُوكٍ أَمْلِكُهُ أَوْ قَالَ كُلُّ مَمْلُوكٍ لِي حُرٌّ بَعْدَ مَوْتِي وَلَهُ مَمْلُوكٌ فَاشْتَرَى مَمْلُوكًا آخَرَ فَالَّذِي كَانَ عِنْدَهُ مُدَبَّرٌ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
It is an obligation of freeing and a bequest, such that it is considered from the third. In bequests, the expected condition and the present condition are considered. Do you not see that in a bequest of wealth, what he acquires after the bequest enters, and in a bequest for the children of so-and-so, those born after it enter. The obligation is only valid when added to ownership or its cause. From the perspective that it is an obligation of freeing, it includes the owned slave by considering the present condition, so he becomes mudabbar such that his sale is not permissible. And from the perspective that it is a bequest, it includes the one he purchases by considering the awaited condition, which is the time of death. Before death, the condition of ownership is pure future, so it does not fall under the wording. At death, it becomes as if he said: 'Every slave of mine or every slave I own is free', contrary to saying 'after tomorrow' as previously, because it is a single transaction which is the obligation of freeing, and there is no bequest in it, and the condition is pure future, so they differ. And it cannot be said: 'You have combined present and future', because we say: Yes, but by two different causes: obligation of freeing and bequest; that is not permissible by a single cause. Translation: ... (Urdu explanation follows)
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the Hidayah regarding a person who says, 'Every slave I own is free after my death' and then acquires another slave. The commentator analyzes the legal effects by treating the statement as comprising two elements: an immediate obligation of freedom (ijab al-'itq) and a bequest (wasiyyah). The immediate part applies to slaves owned at the time of utterance, making them mudabbar (free upon death) and unsellable. The bequest part applies to future acquisitions, so that at death, all slaves owned at any time are freed from the third of the estate. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that only slaves owned at the time of the oath are freed, because the literal wording refers to present ownership. The commentator explains the difference by noting that in the first case, the statement is bipartite (freedom and bequest), while in a case like 'after tomorrow' it is a single transaction, thus the combination of present and future is impermissible only when from a single cause.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave who is declared free upon the master's death by a direct statement (tadbir); such a slave cannot be sold and becomes free from the third of the estate.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest of property or freedom that becomes effective after death, subject to the one-third limit.
إِيجَابُ الْعِتْقِ (ijab al-'itq): Immediate obligation of freeing a slave; in this context, it applies to slaves currently owned, making them mudabbar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, if someone says 'Every slave I own is free after my death' and later buys another slave, what is the status of the later slave?
A) He is not freed at all because he was not owned at the time of utterance
B) He becomes mudabbar immediately upon purchase
C) He is freed from the one-third of the estate upon the master's death
D) He is freed immediately as the statement is considered a present emancipation

Key Takeaway
A statement can combine immediate freeing and a bequest to cover both present and future slaves, as long as the effects arise from two distinct legal causes.

Freeing a Slave for a Payment: Immediate Freedom
Introduces the ruling and conditions of freeing a slave in exchange for property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of 'itq 'ala ja'l, explain that freedom is immediate upon acceptance, and distinguish it from kitabah.

Core Idea
In 'itq 'ala ja'l, freedom is immediate upon acceptance; the payment becomes a debt.

This passage introduces the ruling on freeing a slave in exchange for a specified payment (ja'l). The key point is that the slave becomes free immediately upon acceptance, and the payment becomes a debt owed by the slave. The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) to sale, and contrasts with the contract of kitabah where freedom is deferred until full payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the central act under discussion? (Freeing a slave for a payment). What is the ruling? (Valid, immediate freedom).
2
Understand the analogy to sale
The passage draws an analogy (qiyas) to sale: just as a sale is completed by acceptance and the price becomes a debt, here acceptance frees the slave and the payment becomes a debt.
The illa (effective cause) is exchange (mu'awada).
3
Distinguish from kitabah
In kitabah, the slave remains partially enslaved until full payment; here the slave is free immediately. The payment in kitabah is established despite continuing slavery, which is contradictory.
Kitabah is not analogous because it involves persisting slavery.
4
Recognize permissible forms of payment
The word 'mal' (property) includes cash, goods, animals, and even unspecified items if the genus is known; minor ignorance of description is tolerated.
This broad scope is justified by analogy to marriage, divorce, and blood money compromise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العتق على جعل ترجمہ: مال کے عوض پر آزاد کرنے کا بیان نوٹ: جعل ہر اس مال کو کہا جاتا ہے جو کسی آدمی کے کسی کام کرنے کے عوض مقرر کیا جائے مال کسی بھی صورت میں ہو۔ جس نے اپنے غلام کو مال پر آزاد کیا اور غلام نے اسے قبول کر لیا آزاد ہو جائے گا وَ مَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى مَالٍ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ عَتَقَ وَذَلِكَ مِثْلُ أَنْ تَقُولَ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ أَوْ بِأَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ وَإِنَّمَا يَعْتِقُ بِقُبُولِهِ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةُ الْمَالِ بِغَيْرِ الْمَالِ إِذِ الْعَبْدُ لَا يَمْلِكُ نَفْسَهُ وَمِنْ قَضِيَّةِ الْمُعَاوَضَةِ ثُبُوتُ الْحُكْمِ بِقُبُولِ الْعِوَضِ لِلْحَالِ كَمَا فِي الْبَيْعِ فَإِذَا قَبِلَ صَارَ حُرًّا وَمَا شُرِطَ دَيْنٌ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى تَصِحَّ الْكَفَالَةُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ بَدَلِ الْكِتَابَةِ لِأَنَّهُ ثَبَتَ مَعَ الْمُنَافِي وَهُوَ قِيَامُ الرِّقِّ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ وَإِطْلَاقُ لَفْظِ الْمَالِ يَنْتَظِمُ أَنْوَاعَهُ مِنَ النَّقْدِ وَالْعَرْضِ وَالْحَيَوَانِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بِغَيْرِ عَيْنِهِ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَاوَضَةُ الْمَالِ بِغَيْرِ الْمَالِ فَشَابَهَ النِّكَاحَ وَالطَّلَاقَ وَالصُّلْحَ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمْدِ وَكَذَا الطَّعَامُ وَالْمَكِيلُ وَالْمَوْزُونُ إِذَا كَانَ مَعْلُومَ الْجِنْسِ وَلَا تَضُرُّهُ جَهَالَةُ الْوَصْفِ لِأَنَّهَا يَسِيرَةٌ
Chapter on freeing for a payment. Translation: Explanation of freeing in exchange for property. Note: Ja'l is every property that is stipulated in exchange for a person performing a task. Whoever frees his slave for property and the slave accepts, he becomes free. And whoever frees his slave for property and the slave accepts, he becomes free. That is like saying: 'You are free for one thousand dirhams' or 'for one thousand dirhams'. He becomes free only by his acceptance, because it is an exchange of property for non-property, since the slave does not own himself. And from the requirements of exchange is the establishment of the ruling upon acceptance of the compensation immediately, as in sale. Thus, when he accepts, he becomes free, and the stipulated amount becomes a debt upon him, such that suretyship for it is valid, unlike the kitabah payment because it is established with something contradictory, namely the persistence of slavery as known. And the absolute use of the word 'property' encompasses its types: cash, goods, and animals, even if unspecified, because it is an exchange of property for non-property, so it resembles marriage, divorce, and compromise for intentional homicide. Similarly, food, measured items, and weighed items, if the genus is known, and ignorance of the description does not harm because it is minor.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on freeing a slave in exchange for payment (al-Itq 'ala Ja'l). The commentator defines Ja'l as property given as consideration for a task. The ruling: If a master says to his slave 'You are free for 1000 dirhams' or similar, and the slave accepts, the slave becomes free immediately. The payment becomes a debt on the slave, analogous to a sale. Unlike kitabah (contract of manumission), where the slave remains partly enslaved until payment, here the slave becomes fully free upon acceptance. The word 'mal' (property) is general, including cash, goods, animals, and even unspecified items. The analogy is drawn to marriage (mahr), divorce (khul'), and blood money compromise, where consideration can be non-specific. Ignorance of description is tolerated as minor.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): Property stipulated as consideration for performing a task; in this context, the payment for which the slave is freed.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract where a slave purchases his freedom by paying installments while remaining partly enslaved until full payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi ruling on freeing a slave for a payment, when does the slave become free?
A) Only after paying the full amount
B) Upon acceptance, and the amount becomes a debt
C) After the master dies
D) Upon the slave's request

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'itq 'ala ja'l frees the slave immediately upon acceptance; the payment becomes a debt, distinct from the deferred freedom of kitabah.

Compelling the Master: The Nature of 'Itq 'ala Ja'l
Explains the ruling and istihsan basis for compelling the master.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compelling the master to accept payment in 'itq 'ala ja'l and explain the istihsan basis.

Core Idea
Though worded as a condition, 'itq 'ala ja'l is a contract of exchange, compelling the master to accept payment.

This lesson examines the core ruling in 'itq 'ala ja'l: when a slave brings the agreed payment, the master is compelled to accept it, and the slave becomes free. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling, including the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar and the istihsan (juristic preference) that supports the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its purpose
State the ruling: the judge compels the master to accept the payment, and the slave becomes free. Note the purpose: to protect the slave from deceit (gharur).
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify Imam Zufar's objection: the master's statement is a conditional oath (ta'liq), not a contract, so no compulsion is possible.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence (istihsan)
Understand the istihsan: although the wording is conditional, the purpose is exchange (mu'awada), analogous to kitaba and hibah bi shart al-'iwad. The text argues that treating it as exchange protects the slave from harm.
Qiyas might suggest non-compulsion, but istihsan overrides it.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
Contrast the two views: under Imam Zufar, the master can refuse; under the Hanafi position, the master is forced, and the slave becomes free upon payment.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant for the slave's freedom.

باب العتق على جعل لِلْغُرُورِ عَنِ الْعَبْدِ حَتَّى يُجْبَرَ الْمَوْلى عَلَى الْقُبُولِ فَعَلى هَذَا يَدُورُ الْفِقْهُ وَيُخَرَّجُ الْمَسَائِلُ نَظِيْرُهُ الْهَبَةُ بِشَرْطِ الْعِوَضِ وَلَوْ أَدَّى الْبَعْضَ يُجْبَرُ عَلَى الْقُبُولِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَعْتِقُ مَا لَمْ يُؤَدِّ الْكُلَّ لِعَدَمِ الشَّرْطِ كَمَا إِذَا حَطَّ الْبَعْضَ وَأَدَّى الْبَاقِيَ ثُمَّ لَوْ أَدَّى أَلْفًا اكْتَسَبَهَا قَبْلَ التَّعْلِيقِ رَجَعَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَيْهِ وَعَتَقَ لِاسْتِحْقَاقِهَا وَلَوْ كَانَ اكْتَسَبَهَا بَعْدَهُ لَمْ يَرْجِعِ الْمَوْلَى عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ مَأْذُونٌ [؟] مِنْ جِهَتِهِ بِالْآدَاءِ مِنْهُ ثُمَّ الْآدَاءُ فِي قَوْلِهِ إِنْ أَدَّيْتَ يَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الْمَجْلِسِ لِأَنَّهُ تَخْسِيرٌ وَفِي قَوْلِهِ إِذَا أَدَّيْتَ لَا يَقْتَصِرُ لِأَنَّ إِذَا تُسْتَعْمَلُ لِلْوَقْتِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ مَتَى

ترجمہ پھر اگر غلام نے مال لا کر دید یا تو حاکم اس کے مولی کو اس مال کے لینے پر مجبور کرے گا (اگر وہ مال لینا نہ چاہتا ہو ) اس کے ساتھ ہی غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اس مقام میں اور دوسرے مواقع میں بھی جبر کرنے کے معنی یہ ہوتے ہیں کہ حاکم مولی کو اس مال پر قابض ہو جانے کا حکم دیدے گا۔ کیونکہ اب کوئی روک ٹوک باقی نہیں ہے اور امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ حاکم اسے مال قبول کر لینے پر مجبور نہیں کرنے گا اور قیاس کا تقاضا بھی یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ مولیٰ نے جو کچھ کہا وہ قسم کا تصرف ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے آزادی کی شرط کلام کے ساتھ مشروط کرنا ہوا۔ اس لئے غلام کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف نہیں ہے اور یہ قابل فسخ بھی نہیں ہوتا ہے اور قسم کی شرطوں کو عمل میں لانے کے لئے جبر نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ شرط پائے جانے سے پہلے کسی قسم کا استحقاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف کتابت کے کیونکہ وہ ایک معاوضہ کا معاملہ ہے اور اس میں معاوضہ کا مال واجب ہوتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ کلام لفظ کے اعتبار سے تو بے شک تعلیق یعنی شرطیہ کلام ہے۔ لیکن مقصود کے لحاظ سے یہ معاوضہ کا معاملہ ہے۔ کیونکہ مولی نے غلام کے آزاد ہونے کو جو مال کی ادائیگی پر مشروط کیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب اس کے سوا اور کچھ نہیں تھا کہ غلام کو مال دینے پر آمادہ کرے۔ اس لئے غلام کو آزاد ہونے کی بڑائی اور فضیلت حاصل ہو اور مولیٰ کو اس کے مقابلے میں مال حاصل ہو ۔ جیسا کہ کتابت کے معاملہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے اگر طلاق کے مسئلہ میں اس طرح کہے کہ میں نے تم کو ہزار درہم کے عوض طلاق دی تو یہ مال طلاق کے عوض ہوتا ہے۔ اسی بنا پر اس سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے مولی کے کلام کو ایک اعتبار سے تخلیق اور دوسرے اعتبار سے معاوضہ قرار دیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ہم نے ابتدا میں اس قول کو تعلیق کہا۔ تا کہ ظاہر لفظ پر عمل ہو جائے اور مولی سے بھی ضرر دور ہو جائے۔ اسی بناء پر اس غلام کو بیچنا اس موٹی کے لئے ممنوع نہیں ہوا اور غلام بھی اپنی کمائی میں مکمل طور پر خود مختار نہیں ہوا ہے اور اس کی ادائیگی سے پہلے اس غلام سے جتنی اولاد ہو چکی ہے اس میں آزادی کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہوا ہے اور جب اس غلام نے اپنا مال ادا کرنا چاہا تو انجام کے اعتبار سے اس قول کو معاوضہ کہا۔ تا کہ غلام دھوکہ سے بچ جائے یہاں تک کے اس کو اس مال کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ اس قاعدہ پر فقہ کی بنیاد ہے اور اس سے مسائل پیدا ہوتے ہیں۔ اس کی نظیر عوض کی شرط پر ہبہ کرنا ہے۔ یعنی اگر وہ شخص جسے کچھ ہبہ کیا گیا ( موہوب لہ) عوض دینے کے لئے مال لایا تو ہبہ کرنے والے کو اس بات پر مجبور کیا جائے گا کہ اس مال کو قبول کرلے اور اگر وہ غلام پورامال نہ لائے بلکہ تھوڑا مال لائے تو بھی مولیٰ کو اس پر قبضہ کرنے کے لئے مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ جب تک غلام اپنا پورا امال ادا نہیں کرتا ہے اس وقت تک غلام آزادنہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس وقت تک شرط نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ جیسے کہ اگر مولی نے مجموعہ میں سے کچھ کم کر دیا اور غلام نے باقی مال ادا کر دیا تو بھی وہ غلام فوزا آزاد نہیں ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ پورا مال ادا کرنا مشروط ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر غلام نے وہ رقم لا کر فی الحال ادا کر دی جو اس نے اس معاملہ تعلیق سے پہلے کسی طرح سے جمع کر دی تھی تو وہ غلام آزاد تو ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن مولی اتنی رقم مزید بعد میں اس سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ مولیٰ ان کے روپے کا پہلے سے مستحق تھا اور شرط پائے جانے سے غلام آزاد ہو گیا۔ لیکن اگر اس نے اس معاملہ تعلیق کے بعد وہ روپے کمائے ہوں تو اب اس کا مولی اس سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے گا۔ کیونکہ غلام کو اس کے مولیٰ کی طرف سے تجارت کی اجازت ہو گئی ہے۔ جبکہ اس نے غلام کی طرف سے مال ادا ہونے کی شرط لگائی۔ پھر اگر مولی نے غلام سے یہ کہا ہو کہ اگرتم مجھ کو ہزار روپے دے دو تو تم آزاد ہو۔ تو اس کلام کا اثر اس مجلس تک رہے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ جملہ اختیار دینے کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی اس مجلس میں غلام کے اختیار پر رہے گا اور اگر مولیٰ نے اس طرح کہا کہ جب تم مجھ کو ہزار روپے ادا کردو تو اس کا اثر صرف اسی مجلس تک نہیں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ ادا کا استعمال ( کسی وقت) کے مانند صرف وقت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی جب کبھی ادا کر دے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔

تشريح ... وَ إِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أَخْبَرَهُ الْحَاكِمُ عَلَى قَبْضِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْعَبْدُ وَمَعْنَى الْإِخبار فيه .... الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
Chapter: Manumission for a Payment. [The statement] is for the protection of the slave from deceit, so the master is compelled to accept. Upon this principle the fiqh revolves and from it issues issues. Its analogue is a gift with a condition of compensation. And if he pays part of it, he is compelled to accept, except that he does not become free until he pays the whole, due to the absence of the condition, just as if he deducted part and he paid the rest. Then if he pays a thousand that he earned before the ta'liq, the master takes it back from him and he becomes free because of his entitlement to it. But if he earned it after [the ta'liq], the master does not take it back from him because he is permitted [from?] from his side to pay from it. Then the payment in his statement 'if you pay' is restricted to the session because it is a giving of option (takhsir), and in his statement 'when you pay' it is not restricted, because 'idha' is used for time like 'mata'.

The Urdu commentary explains: Then if the slave brings the money and pays it, the judge will compel his master to take this money (if he does not want to). With it the slave becomes free. The meaning of compulsion here and elsewhere is that the judge orders the master to take possession of the money because no obstacle remains. Imam Zufar said the judge will not compel him to accept, and qiyas also demands this, because the master's statement is a kind of oath, a conditional freeing that does not depend on acceptance and is not revocable; no right is established before the condition is met, unlike kitaba which is a contract of exchange. Our evidence: this speech is indeed linguistically a conditional statement, but in purpose it is a contract of exchange, so we treat it as ta'liq initially to act on the literal word and avoid harm to the master, and as mu'awada ultimately to protect the slave from deceit. On this rule fiqh revolves. Its analogue is a gift with a condition of compensation. If the slave brings part, the master is compelled to accept, but he is not free until full payment. Similarly, if he brings money earned before the ta'liq, the master takes it back and the slave is free, because the master was already entitled to it; but if earned after, the master does not take it back because the slave is authorized to trade from his side. Then the difference between 'in addayta' (if you give) which is restricted to the session as it is a grant of option, and 'idha addayta' (when you give) which is not restricted because 'idha' denotes time like 'mata'.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on manumission for payment (al-Itq 'ala Ja'l). The author first states the core ruling: when a slave brings the payment agreed upon for his freedom, the judge compels the master to accept it, and the slave becomes free. This ruling is derived from considering the contract as a mu'awada (exchange) despite its conditional wording, to protect the slave from deception (gharur). The commentary then presents the objection of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) who held that no compulsion exists because the master's statement is a conditional oath, which does not create a right before the condition. The Hanafi response uses istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas: the statement is treated as a contract of exchange in purpose, analogous to kitaba (manumission by contract) and hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with condition of compensation). The passage also details sub-rulings: partial payment requires compulsion but not full freedom; money earned before the ta'liq is reclaimed by the master, but money earned after belongs to the slave due to implied permission. Finally, it distinguishes between 'in addayta' (which makes the offer valid only in that session, akin to giving an option) and 'idha addayta' (which makes the offer valid indefinitely, as 'idha' indicates time).

Key Terms
العتق على جعل (al-'itq 'ala ja'l): Manumission of a slave in exchange for a specified payment made by the slave.
الغرور (al-gharur): Deception or harm to the slave if the master could refuse acceptance.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): A conditional statement; the master's speech as a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the master compelled to accept payment in 'itq 'ala ja'l?
A) Because the master's statement is a binding contract from the start.
B) Because the purpose is exchange (mu'awada), and compulsion protects the slave from deceit.
C) Because the slave has a right to freedom regardless of payment.
D) Because the master made an oath that must be fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
The master is compelled to accept payment in 'itq 'ala ja'l because the purpose is exchange, overriding the literal conditional wording.

Sub-Rulings: Partial Payment, Earnings Timing, and Wording Nuances
Details subsidiary rulings on payment, earnings, and wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rulings on partial payment, earnings before/after ta'liq, and the effect of 'in' vs 'idha' in 'itq 'ala ja'l.

Core Idea
Partial payment compels acceptance but not freedom; earnings before ta'liq are reclaimed; 'in' limits to session, 'idha' does not.

This lesson covers important details that follow from the principle of 'itq 'ala ja'l. We will examine what happens if the slave pays only part of the amount, how earnings before and after the conditional statement affect the transaction, and the difference between the wording 'in addayta' (if you give) and 'idha addayta' (when you give). These details are essential for applying the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Examine partial payment
If the slave pays part of the agreed amount, the master is compelled to accept even that partial payment, but the slave does not become free until the entire amount is paid. This is because the condition of full payment has not been met.
Analogous to a gift with condition of compensation: partial performance compels acceptance but not full transfer.
2
Analyze earnings before and after ta'liq
If the slave pays money that he earned before the master's statement (ta'liq), the master takes it back from the slave after the slave becomes free, because the master was already entitled to those earnings. If the money was earned after the statement, the master cannot take it back, because the slave is impliedly permitted to earn and pay from that.
Earnings before belong to master; after, they are considered part of the exchange.
3
Distinguish between 'in' and 'idha'
The word 'in' (if) in 'in addayta' restricts the offer to the current session (majlis) because it gives an option (takhsir). The word 'idha' (when) in 'idha addayta' does not restrict to the session; it is like 'mata' (whenever), so the offer remains open indefinitely.
This is a linguistic nuance affecting the duration of the offer.

واجب ہوتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ کلام لفظ کے اعتبار سے تو بے شک تعلیق یعنی شرطیہ کلام ہے۔ لیکن مقصود کے لحاظ سے یہ معاوضہ کا معاملہ ہے۔ کیونکہ مولی نے غلام کے آزاد ہونے کو جو مال کی ادائیگی پر مشروط کیا ہے تو اس کا مطلب اس کے سوا اور کچھ نہیں تھا کہ غلام کو مال دینے پر آمادہ کرے۔ اس لئے غلام کو آزاد ہونے کی بڑائی اور فضیلت حاصل ہو اور مولیٰ کو اس کے مقابلے میں مال حاصل ہو ۔ جیسا کہ کتابت کے معاملہ میں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے اگر طلاق کے مسئلہ میں اس طرح کہے کہ میں نے تم کو ہزار درہم کے عوض طلاق دی تو یہ مال طلاق کے عوض ہوتا ہے۔ اسی بنا پر اس سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے مولی کے کلام کو ایک اعتبار سے تخلیق اور دوسرے اعتبار سے معاوضہ قرار دیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ہم نے ابتدا میں اس قول کو تعلیق کہا۔ تا کہ ظاہر لفظ پر عمل ہو جائے اور مولی سے بھی ضرر دور ہو جائے۔ اسی بناء پر اس غلام کو بیچنا اس موٹی کے لئے ممنوع نہیں ہوا اور غلام بھی اپنی کمائی میں مکمل طور پر خود مختار نہیں ہوا ہے اور اس کی ادائیگی سے پہلے اس غلام سے جتنی اولاد ہو چکی ہے اس میں آزادی کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہوا ہے اور جب اس غلام نے اپنا مال ادا کرنا چاہا تو انجام کے اعتبار سے اس قول کو معاوضہ کہا۔ تا کہ غلام دھوکہ سے بچ جائے یہاں تک کے اس کو اس مال کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ اس قاعدہ پر فقہ کی بنیاد ہے اور اس سے مسائل پیدا ہوتے ہیں۔ اس کی نظیر عوض کی شرط پر ہبہ کرنا ہے۔ یعنی اگر وہ شخص جسے کچھ ہبہ کیا گیا ( موہوب لہ) عوض دینے کے لئے مال لایا تو ہبہ کرنے والے کو اس بات پر مجبور کیا جائے گا کہ اس مال کو قبول کرلے اور اگر وہ غلام پورامال نہ لائے بلکہ تھوڑا مال لائے تو بھی مولیٰ کو اس پر قبضہ کرنے کے لئے مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ تا کہ جب تک غلام اپنا پورا امال ادا نہیں کرتا ہے اس وقت تک غلام آزادنہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس وقت تک شرط نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ جیسے کہ اگر مولی نے مجموعہ میں سے کچھ کم کر دیا اور غلام نے باقی مال ادا کر دیا تو بھی وہ غلام فوزا آزاد نہیں ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ پورا مال ادا کرنا مشروط ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر غلام نے وہ رقم لا کر فی الحال ادا کر دی جو اس نے اس معاملہ تعلیق سے پہلے کسی طرح سے جمع کر دی تھی تو وہ غلام آزاد تو ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن مولی اتنی رقم مزید بعد میں اس سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ مولیٰ ان کے روپے کا پہلے سے مستحق تھا اور شرط پائے جانے سے غلام آزاد ہو گیا۔ لیکن اگر اس نے اس معاملہ تعلیق کے بعد وہ روپے کمائے ہوں تو اب اس کا مولی اس سے کچھ واپس نہیں لے گا۔ کیونکہ غلام کو اس کے مولیٰ کی طرف سے تجارت کی اجازت ہو گئی ہے۔ جبکہ اس نے غلام کی طرف سے مال ادا ہونے کی شرط لگائی۔ پھر اگر مولی نے غلام سے یہ کہا ہو کہ اگرتم مجھ کو ہزار روپے دے دو تو تم آزاد ہو۔ تو اس کلام کا اثر اس مجلس تک رہے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ جملہ اختیار دینے کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی اس مجلس میں غلام کے اختیار پر رہے گا اور اگر مولیٰ نے اس طرح کہا کہ جب تم مجھ کو ہزار روپے ادا کردو تو اس کا اثر صرف اسی مجلس تک نہیں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ ادا کا استعمال ( کسی وقت) کے مانند صرف وقت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی جب کبھی ادا کر دے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔

تشريح ... وَ إِنْ أَحْضَرَ الْمَالَ أَخْبَرَهُ الْحَاكِمُ عَلَى قَبْضِهِ وَعَتَقَ الْعَبْدُ وَمَعْنَى الْإِخبار فيه .... الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
Chapter: Manumission for a Payment. [The statement] is for the protection of the slave from deceit, so the master is compelled to accept. Upon this principle the fiqh revolves and from it issues issues. Its analogue is a gift with a condition of compensation. And if he pays part of it, he is compelled to accept, except that he does not become free until he pays the whole, due to the absence of the condition, just as if he deducted part and he paid the rest. Then if he pays a thousand that he earned before the ta'liq, the master takes it back from him and he becomes free because of his entitlement to it. But if he earned it after [the ta'liq], the master does not take it back from him because he is permitted [from?] from his side to pay from it. Then the payment in his statement 'if you pay' is restricted to the session because it is a giving of option (takhsir), and in his statement 'when you pay' it is not restricted, because 'idha' is used for time like 'mata'.

The Urdu commentary explains: Then if the slave brings the money and pays it, the judge will compel his master to take this money (if he does not want to). With it the slave becomes free. The meaning of compulsion here and elsewhere is that the judge orders the master to take possession of the money because no obstacle remains. Imam Zufar said the judge will not compel him to accept, and qiyas also demands this, because the master's statement is a kind of oath, a conditional freeing that does not depend on acceptance and is not revocable; no right is established before the condition is met, unlike kitaba which is a contract of exchange. Our evidence: this speech is indeed linguistically a conditional statement, but in purpose it is a contract of exchange, so we treat it as ta'liq initially to act on the literal word and avoid harm to the master, and as mu'awada ultimately to protect the slave from deceit. On this rule fiqh revolves. Its analogue is a gift with a condition of compensation. If the slave brings part, the master is compelled to accept, but he is not free until full payment. Similarly, if he brings money earned before the ta'liq, the master takes it back and the slave is free, because the master was already entitled to it; but if earned after, the master does not take it back because the slave is authorized to trade from his side. Then the difference between 'in addayta' (if you give) which is restricted to the session as it is a grant of option, and 'idha addayta' (when you give) which is not restricted because 'idha' denotes time like 'mata'.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on manumission for payment (al-Itq 'ala Ja'l). The author first states the core ruling: when a slave brings the payment agreed upon for his freedom, the judge compels the master to accept it, and the slave becomes free. This ruling is derived from considering the contract as a mu'awada (exchange) despite its conditional wording, to protect the slave from deception (gharur). The commentary then presents the objection of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) who held that no compulsion exists because the master's statement is a conditional oath, which does not create a right before the condition. The Hanafi response uses istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas: the statement is treated as a contract of exchange in purpose, analogous to kitaba (manumission by contract) and hibah bi shart al-'iwad (gift with condition of compensation). The passage also details sub-rulings: partial payment requires compulsion but not full freedom; money earned before the ta'liq is reclaimed by the master, but money earned after belongs to the slave due to implied permission. Finally, it distinguishes between 'in addayta' (which makes the offer valid only in that session, akin to giving an option) and 'idha addayta' (which makes the offer valid indefinitely, as 'idha' indicates time).

Key Terms
التخسير (al-takhsir): Giving an option; the slave has the choice to pay only in that session.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): A conditional statement; the master's speech as a condition.
العتق على جعل (al-'itq 'ala ja'l): Manumission of a slave in exchange for a specified payment made by the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master says 'idha addayta' (when you give), when can the slave make the payment to become free?
A) Only in the same session (majlis).
B) At any time, because 'idha' indicates a future time without restriction.
C) Only within the same day.
D) Only before the master revokes the statement.

Key Takeaway
In 'itq 'ala ja'l, partial payment does not free the slave, earnings before ta'liq are reclaimed, and wording affects the duration of the offer.

Manumission for Service: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation after immediate death of freed slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad regarding the compensation due when a slave freed for service dies immediately, and identify the legal reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
Freedom is valid, but compensation is due; the dispute is whether it is the full value or the service value.

This passage from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute. When a master frees his slave for four years of service, and the slave dies immediately after acceptance, the freedom is valid. The question is: what must the slave's estate pay the master? The two great imams differ from Imam Muhammad, and their disagreement is rooted in a foundational question about the nature of compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the core scenario
The master frees the slave for four years of service; the slave accepts; the slave dies immediately. Recognize that the freedom is valid despite the death.
The acceptance triggers immediate freedom.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the slave's estate owes the full market value of the slave. Imam Muhammad: the estate owes the value of the four years of service.
The amounts may differ if slave value ≠ service value.
3
Analyse the reasoning for freedom
Freedom is valid because the service for a known period is a valid compensation (iwad). The master's offer and slave's acceptance complete the contract.
The service is analogous to money as compensation.
4
Examine the dispute's basis
The text links this dispute to another: selling the slave's own self for a specific slave girl. The same difference arises there, showing a deeper methodological divergence.
This will be explored in the next lesson.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if the slave's market value is higher than the service value, the two imams' view gives the master more. If lower, Muhammad's view gives more.
The difference matters for estate valuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ عَتَقَ ثُمَّ مَاتَ مِنْ سَاعَتِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَةُ نَفْسِهِ فِي مَالِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ قِيمَةُ خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ أَمَّا الْعِتْقُ فَلِأَنَّهُ جُعِلَتِ الْخِدْمَةُ فِي مُدَّةٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِوَضًا فَيَتَعَلَّقُ الْعِتْقُ بِالْقُبُولِ وَقَدْ وُجِدَ وَلَزِمَتْهُ خِدْمَةُ أَرْبَعِ سِنِينَ لِأَنَّهُ يَصْلُحُ عِوَضًا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَعْتَقَهُ عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْعَبْدُ فَالْخِلَافِيَّةُ فِيهِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى خِلَافِيَّةٍ أُخْرَى وَهِيَ أَنَّ مَنْ بَاعَ نَفْسَ الْعَبْدِ مِنْهُ بِجَارِيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا ثُمَّ اسْتُحِقَّتِ الْجَارِيَةُ أَوْ هَلَكَتْ يَرْجِعُ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الْعَبْدِ بِقِيمَةِ نَفْسِهِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَبِقِيمَةِ الْجَارِيَةِ عِنْدَهُ وَهِيَ مَعْرُوفَةٌ وَوَجْهُ الْبِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ كَمَا يَتَعَذَّرُ تَسْلِيمُ الْجَارِيَةِ بِالْهَلَاكِ وَالِاسْتِحْقَاقِ يَتَعَذَّرُ الْوُصُولُ إِلَى الْخِدْمَةِ بِمَوْتِ الْعَبْدِ وَكَذَا بِمَوْتِ الْوَلِيِّ فَصَارَ نَظِيرُهَا

ترجمه امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام کو پورے چار سال تک اپنی خدمت بجالانے پر آزاد کیا۔ جسے غلام نے قبول کر لیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ پھر اگر وہ غلام اسی وقت مر جائے تو امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک اس غلام کی قیت (یعنی اس کی قیمت) اس کے مال میں (بطور تاوان) واجب ہوگی۔ اور امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک چار سال کی خدمت کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ بہرحال غلام کا آزاد ہونا تو درست ہے کیونکہ خدمت کو ایک معین مدت میں عوض قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ پس عتق قبول کے ساتھ وابستہ ہو گیا اور وہ مل گیا اور غلام پر چار سال کی خدمت لازم ہے کیونکہ وہ عوض صلح ہے۔ پس یہ اسی طرح ہے جیسے اسے ایک ہزار درہم پر آزاد کیا پھر غلام مر گیا۔ یہاں اختلاف ایک دوسرے اختلاف پر مبنی ہے کہ جس نے غلام کو اس سے ایک خاص لونڈی کے عوض بیچ دیا پھر وہ لونڈی مستحقہ نکلی یا ہلاک ہوگئی تو امام صاحبین کے نزدیک مولی غلام پر اس کی قیمت (یعنی غلام کی قیمت) واپس لے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک لونڈی کی قیمت۔ اور یہ مسئلہ مشہور ہے۔ اور اس اختلاف کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح لونڈی کی تسلیم ہلاکت یا استحقاق کی وجہ سے متعذر ہو گئی اسی طرح غلام کی موت سے خدمت تک پہنچنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ پس یہ دونوں ایک جیسے ہیں۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever frees his slave for his service of four years, and the slave accepts, he becomes free. Then if he dies immediately, upon him is the value of himself in his wealth according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: the value of his service of four years. As for the freedom, it is because the service for a known period was made a compensation, so freedom becomes attached to the acceptance and it occurred, and the service of four years becomes binding on him because it is valid as a compensation. So it becomes like if he freed him for one thousand dirhams then the slave died. The difference here is based on another difference: that one who sold the slave's own self to him for a specific slave girl, then the slave girl is claimed or perishes, the master takes back from the slave the value of himself according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to him (Muhammad) the value of the slave girl. And this is well-known. The basis of this is that just as the delivery of the slave girl is obstructed by destruction or claim, so too the attainment of service is obstructed by the slave's death, so they are analogous.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case where a master frees his slave for four years of service, the slave accepts and becomes free, but then dies immediately (before performing any service). The dispute is about what the slave's estate owes the master: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the full value of the slave (i.e., his market price) must be paid, while Imam Muhammad says only the value of the four years of service (i.e., the compensation agreed upon) is due. The text explains that the freedom itself is valid because the service is a valid compensation (iwad). The disagreement is then linked to another well-known dispute: if a master sells a slave to himself (i.e., the slave buys his own freedom for a specific slave girl) and that slave girl is later claimed by a third party or perishes, the two imams say the master can recover the full value of the slave, whereas Muhammad says only the value of the slave girl. The reasoning is that when the subject matter (slave girl or the service) cannot be delivered due to extinction (halak) or claim (istihqaq), the master's right is affected. The position of the two imams focuses on the value of the slave's person as the default, while Muhammad focuses on the agreed compensation.

Key Terms
قيمة النفس (qimat al-nafs): The full market value of the slave.
قيمة الخدمة (qimat al-khidma): The monetary value of the service for a specific period (here, four years).
عوض (iwad): Compensation or consideration in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A master frees his slave for four years of service. The slave accepts and dies immediately. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what must the slave's estate pay?
A) Nothing, because the service could not be performed.
B) The full market value of the slave.
C) The value of four years of service.
D) Only the slave's earnings.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a slave freed for service dies immediately, the freedom stands, but the estate must compensate the master; the amount is disputed between the two imams and Imam Muhammad.

The Parallel Case: Selling the Slave for a Specific Slave Girl
Analogy linking two intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the dispute over compensation after a slave's death is built upon an earlier dispute concerning the sale of a slave for a specific slave girl, and identify the illa (effective cause) that connects the two cases.

Core Idea
The compensation dispute is not isolated; it mirrors a fundamental disagreement about default value versus specific compensation.

Imam Muhammad explains that the difference in the manumission-for-service case is based on another well-known dispute: when a master sells the slave's own self to him for a specific slave girl, and that slave girl is later claimed or perishes. The same pattern of disagreement arises, revealing a deeper methodological divergence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parallel case
The master sells the slave's own self to him for a specific slave girl; the slave accepts; the slave girl is later claimed (istihqaq) or perishes (halak).
This is the 'well-known' case referenced.
2
State the ruling in the parallel case
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: master recovers the full value of the slave. Imam Muhammad: master recovers the value of the slave girl.
The positions are identical in structure to the manumission case.
3
Extract the shared illa
In both cases, the agreed compensation (slave girl or service) cannot be delivered due to an external cause (claim/destruction or death). This obstruction (ta'adhur al-taslim) is the common effective cause.
The illa is the inability to deliver the specific compensation.
4
Trace the building (bina')
The text says the first dispute is 'built upon' (mabniyya) the second. This means the reasoning from the slave girl case is directly applied to the manumission case.
The same legal question arises: what is the default when the specific compensation fails?
5
Apply the analogy
Verify that the hukm in the far' (manumission) matches the asl (sale) for each position. The two imams consistently demand full slave value; Muhammad consistently demands the specific compensation value.
This consistency strengthens the analogy.

قَالَ وَمَنْ أَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ عَتَقَ ثُمَّ مَاتَ مِنْ سَاعَتِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَةُ نَفْسِهِ فِي مَالِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ قِيمَةُ خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ أَمَّا الْعِتْقُ فَلِأَنَّهُ جُعِلَتِ الْخِدْمَةُ فِي مُدَّةٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِوَضًا فَيَتَعَلَّقُ الْعِتْقُ بِالْقُبُولِ وَقَدْ وُجِدَ وَلَزِمَتْهُ خِدْمَةُ أَرْبَعِ سِنِينَ لِأَنَّهُ يَصْلُحُ عِوَضًا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَعْتَقَهُ عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْعَبْدُ فَالْخِلَافِيَّةُ فِيهِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى خِلَافِيَّةٍ أُخْرَى وَهِيَ أَنَّ مَنْ بَاعَ نَفْسَ الْعَبْدِ مِنْهُ بِجَارِيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا ثُمَّ اسْتُحِقَّتِ الْجَارِيَةُ أَوْ هَلَكَتْ يَرْجِعُ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الْعَبْدِ بِقِيمَةِ نَفْسِهِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَبِقِيمَةِ الْجَارِيَةِ عِنْدَهُ وَهِيَ مَعْرُوفَةٌ وَوَجْهُ الْبِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ كَمَا يَتَعَذَّرُ تَسْلِيمُ الْجَارِيَةِ بِالْهَلَاكِ وَالِاسْتِحْقَاقِ يَتَعَذَّرُ الْوُصُولُ إِلَى الْخِدْمَةِ بِمَوْتِ الْعَبْدِ وَكَذَا بِمَوْتِ الْوَلِيِّ فَصَارَ نَظِيرُهَا

ترجمه امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام کو پورے چار سال تک اپنی خدمت بجالانے پر آزاد کیا۔ جسے غلام نے قبول کر لیا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ پھر اگر وہ غلام اسی وقت مر جائے تو امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک اس غلام کی قیت (یعنی اس کی قیمت) اس کے مال میں (بطور تاوان) واجب ہوگی۔ اور امام محمد رحمہ اللہ کے نزدیک چار سال کی خدمت کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ بہرحال غلام کا آزاد ہونا تو درست ہے کیونکہ خدمت کو ایک معین مدت میں عوض قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ پس عتق قبول کے ساتھ وابستہ ہو گیا اور وہ مل گیا اور غلام پر چار سال کی خدمت لازم ہے کیونکہ وہ عوض صلح ہے۔ پس یہ اسی طرح ہے جیسے اسے ایک ہزار درہم پر آزاد کیا پھر غلام مر گیا۔ یہاں اختلاف ایک دوسرے اختلاف پر مبنی ہے کہ جس نے غلام کو اس سے ایک خاص لونڈی کے عوض بیچ دیا پھر وہ لونڈی مستحقہ نکلی یا ہلاک ہوگئی تو امام صاحبین کے نزدیک مولی غلام پر اس کی قیمت (یعنی غلام کی قیمت) واپس لے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک لونڈی کی قیمت۔ اور یہ مسئلہ مشہور ہے۔ اور اس اختلاف کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح لونڈی کی تسلیم ہلاکت یا استحقاق کی وجہ سے متعذر ہو گئی اسی طرح غلام کی موت سے خدمت تک پہنچنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ پس یہ دونوں ایک جیسے ہیں۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Whoever frees his slave for his service of four years, and the slave accepts, he becomes free. Then if he dies immediately, upon him is the value of himself in his wealth according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: the value of his service of four years. As for the freedom, it is because the service for a known period was made a compensation, so freedom becomes attached to the acceptance and it occurred, and the service of four years becomes binding on him because it is valid as a compensation. So it becomes like if he freed him for one thousand dirhams then the slave died. The difference here is based on another difference: that one who sold the slave's own self to him for a specific slave girl, then the slave girl is claimed or perishes, the master takes back from the slave the value of himself according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to him (Muhammad) the value of the slave girl. And this is well-known. The basis of this is that just as the delivery of the slave girl is obstructed by destruction or claim, so too the attainment of service is obstructed by the slave's death, so they are analogous.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case where a master frees his slave for four years of service, the slave accepts and becomes free, but then dies immediately (before performing any service). The dispute is about what the slave's estate owes the master: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say the full value of the slave (i.e., his market price) must be paid, while Imam Muhammad says only the value of the four years of service (i.e., the compensation agreed upon) is due. The text explains that the freedom itself is valid because the service is a valid compensation (iwad). The disagreement is then linked to another well-known dispute: if a master sells a slave to himself (i.e., the slave buys his own freedom for a specific slave girl) and that slave girl is later claimed by a third party or perishes, the two imams say the master can recover the full value of the slave, whereas Muhammad says only the value of the slave girl. The reasoning is that when the subject matter (slave girl or the service) cannot be delivered due to extinction (halak) or claim (istihqaq), the master's right is affected. The position of the two imams focuses on the value of the slave's person as the default, while Muhammad focuses on the agreed compensation.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A claim by a third party that the slave girl was actually theirs, rendering the sale defective.
بِناء (bina'): The legal construction by which one ruling is derived from another; here, the manumission dispute is built upon the slave girl dispute.
نظير (nazir): Analogue or parallel case; the text concludes that the two cases are nazir (analogous).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the dispute in the manumission case is 'built upon' which other dispute?
A) Freeing a slave for a sum of money
B) Selling a slave for a specific slave girl
C) A master marrying a slave
D) A slave being injured by a third party

Key Takeaway
The dispute about compensation for a slave freed for service is not isolated; it is built upon a parallel dispute about selling a slave for a specific slave girl, sharing the same illa of obstructed delivery.

Post-Death Emancipation on Payment: Timing of Acceptance
Ruling on emancipation after death with payment condition and timing of acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's statement 'You are free after my death on a thousand dirhams' and explain the timing of acceptance and the necessity of heir's action.

Core Idea
Acceptance after death is valid, but the slave is not freed unless the heir acts.

This passage examines a specific conditional emancipation contract where the master offers freedom upon his death in exchange for payment. The key legal puzzle is the timing of acceptance and whether the contract itself effects freedom or is merely a promise. The Hanafi school distinguishes this from tadbir (immediate acceptance) and ultimately rules that the heir's intervention is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's statement and its temporal attribution
Note that the master says 'You are free after my death on a thousand dirhams.' The phrase 'after my death' attributes the offer to a future time.
Contrast with tadbir which is an immediate offer of mudabbar status.
2
Determine the timing of acceptance based on the analogy
The text analogizes this to 'You are free tomorrow on a thousand dirhams.' In both cases, acceptance is valid only at the specified future time (after death / tomorrow).
The offer is suspended until that time.
3
Contrast with tadbir where acceptance is immediate
If the master says 'You are mudabbar on a thousand dirhams,' the offer is immediate, so acceptance must be immediate as well. The slave becomes mudabbar instantly, but the payment is not yet due.
This distinction hinges on the wording of the offer.
4
Understand the final ruling from the mashayikh
Even though acceptance is valid after death, the slave does not become free by his own acceptance. The deceased master lacks capacity to emancipate; only the heir, executor, or judge can free him.
This ruling is from al-Jami' al-Saghir and is considered sahih (correct).
5
Note the legal basis (ta'lil)
The reason (illa) is that emancipation is an act requiring the owner's capacity. A dead person cannot perform legal acts. Therefore, the slave remains enslaved until the heir frees him.
The contract is not void; it is a promise that requires the heir's execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِعَبْدِهِ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ بَعْدَ مَوْتِى عَلَى الْفِ دِرْهَم فَالْقَوْلُ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ لِإِضَافَةِ الْإِيجَابِ إِلَى مَا بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا قَالَ أَنْتَ حُرٌّ غَدًا عَلَى الْفِ دِرْهَمٍ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ اَنْتَ مُدَبَّرٌ عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ حَيْثُ يَكُونُ الْقُبُولُ إِلَيْهِ فِى الْحَالِ لأَنَّ إِيجَابَ التَّدْبِيرِ فِى الْحَالِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَجِبُ الْمَالُ لِقِيَامِ الرِّقِّ قَالُوا لَا يَعْتِقُ عَلَيْهِ فِي مَسْأَلَةِ الْكِتَابِ وَإِنْ قَبِلَ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ مَا لَمْ يَعْتِقَهُ الْوَارِثُ لِأَنَّ الْمَيِّتَ لَيْسَ بِأَهْلٍ لِلْإِعْتَاقِ وَهَذَا صَحِيحٌ ترجمہ: اور جس نے اپنے غلام سے کہا کہ تم میری موت کے بعد ہزار روپے کی ادائیگی پر آزاد ہو تو اس غلام کا اسے قبول کرنا مولیٰ کے مرجانے کے بعد معتبر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے مولی نے اس کلام کو اپنی موت کے بعد پر منسوب کیا ہے۔ تو گویا اس نے یوں کہا کہ تم کل کے دن ہزار روپے پر آزاد ہو۔ یعنی اس نے اپنے کلام میں جو وقت مقرر کیا ہے گویا اسی وقت پر اس نے موجودہ کلام کیا ہے۔ لہذا اسی وقت اس کا قبول بھی معتبر ہو گا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے کہ اگر یوں کہا کہ تم ہزار درہم کے عوض مدبر ہو۔ کہ اس کلام میں قبول کرنا فی الحال غلام کی طرف معتبر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے مدبر کرنے کے لئے فی الحال کلام کیا ہے۔ لیکن اس کا مال ابھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ غلام ابھی تک ایک خالص ( بے اختیار ) غلام ہے۔ پھر مشایخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کتاب (جامع صغیر) کے مسئلہ میں غلام آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ اگر چہ غلام اپنے مولیٰ کی موت کے بعد قبول بھی کرے۔ جب تک کہ اس کا وارث (یا وصی یا قاضی ) اسے آزاد نہ کر دے کیونکہ اس وقت مردہ مولی کو اپنے غلام آزاد کرنے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی حکم صحیح ہے۔
And whoever says to his slave: 'You are free after my death on a thousand dirhams', then acceptance is after death, because the offer is attributed to after death, so it becomes as if he said: 'You are free tomorrow on a thousand dirhams'. Contrary to if he said: 'You are mudabbar on a thousand dirhams', where acceptance is to him immediately, because the offer of tadbir is immediate, except that the money is not obligatory due to the existence of slavery. They (the scholars) said: He is not freed in the issue of the book (al-Jami' al-Saghir) even if he accepts after death, unless the heir frees him, because the dead person is not qualified for emancipation. And this is correct. Translation: And whoever said to his slave 'You are free after my death on payment of a thousand rupees', then the slave's acceptance thereof will be valid only after the master's death. Because his master attributed his speech to after his death. So it is as if he said 'You are free tomorrow on a thousand rupees'. That is, the time he specified in his speech is as if he made that statement at that time. Hence, his acceptance at that time is also valid. Contrary to the case if he said 'You are mudabbar in exchange for a thousand dirhams'. In that statement, acceptance is valid immediately from the slave. Because he made his speech for tadbir immediately. But his money will not be obligatory yet, because the slave is still a pure (powerless) slave. Then the mashayikh ruled that in the issue of the book (al-Jami' al-Saghir), the slave will not be freed, even if the slave accepts after the master's death, unless his heir (or executor or judge) frees him, because at that time the dead master does not have the capacity to free his slave. And this ruling is correct.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on a specific type of emancipation contract: when a master says to his slave 'You are free after my death on a thousand dirhams'. The key issue is the timing of acceptance. The author explains that acceptance by the slave is only valid after the master's death, because the offer (ījāb) is attributed to that future time. This is analogous to saying 'You are free tomorrow on a thousand dirhams' – the condition specifies a future time. In contrast, if the master says 'You are mudabbar on a thousand dirhams', acceptance is immediate because tadbir is a form of emancipation that takes effect upon death, but the offer is made in the present. The passage then notes a ruling from the mashāyikh (later authorities) based on the issue in al-Jāmi' al-Ṣaghīr: even if the slave accepts after death, he is not freed unless the heir (or executor or judge) frees him, because the deceased is not legally capable of emancipation. This is a substantive ruling: the contract itself does not effect freedom; rather, it is a promise that requires the heir's action.

Key Terms
الإِيجَاب (al-ījāb): The offer or declaration made by the master in the emancipation contract.
التَّدْبِير (al-tadbīr): A form of emancipation where the master declares that the slave will be free upon the master's death, with the condition that acceptance is immediate.
الْقَبُول (al-qabūl): The acceptance by the slave of the master's offer; its timing depends on the nature of the offer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a master tells his slave 'You are free after my death on a thousand dirhams', when is the slave's acceptance valid?
A) Immediately, like tadbīr.
B) Only after the master's death.
C) At any time before the master's death.
D) The acceptance is never valid.

Key Takeaway
The slave does not gain freedom by his own acceptance after the master's death; the heir must act to free him.

Compensation Upon Death After Emancipation for Service: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation after emancipation for service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation when a slave dies after accepting emancipation in exchange for service and identify the foundational dispute on which it is based.

Core Idea
When service is impossible, compensation amount depends on whether the 'iwaḍ is the service's value or the slave's value.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Saghir, as commented in al-Hidayah. When a slave is freed in exchange for four years of service and dies before serving, should his estate owe the value of his person or the value of the service? The answer hinges on a deeper analogy with a sale of the slave's person for a specific slave-girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the agreement
The master says: 'You are free in exchange for your service for four years.' The slave accepts. The slave then dies immediately. Both sides agree the slave is free upon acceptance. The dispute is about what compensation is due from the slave's estate.
The contract is valid (sahih) because service is suitable as compensation ('iwaḍ).
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that the value of the slave's person (qīmat nafsihi) is due. Imam Muhammad holds that only the value of the service for four years (qīmat khidmatihi) is due.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Recognize the basis in another dispute
The passage says this dispute is built on another known dispute: if a master sells his slave's person in exchange for a specific slave-girl, and that slave-girl is lost or reclaimed, the Shaykhayn say the master recovers the value of the slave, while Muhammad says he recovers the value of the slave-girl.
This foundational dispute establishes the principle: when the compensation item is impossible to deliver, what value replaces it?
4
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
In our case, the service is like the slave-girl: both are the 'iwaḍ. Death of the slave prevents delivery of service, just as loss of the slave-girl prevents delivery of her. The same reasoning applies: the Shaykhayn analogize to the slave's person being the subject of the exchange, while Muhammad analogizes to the specific compensation item.
The analogy is talil (reasoning) showing the logical connection between the two cases.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the slave has assets, under the Shaykhayn the master claims the (usually higher) value of the slave. Under Muhammad, he claims only the (potentially lower) value of the service. The difference affects the estate's liability.
This illustrates why ikhtilaf matters in practice: different outcomes for the same set of facts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ اَعْتَقَ عَبْدَهُ عَلَى خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ فَقَبِلَ الْعَبْدُ عَتَقَ ثُمَّ مَاتَ مِنْ سَاعَتِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيْمَةُ نَفْسِهِ فِي مَالِهِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ قِيمَةُ خِدْمَتِهِ أَرْبَعَ سِنِينَ أَمَّا الْعِتْقُ فَلِأَنَّهُ جُعِلَ الْخِدْمَةُ فِي مُدَّةٍ مَعْلُومَةٍ عِوَضًا فَيَتَعَلَّقُ الْعِتْقُ بِالْقُبُولِ وَقَدْ وُجِدَ وَلَزِمَتْهُ خِدْمَةُ أَرْبَعِ سِنِينَ لِأَنَّهُ يَصْلُحُ عِوَضًا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَعْتَقَهُ عَلَى أَلْفِ دِرْهَمٍ ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْعَبْدُ فَالْخِلَافُ فِيهِ بِنَاءً عَلَى خِلَافٍ آخَرَ وَهِيَ أَنَّ مَنْ بَاعَ نَفْسَ الْعَبْدِ مِنْهُ بِجَارِيَةٍ بِعَيْنِهَا ثُمَّ اسْتُحِقَّتِ الْجَارِيَةُ أَوْ هَلَكَتْ يَرْجِعُ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الْعَبْدِ بِقِيْمَةِ نَفْسِهِ عِنْدَهُمَا وَبِقِيْمَةِ الْجَارِيَةِ عِنْدَهُ وَهِيَ مَعْرُوفَةٌ وَوَجْهُ الْبِنَاءِ أَنَّهُ كَمَا يَتَعَذَّرُ تَسْلِيمُ الْجَارِيَةِ بِالْهَلَاكِ وَالِاسْتِحْقَاقِ يَتَعَذَّرُ الْوُصُولُ إِلَى الْخِدْمَةِ بِمَوْتِ الْعَبْدِ وَكَذَا بِمَوْتِ الْمَوْلَى فَصَارَ نَظِيرَهَا ترجمه: امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنے غلام کو پورے چار سال تک اپنی خدمت بجالانے پر آزاد کیا۔ جسے غلام نے قبول کر لیا تو وہ آزاد ہو گیا۔ لیکن اس خدمت کی ادائیگی سے پہلے ہی وہ غلام مر گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ وابو یوسف کے نزدیک غلام کے مال میں (اگر موجود ہو ) تو غلام کی ذات کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور امام محمد نے کہا ہے کہ غلام کی چار سالہ خدمت کی قیمت لازم ہوگی اور مصنف نے کہا ہے کہ آزاد ہونا اس وجہ سے ہوا کہ یہ ایک معین مدت تک خدمت کرنا آزادی کا عوض قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے غلام کے قبول کرنے پر آزادی متعلق ہو جائے گی اور غلام کا اس شرط کو قبول کر لینا پایا گیا ہے اور غلام پر چار برس اس کی خدمت واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس کی خدمت بجا آوری میں اس کے عوض بننے کی صلاحیت موجود ہے یعنی خدمت گزاری اس کا عوض ہو سکتی ہے۔ تو ایسا ہو گیا کہ گویا مولیٰ نے غلام کو ہزار روپے پر آزاد کیا۔ پھر وہ غلام اس شرط کو قبول کر لینے کے بعد مال کی ادائیگی سے پہلے انتقال کر گیا۔ معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ اس مسئلہ میں موجودہ اختلاف در اصل ایک دوسرے مسئلہ میں اختلاف پر مبنی ہے اور وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے غلام سے اپنی ایک معینہ باندی کی طرف اشارہ کر کے کہا کہ میں نے تم کو تمہاری ذات فروخت کی جس کا عوض یہ باندی ہے اور غلام نے اس کہنے اور ایجاب کرنے کو قبول کر لیا جس سے وہ غلام آزاد ہو گیا۔ پھر کسی شخص نے اس باندی پر اپنی مملوکہ ہونے کا دعوی کیا اور اسے ثابت کر کے اپنے قبضہ میں لے لیا یا سپرد کرنے سے وہ باندی مرگئی۔ اس صورت میں شیخین کے نزدیک یہ مولی اپنے اس سابق غلام سے اس کی ذات کی قیمت (جو پہلے ہو سکتی تھی ) مانگ لے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک خود اس کی اپنی قیمت نہیں بلکہ اس معینہ باندی کی قیمت لے گا۔ یہ مسئلہ فقہاء میں معروف ہے۔ اس پر آزادی کے ہمارے مسئلہ کی بنیاد ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہ اس باندی کے مرجانے یا کسی کی مستحق ثابت ہو جانے سے اب پہلے مولی کے پاس آنا ممکن نہیں رہا۔ اس طرح غلام کے مرنے سے غلام کی خدمت ملنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس طرح یہ مسئلہ کی نظیر ہو گیا ۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: And whoever emancipates his slave in exchange for his service for four years, and the slave accepts, he is free. Then he dies immediately, then upon him is the value of his person in his property according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad said: the value of his service for four years. As for the emancipation, it is because service for a known period is made as a compensation, so emancipation is attached to acceptance, and it has occurred. And service for four years becomes obligatory upon him because it is suitable as compensation. So it becomes like when he emancipates him for a thousand dirhams, then the slave dies. The dispute here is based on another dispute: that whoever sells the person of his slave to him in exchange for a specific slave-girl, then the slave-girl is claimed (by a rightful owner) or perishes, the master recovers from the slave the value of his person according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to him (Muhammad) the value of the slave-girl. And this is known. And the basis is that just as delivery of the slave-girl is prevented by destruction or claim (of ownership), so is access to service prevented by the death of the slave, similarly by the death of the master. So it becomes analogous. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that if someone freed his slave in exchange for his performing service for four full years, and the slave accepted, then he is free. But if the slave died before performing that service, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the value of the slave's person (if he has property) is obligatory, and Imam Muhammad said: the value of the service for four years is obligatory. And the author said: The freedom occurred because service for a specified period was made as a compensation for freedom. Thus freedom is attached to acceptance, and acceptance has been found. And four years of service become obligatory upon him because his service is suitable as compensation. So it is as if the master freed him for a thousand dirhams, then the slave died after acceptance but before payment. It should be known that the existing dispute in this issue is based on another dispute: that a person sold his slave's person to him (the slave) by pointing to a specific slave-girl and saying 'I have sold you your person in exchange for this slave-girl', and the slave accepted, so the slave became free. Then someone claimed ownership of that slave-girl and proved it and took possession, or the slave-girl died before delivery. In this case, according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the master will recover from his former slave the value of his person, and according to Imam Muhammad, not the value of his own person but the value of that specific slave-girl. This issue is well-known among jurists. Upon this is based our issue of emancipation. The reason is that because the slave-girl died or was claimed by a rightful owner, she cannot be delivered to the master. Similarly, due to the slave's death, the service cannot be obtained. So this issue became analogous.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the compensation owed when a slave is freed in exchange for four years of service, but dies before performing the service. Imam Muhammad's text in al-Jami' al-Saghir states that the slave becomes free upon acceptance, but upon his death, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that the value of the slave's own person (qīmat nafsihi) is due from his estate, while Imam Muhammad holds that only the value of the service for four years (qīmat khidmatihi) is due. The commentary explains the reasoning: both sides agree that emancipation is valid because service is a suitable compensation (ʿiwaḍ). The dispute arises from a foundational dispute: if a master sells his slave's person to himself in exchange for a specific slave-girl, and that slave-girl is then lost or claimed, the Shaykhayn say the master recovers the slave's person's value, while Muhammad says he recovers the slave-girl's value. This is the basis: in both cases, the subject of the compensation (the slave-girl or the service) becomes impossible to deliver, so the question is what value replaces it. The passage clarifies that the ruling applies similarly whether the slave dies or the master dies.

Key Terms
قِيمَةُ نَفْسِهِ (qīmat nafsihī): The market value of the slave's person at the time of the contract.
قِيمَةُ خِدْمَتِهِ (qīmat khidmatihī): The monetary value of the slave's service for the specified period (here four years).
الْعِوَض (al-ʿiwaḍ): The compensation or countervalue in a contract; in this case, service is the ʿiwaḍ for emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a slave dies after accepting emancipation in exchange for four years of service, what compensation is due from his estate?
A) The value of the slave's person.
B) The value of the service for four years.
C) Nothing, because the service was not performed.
D) The value of a specific slave-girl.

Key Takeaway
When a condition of service becomes impossible due to death, Hanafi imams disagree whether the compensation is the value of the person or the value of the service, based on a foundational analogy to a sale of the slave's person for a specific item.

Manumission for Service: Compensation Upon Slave's Death
Explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on the compensation when a slave dies after accepting manumission for service.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the compensation due from a slave's estate when he dies after accepting manumission for service, and state the Shaykhayn's position and its basis.

Core Idea
In 'itq 'ala ja'l, if the slave dies before service, the Shaykhayn require the slave's market value; Imam Muhammad requires the value of the service only.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: a master frees his slave in exchange for a fixed period of service (four years). The slave accepts but dies before performing any service. What must be paid from the slave's estate? We will explore the two positions, their underlying reasoning, and the connection to a well-known analogous case involving a slave-girl.

Guided Path
1
State the case and the Hanafi positions
Identify the key facts: master says 'you are free in exchange for 4 years service', slave accepts, then dies before service. State the two positions: Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) say value of slave's person; Imam Muhammad says value of the service.
2
Trace the underlying analogy
Identify the established case where a master sells his slave for a specific slave-girl, the slave becomes free, and then the slave-girl is lost. This case informs the current dispute.
The analogy shows the same disagreement: value of the slave's person vs. value of the specific item (slave-girl or service).
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's reasoning
Explain why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the slave's person is the subject of the transaction. Key points: the slave is valuable property (mal mutaqawwim); acceptance triggers manumission immediately; the consideration is for the person, not for the service per se.
They analogize to a slave freed for a fixed dirham amount who dies before paying.
4
Analyze Imam Muhammad's reasoning
Explain why Imam Muhammad holds that the service (a specific non-property right) is the consideration. Key points: manumission has no price in Sharia; the service is a right, not property; when delivery becomes impossible, the value of the specified thing (the service) is due.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Note the practical difference: full market value of the slave vs. the (likely lower) value of the service. Identify the relied-upon position: the Shaykhayn's view is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
The basis for tarjih: the slave is property, and consideration for property is property.

دوسرے مسئلہ میں اختلاف پر مبنی ہے اور وہ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اپنے غلام سے اپنی ایک معینہ باندمی کی طرف اشارہ کر کے کہا کہ میں نے تم کو تمہاری ذات فروخت کی جس کا عوض یہ باندی ہے اور غلام نے اس
