بعد فوت ہو گیا۔ کیا ایسی صورت میں غلام آزاد ہوا۔ یا اس کے نفس کی قیمت واجب الادا ہوگی یا خدمت کی قیمت ادا کرنا لازمی ہوگی ۔ چونکہ آقا نے غلام کو خود اسی کے ہاتھوں خدمت کے عوض فروخت کیا تھا۔ اسلئے عنق کا عوض خدمت ہوئی ۔ اگر غلام متعینہ یا معلوم مدت تک زندہ رہا اور معینہ بدت تک خدمت گزاری کی تو وجود شرط کی وجہ سے ایجاب عتق ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اگر غلام قبول کرنے کے بعد اور ادائے خدمت سے پہلے چل بسا تو شیخین (امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف) کے نزدیک غلام کے مال میں سے اس کے نفس کی قیمت ادا کی جائے گی۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ایک معلوم مدت کی قیمت واجب الادا ہوگی ۔ شیخین اور امام محمد کے بیان کردہ مسئلہ کی حقیقت اسی طرح مسئلہ خدمت میں بھی ادائے عوض ناممکن ہے۔ اس اصول کے پیش نظر امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہوگی کہ متعینہ چیز کی قیمت کا وجوب اسلئے ہوگا کہ کسی چیز کا تعین اس چیز کا عوض ہے۔ جو کہ مال نہیں ۔ یعنی یہ حق کا عوض ہے۔ جبکہ شریعت میں عشق کی قیمت نہیں ہے۔ لہذا چیز کا تعین در اصل اس کا مین ہے جس کی قیمت کا وجوب لازم ہوگا۔ شیخین (امام اعظم و امام ابو یوسف) کی دلیل یہ ہوگی۔ کہ متعینہ چیز غلام کی ذات کا عوض ہے عشق کا نہیں۔ کیونکہ غلام مال متقوم ہے۔ اسلئے اگر غلام قبول کرنے کے بعد اور ادائے خدمت سے پہلے فوت ہو گیا۔ تو غلام کے مال میں سے اس کے نفس (ذات) کی قیمت ادا کی جائے گی۔ عشق تو غلام کے قبول کرتے ہی ثابت ہو گیا۔ یعنی غلام نے اس کو قبول کیا تو وہ آزاد ہو گیا۔ اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے آقا نے ہزار درہم پر غلام کو آزاد کیا اور قبول کے بعد اور ادائے مال سے پہلے جاں بحق ہو گیا۔
اس مثال سے یہ واضح ہوا کہ یہ صورت معاوضہ کے حکم میں ہے کہ وجود قبول سے نزول معتق متحقق ہوتا ہے۔ واضح رہے کہ شیخین اور امام محمد کے مابین اختلاف کی بنیاد دوسرے اختلاف پر قائم ہے۔ وہ یہ ہے کہ آقا نے اپنے غلام کو خود اسی کے ہاتھ ایک متعینہ لونڈی کے بدلے میں فروخت کر دیا۔ غلام اسے قبول کر کے آزاہ ھو گیا۔ پھر اس لونڈی پر کسی دوسرے شخص نے اپنا حق ثابت کر کے آقا سے واپس کر لی یا وہ لونڈی آقا کے حوالے کرنے سے پہلے چل بسی۔ تو شیخین کے نزدیک آقا اپنے اس غلام سے اس کے نفس (ذات) کی قیمت وصول کرے گا۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم . ۳۳ باب العتق على جعل
لونڈی متذکرہ کی قیمت وصول کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ خدمت ایسی چیز کا عوض ہے جو کہ مال نہیں ۔ یعنی یہ عشق کا عوض ہے۔ عشق کی قیمت نہیں ہوتی۔ چنانچہ خدمت کی سپر دی ناممکن ہے تو اس کی قیمت ادا کرنا ضروری ہے۔ جبکہ شیخین فرماتے ہیں کہ خدمت کا عوض مال ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ غلام کی ذات کا عوض ہے۔ اور غلام کا شمار مال میں ہوتا ہے۔ مگر جب عوض خدمت کا ادا کرنا ممکن نہیں ۔ تو غلام جو کہ اپنے عوض کا بدل ہے۔ اس کا ادا کرنا ضروری ہو الیکن غلام کو واپس کر ناصحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حق فسح کو قبول نہیں کرتا۔ اسلئے اس کی قیمت ادا کر نالازمی ہو گیا۔ لونڈی ہو یا غلام دونوں خدمت گار ہوتے ہیں۔ لونڈی سپرد ہونے سے قبل ہلاکت یا وجود استحقاق کی وجہ سے اور غلام آقا کا قول قبول کرنے کی وجہ سے اثبات عشق کی بنا پر مولی (آقا) کے قیام رق (غلامی) سے دور ہو گئے۔ یا آقا اپنی موت کے ان دونوں (لونڈی اور غلام) سے خدمت وصول نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسلئے غلام کے نفس (ذات) کی قیمت ہی وصول کی جائے گی نہ کہ خدمت کی۔
Chapter of Manumission on Payment. If the slave accepted, then he became free. But before performing the service, the slave died. According to Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, from the slave's property (if present), the value of the slave's person is obligatory. And Imam Muhammad said that the value of the four years of service is incumbent. And the author said that the freeing occurred because serving for a fixed period was made the consideration for freedom. Therefore, upon the slave's acceptance, freedom becomes contingent, and the slave's acceptance of the condition is found, and four years of service are obligatory on the slave. Because in performing this service, the capacity to be a consideration exists, meaning service can be its consideration. So it became as if the master freed the slave for a thousand rupees. Then the slave died after accepting the condition but before paying the wealth. It should be known that the existing difference in this issue is actually based on a difference in another issue, which is: A man said to his slave, pointing to a specific slave-girl of his, 'I have sold you for your person, whose consideration is this slave-girl,' and the slave accepted the statement and offer, so the slave became free. Then someone claimed ownership of that slave-girl, proved it, and took possession, or the slave-girl died after being handed over. In this case, according to the Shaykhayn, this master will demand from his former slave the value of his person (which he could have had), and according to Imam Muhammad, he will receive not his own value but the value of that specific slave-girl. This issue is well-known among jurists. Our issue of freedom is based on it. Because with the death of the slave-girl or another proving entitlement, it is no longer possible for her to come to the former master. Similarly, with the death of the slave, receiving the slave's service is impossible. Thus this became analogous. Explanation: The master freed his slave in exchange for four years of service, and the slave accepted it. The slave died after acceptance but before performing service. In such a case, is the slave freed, or is the value of his person obligatory, or is the value of service necessary to pay? Since the master sold the slave to himself in exchange for service, the consideration for manumission became service. If the slave lived the fixed period and performed service, due to the condition being met, the manumission is established. If the slave died after acceptance but before service, according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf), the value of his person is paid from his property. According to Imam Muhammad, the value of a fixed period is obligatory. The reality of the issue stated by Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad is that in the service issue, paying the consideration is impossible. Based on this principle, Imam Muhammad's proof is that the obligation of the value of a specific thing is because specification of a thing is its consideration, which is not property. That is, it is a consideration for a right, while in Shariah there is no value for manumission. Therefore, specifying the thing is essentially its equivalent, so its value becomes obligatory. The proof of the Shaykhayn (Imam A'zam and Imam Abu Yusuf) is that the specific thing is a consideration for the slave's person, not for manumission, because the slave is valuable property. So if the slave dies after acceptance but before service, the value of his person is paid from his property. Manumission is established upon the slave's acceptance, i.e., when the slave accepted, he became free. An example of this is if the master freed the slave for a thousand dirhams, and he died after acceptance but before paying the wealth. From this example, it becomes clear that this case is in the ruling of compensation: upon the existence of acceptance, the descent of manumission occurs. It should be clear that the difference between Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad is based on another difference. That is: The master sold his slave to himself in exchange for a specific slave-girl. The slave accepted and became free. Then someone proved a right over that slave-girl and took her back from the master, or the slave-girl died before being handed over. According to the Shaykhayn, the master will collect from this slave the value of his person. According to Imam Muhammad, the value of that specific slave-girl will be collected. Because service is the consideration for something that is not property, i.e., it is the consideration for manumission. Manumission has no value. Therefore, delivering service is impossible, so its value must be paid. The Shaykhayn say that the consideration for service is property, because it is consideration for the slave's person, and the slave is counted as property. But when it is not possible to pay the consideration of service, the slave, who is the substitute of his consideration, must be paid, but returning the slave is not correct because the right does not accept dissolution. Hence, its value becomes necessary. Both the slave-girl and the slave are servants. The slave-girl, due to destruction before delivery or existence of entitlement, and the slave, due to acceptance of the master's statement and establishment of manumission, have been removed from the master's ownership. Or the master cannot receive service from both due to death. Therefore, only the value of the slave's person will be collected, not the service.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a slave who is freed in exchange for a fixed period of service (four years) and dies after accepting but before performing any service. The core legal question is: What compensation is due from the slave's estate? The text presents two positions: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that the value of the slave's person (his market value) must be paid from his property. (2) Imam Muhammad holds that only the value of the remaining service (the four years) is due. The author explains that this dispute is rooted in another well-known case: a master sells his slave in exchange for a specific slave-girl; if that slave-girl is lost or claimed by another, the Shaykhayn require the value of the slave's person, while Imam Muhammad requires the value of the slave-girl. The underlying principle is whether the consideration for manumission is considered a property right (as Shaykhayn view it, since the slave is valuable property) or a non-property right (as Imam Muhammad views it, since manumission itself is not priced). The passage then provides a detailed analogy: the case of the slave dying before service is analogous to the case of the slave-girl being lost before delivery. The author concludes that the Shaykhayn's position is that the slave's person is the consideration, so his value must be paid; Imam Muhammad's position is that the service (a specific non-property) is the consideration, so its value must be paid. The passage also includes a brief example of a slave freed for a thousand dirhams who dies before payment, which illustrates the Shaykhayn's view that the acceptance itself triggers manumission and the obligation of the value of the person.

Key Terms
عتق على جعل ('itq 'ala ja'l): Manumission upon a payment or condition, where freedom is granted in exchange for a specified consideration (often service or money).
خدمة (khidmah): Service, specifically the labor or work promised by the slave for a fixed period as consideration for freedom.
عوض ('iwad): Consideration, the thing given in exchange for something else. Here, it is the service or value given for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, if a slave is freed in exchange for four years of service but dies before performing any service, what must be paid from his estate?
A) The value of the remaining service (four years of labor)
B) The value of the slave's person (his market price)
C) Nothing, because manumission is invalid
D) The value of the slave-girl mentioned in the analogy

Key Takeaway
In 'itq 'ala ja'l, if the slave dies after acceptance but before service, the relied-upon Hanafi position requires payment of the slave's full market value, not just the value of the service.

Conditional Manumission with Marriage and Third-Party Payment
Ruling that freeing is valid but no payment owed when marriage condition fails

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional manumission with a third-party payment promise and distinguish it from the ruling in divorce by identifying the underlying legal principle.

Core Idea
A third-party promise to pay for a manumission creates no liability because stipulating payment on a stranger is invalid in manumission—unlike divorce.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced ruling where a third party promises to pay for freeing a slave-girl on condition of marriage, but the condition fails. The Hanafi school holds that the freeing is valid and the promisor owes nothing. Understanding the reasoning behind this distinction—comparing manumission with divorce—is essential for grasping the school's approach to stipulations involving strangers. Let's walk through the scenario, the ruling, and the ta'lil (causal reasoning) that justifies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exact scenario
Read the scenario carefully: A (orderer) tells B (owner): 'Free your slave-girl for 1000 dirhams upon me on condition that you marry her to me.' B frees the slave-girl, but she refuses marriage.
The condition is marriage, not payment. Payment is promised by a third party (A).
2
State the ruling from the text
The text says: 'al-'itq ja'iz wa la shay'a 'ala al-āmir' – the freeing is valid and nothing is on the orderer. Note that the freeing is valid because the owner performed the act; the condition failure does not invalidate the manumission.
The ruling has two parts: validity of the act and non-liability of the orderer.
3
Identify the general principle
The text invokes a previously established principle: If someone tells an owner to free his slave for a sum promised by the orderer, nothing is on the orderer. This is because stipulating payment on a stranger (ajnabī) is not permissible in manumission.
The principle is about sharṭ al-badal 'ala al-ajnabī in 'itq vs. ṭalāq.
4
Compare with divorce
The text contrasts the case with divorce: if someone says 'Divorce your wife for 1000 dirhams upon me,' and the husband does, the orderer becomes liable. The reason: stipulating payment on a stranger is permissible in divorce.
This contrast highlights the difference in legal treatment of third-party payments between 'itq and ṭalāq.
5
Note the fa'idah (benefit) about circumcision
The text adds a benefit: by analogy, if a father circumcises his young daughter with his own wealth, the obligation falls on him. This is inferred from the manumission rule: if a stranger would be liable, the father is a fortiori liable.
This secondary point reinforces the principle that liability follows the person who performs the act if the condition is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لِغَيْرِهِ اَعْتِقَ عَبْدَكَ عَلَى اَلْفِ دِرْهَم عَلَيَّ فَفَعَلَ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٌ وَيَقَعُ الْعِتْقُ عَنِ الْمَامُورِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ لِغَيْرِهِ طَلَّقْ امْرَأَتَكَ عَلَى اَلْفِ دِرْهُم عَلَيَّ فَفَعَلَ حَيْثُ يَحِبُّ الْاَ لْفُ عَلَى الَّا مِرِلَاتَ اشْتِرَاطَ الْبَدَلِ عَلَى الْأَجْنَبِي فِى الطَّلَاقِ جَائِزَوَ فِى الْعِتَاقِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَقَدْ قَرَّرْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ نکاح کرنے سے انکار کر دیا۔ تو یہ آزاد ہو جانا جائز ہوا۔ لیکن اس حکم دینے والے پر کچھ بھی مال لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے سے کہا کہ تم اپنے غلام کو ایسے ہزار درہم کے عوض آزاد کرو جو مجھ پر لازم ہوں گے اور اس نے اسے آزاد کر دیا تو اس کہنے والے پر لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے اور آزاد کرنا اسی شخص کی طرف سے ہوتا ہے جس کا وہ غلام تھا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے کہ اگر دوسرے سے کسی نے یہ کہا کہ تم اپنی بیوی کو ہزار درہم کے عوض طلاق دے دو جو کہ مجھ پر لازم ہوں گے اور اس نے ایسا ہی کیا تو کہنے والے پر وہ ہزار درہم لازم آجائیں گے۔ کیونکہ طلاق کے مسئلہ میں کسی اجنبی پر مال عوض کی شرط لگانا جائز ہے لیکن آزادی کے مسئلہ میں اجنبی کے ذمہ مال کی شرط کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اس مسئلہ کو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ فائدہ یعنی ضلع کے باب میں یہ مسئلہ بیان کیا جا چکا ہے کہ اگر باپ نے اپنے مال سے اپنی چھوٹی لڑکی کا ضلع لیا تو باپ پر ہی لازم ہوگا کیونکہ جب اجنبی شخص پر مال لازم ہو جاتا ہے تو باپ پر بدرجہ اولی لازم ہوگا۔ تشریح ایک شخص نے دوسرے سے کہا اعتق اَمَتَكَ عَلَى الْفِ دِرْهَم عَلَيَّ عَلَى أَنْ تَزَوَّجَنِيهَا پس مالک نے اپنی باندی کو آزاد کر دیا آزادی واقع ہو جائے گی اور اجنبی شخص پر کچھ لازم نہ ہوگا جیسے اگر کسی نے دوسرے شخص سے کہا اعتق عَبْدَكَ عَلَى الْفِ دِرْهَم عَلَيَّ مالک نے غلام کو آزاد کرا دیا تو اجنبی شخص پر کچھ لازم نہ ہوگا اور وجہ یہ ہے کہ اپنی ملکیت کو دوسرے کے مال کے بدلے میں مشروط کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ لہذا باندی آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے کہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے آدمی سے کہا طلق امرأتكَ عَلَى الْفِ دِرْهَم عَلَيَّ اس شخص نے طلاق
And if someone says to another, 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand dirhams upon me on condition that you marry her to me,' so he does it, but she refuses to marry him, then the freeing is valid and nothing is on the orderer. Because if someone says to another, 'Free your slave for a thousand dirhams upon me,' and he does, nothing is incumbent on him, and the freeing occurs from the one commanded. Contrary to the case when he says to another, 'Divorce your wife for a thousand dirhams upon me,' and he does, where the thousand becomes obligatory on the orderer. Because stipulating a payment on a stranger in divorce is permissible, but in manumission it is not permissible. And we have already established this before. Translation: And if someone said to another, 'Free your slave-girl in exchange for a thousand dirhams which will be obligatory on me, but on condition that you marry her to me.' So the man did that, but the woman refused to marry him. So the freeing is valid, but nothing is obligatory on the orderer. Because if one person said to another, 'Free your slave for a thousand dirhams which will be obligatory on me,' and he freed him, nothing is on the speaker, and the freeing is from the slave's owner. Contrary to the case where someone said to another, 'Divorce your wife for a thousand dirhams which will be on me,' and he did, then those thousand dirhams become obligatory on the speaker. Because in the issue of divorce, stipulating payment by a stranger is permissible, but in the issue of manumission, it is not permissible to stipulate payment on a stranger. And we have already explained this issue. Benefit: In the chapter on circumcision, it has been stated that if a father circumcises his young daughter with his own wealth, it is obligatory on him. Because when a stranger becomes liable for payment, the father is more worthy. Explanation: One person said to another, 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand dirhams upon me on condition that you marry her to me.' So the owner freed his slave-girl. The freedom occurs, and nothing is on the stranger. Just as if someone said to another, 'Free your slave for a thousand dirhams upon me,' and the owner freed the slave, then nothing is on the stranger. The reason is that making one's own ownership conditional on another's wealth is not valid. Hence the slave-girl becomes free. Contrary to the case where someone said to another, 'Divorce your wife for a thousand dirhams upon me,' and that person divorced.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a conditional manumission where a third party promises to pay the consideration and also stipulates marriage. The scenario: A (the orderer) says to B (the owner), 'Free your slave-girl for a thousand dirhams upon me, on condition that you marry her to me.' B frees the slave-girl, but the slave-girl refuses to marry A. The ruling: The freeing is valid and A is not liable to pay anything. The text explains that this is based on a general principle: If a stranger (ajnabi) tells an owner to free his slave for a specific payment promised by the stranger, the freeing is valid but the stranger is not liable for the payment. In contrast, if a stranger tells a husband to divorce his wife for a payment promised by the stranger, the stranger becomes liable for that payment. The difference is that in divorce, it is permissible to stipulate a payment on a third party, but in manumission, it is not permissible. The text further adds a 'benefit' (fa'idah) drawn from the chapter on circumcision: by analogy, if a father circumcises his young daughter with his own wealth, the obligation falls on him directly, because if a stranger were liable, the father is a fortiori liable. The explanation reiterates that conditional manumission with a promise of payment from a stranger does not make the stranger liable because one cannot make ownership conditional on another's wealth. The passage concludes with a contrast to divorce where liability attaches.

Key Terms
الآمر (al-āmir): The person who tells another to perform an act (here, to free a slave or divorce a wife) and promises to pay a consideration.
شرط البدل على الأجنبي (sharṭ al-badal 'ala al-ajnabī): Stipulating that a payment (badal) be made by a third party (ajnabī) who is not a party to the original transaction.
عتاق ('itāq): Manumission, the act of freeing a slave. In this context, it refers to freeing someone else's slave with a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the given scenario, if a person tells a slave-owner to free his slave-girl for a thousand dirhams promised by the orderer on condition that the owner marries her to him, and the owner does so but the slave-girl refuses marriage, what is the ruling?
A) The freeing is invalid because the condition failed.
B) The freeing is valid and the orderer must pay the thousand dirhams.
C) The freeing is valid but the orderer owes nothing.
D) The owner must take legal action to enforce marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a third party's promise to pay for a manumission creates no liability because stipulating payment on a stranger is invalid in acts of manumission, unlike in divorce where such stipulation is valid and binding.

Prohibition of Selling a Mudabbar: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with textual and analogical proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling a mudabbar, cite the hadith evidence, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A mudabbar cannot be sold; his cause of freedom is already active.

The mudabbar is a slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death. This declaration establishes a cause (sabab) of freedom. The Hanafi school rules that this cause is immediate and binding, so selling or gifting the mudabbar would nullify it and is therefore prohibited. The Shafi'i school, however, permits such transactions, viewing the declaration as a mere will. In this lesson, we examine the classical dispute and the Hanafi proofs.

Guided Path
1
Define the mudabbar and tadbir
Identify the slave status (mudabbar) and the act of declaration (tadbir). Understand that tadbir suspends freedom on the condition of the master's death.
Tadbir is not an immediate emancipation but a cause.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted. The primary proof is the hadith: 'The mudabbar is not sold, nor gifted, nor inherited; he is free from one-third.' The reasoning is that tadbir creates an immediate cause of freedom.
The hadith is narrated by al-Darqutni with a weak chain but accepted as evidence.
3
Examine the Hanafi reasoning (ta'lil)
Why is the cause immediate? Because after death the master's capacity for transactions ceases, so the cause must operate now. Unlike other suspended contracts (e.g., contingent divorce), where the delaying of causality is possible because capacity remains at the time of the condition.
The key distinction is between oaths (which intend prevention) and tadbir (which intends freedom).
4
Present the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i allows sale and gift, analogizing tadbir to a will (wasiyyah) which does not prevent transfer. He cites the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet (ﷺ) sold a mudabbar.
The Shafi'i rely on a sahih hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rejects the analogy: the hadith of Jabir involved a mere intention, not a fully executed tadbir. The majority (including Imam Malik) uphold the prohibition. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, the mudabbar cannot be transferred; under Shafi'i, he can.

Source Text

باب التدبير
وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْمُدَبَّرُ لَا يُبَاعُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ وَلَا يُورَثُ وَهُوَ حُرٌّ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ وَلَانَّهُ سَبَبُ الْحُرِّيَّةِ لَا الْحُرِّيَّةَ تَنْبُتُ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ وَلَا سَبَبَ غَيْرُهُ ثُمَّ جَعْلُهُ سَبَبًا فِي الْحَالِ أَوْلَى لِوُجُودِهِ فِي الْحَالِ وَعَدَمِهِ بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ وَلأَنَّ مَا بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ حَالُ بُطْلَانِ أَهْلِيَّةِ التَّصَرُّفِ فَلَا يُمْكِنُ تَأْخِيرُ السَّبَبِيَّةِ إِلَى زَمَانِ بُطْلَانِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ سَائِرِ التَّعْلِيقَاتِ لِأَنَّ الْمَانِعَ مِنَ السَّبَبِيَّةِ قَائِمٌ قَبْلَ الشَّرْطِ لِأَنَّهُ يَمِينٌ وَالْيَمِينُ مَانِعٌ وَالْمَنْعُ هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ وَإِنَّهُ يُضَادُّ وُقُوعَ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعِتَاقِ وَأَمْكَنَ تَأْخِيرُ السَّبَبِيَّةِ إِلَى زَمَانِ الشَّرْطِ لِقِيَامِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ عِنْدَهُ فَافْتَرَقَا وَلِأَنَّهُ وَصِيَّةٌ وَالْوَصِيَّةُ خِلَافَةٌ فِي الْحَالِ كَالْوِرَاثَةِ وَإِبْطَالُ السَّبَبِ لَا يَجُوزُ وَفِي الْبَيْعِ وَمَا يُضَاهِيِهِ ذَلِكَ
ترجمہ: پھر جب وہ مدبر ہو گیا تو اسے بیچنا یا اس کا ہبہ کرنا اور کسی طرح اسے اپنی ملکیت سے نکالنا سوائے اسے آزاد کرنے کے جائز نہیں ہے۔ یعنی اگر فی الفور مدبر کو مکمل آزاد کر دے تو جائز ہوگا جیسے کتابت کی صورت میں مکاتب کو کسی طرح اپنی ملکیت سے نکالنا جائز نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر چاہے تو اسے مکمل آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ جمہور علماء کا یہی قول ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا ہے کہ مدبر کو بیچنا اور ہبہ کرنا وغیرہ ہے کہ مدبر کو نہ فروخت کیا جائے اور نہ ہبہ کیا جائے اور نہ میراث میں اسے پیش کیا جائے۔ بلکہ وہ تہائی ترکہ سے آزاد ہوتا ہے۔ (دار قطنی نے سند ضعیف کے ساتھ اس حدیث کی روایت کی ہے) اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مدبر بنانا آزادی کا سبب ہوتا ہے۔ اب جبکہ موت کے بعد آزادی ثابت ہوتی ہے تو اس کا کوئی سبب بھی چاہئے حالانکہ مدبر بنانے کے سوا دوسرا کوئی سبب نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر اس سبب کو فوری سبب مان لینا اولی ہے۔ کیونکہ مدبر بنانا الحال پایا گیا ہے اور موت کے بعد نہیں پایا گیا ہے۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ موت کے بعد آدمی سے کچھ بھی تصرف کرنے کی صلاحیت ختم ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے صلاحیت اور لیاقت کے ختم ہونے تک سبب پیدا ہونے کی تاخیر کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ یعنی فی الفور آزادی کا سبب ہو گیا۔ بخلاف دوسری تعلیقات کے کیونکہ ان میں سبب ہونے سے مانع موجود ہے۔ یعنی جب تک شرط نہ پائی جائے تب تک اس کی جزاء واقع نہیں ہوسکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ تعلیق تو قسم ہوتی ہے اور قسم روکنے والی چیز ہوتی ہے اور روکنا ہی مقصود ہوتا ہے اور روکنے کے باوجود طلاق یا عتاق کا واقع ہو ناممکن نہیں ہے اور یہاں شرط کے پائے جانے تک سببیت کو موخر کرناممکن ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ شرط پائے جانے کے وقت طلاق یا عتاق کی صلاحیت باقی رہتی ہے۔ اس طرح مدبر بنانے اور دوسری تعلیقات میں فرق ہو گیا۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ مدبر بنانا ایک وصیت ہے اور وصیت میں وراثت کے مثل خلیفہ ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے اور سبب کو باطل کرنا جائز نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ بیع و ہبہ وغیرہ میں باطل کرنا لازم ہے۔
تشریح: مدبر کے حکم کے بارے میں فقہائے کرام کے اقوال اور ان کے دلائل کا خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ جمہور فقہاء کے نزدیک مدبر اس لائق نہیں رہتا ہے کہ ایک شخص کی ملکیت سے نکل کر دوسرے کی ملکیت میں جائے۔ کیونکہ اس میں آزادی کا سبب فی الحال موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر کسی نے اپنے مملوک کو مدبر بنایا اور وہ اس مالک کی موت کے بعد آزاد ہوا تو بالاتفاق اس کے آزاد ہونے کا اس کے سوائے اور دوسرا کوئی سبب نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ اس کے مولی نے اپنی زندگی ہی میں اسے مدبر بنایا تھا۔ مگر یہ سب اس کی موت کے بعد ہی ظاہر ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے مرجانے کے بعد تو اس میں کوئی صلاحیت باقی نہیں رہی بلکہ زندگی میں جس وقت بنایا اسی وقت اس میں آزادی کا سبب پیدا ہو گیا۔ پھر اگر اس کو بیچنا اور ہبہ کرنا وغیرہ جائز ہو تو اس کی آزادی کے سبب کو مٹانا لازم ہو گا۔ حالانکہ یہ جائز نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ مدبر کو بیچنا وغیرہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ لیکن امام شافعی نے ان قیاسات کے مقابلہ میں حضرت جابر رضی اللہ عنہ کی حدیث پیش کی کہ انصار میں سے ایک شخص نے اپنا غلام مدبر بنایا تھا حالانکہ اس کے پاس دوسرا کوئی مال نہ تھا۔ جب یہ خبر رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو پہنچی تو آپ وہاں تشریف لے آئے اور فرمایا کہ کون شخص مجھ سے یہ غلام خریدنا چاہتا ہے۔ بالآخر نعیم بن عبداللہ نے اسے سو درہم سے خرید لیا اور آپ نے وہ رقم پوری اس کے مالک انصاری کو دے دی اور فرمایا کہ تم اس رقم سے اپنا قرض ادا کردو۔ اس کی روایت بخاری و مسلم و ترمذی و نسائی اور دار قطنی نے کی ہے اور یہ حدیث صحیح ہے۔ اور امام احمد و اسحاق کا یہی مذہب بھی ہے۔ مگر اس کا جواب یہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ آپ نے اسے مدبر بنانا جائز نہیں رکھا یعنی ابھی مدبر بنانے کا ارادہ ہی کیا تھا اور آپ نے اسے فروخت کر دیا۔ لیکن اس تاویل میں کچھ اشکال ہے۔ البتہ جمہور علمائے سلف کا وہی قول ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے اور امام مالک کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔
Chapter of Tadbir. Our evidence: The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The mudabbar is not to be sold, nor given as a gift, nor inherited; he is free from one-third (of the estate).' And because (tadbir) is a cause of freedom, not freedom itself; freedom occurs after death, and there is no cause other than this. Then making it a cause immediately is more appropriate because it exists in the present and is absent after death. And because after death is a state of incapacity for transactions, so delaying the causality to a time of incapacity is not possible, unlike other dangling conditions (ta'liqat), because in those the obstacle to causality exists before the condition (since it is an oath and oaths prevent, and prevention is intended, and it contradicts the occurrence of divorce or emancipation; delaying causality to the time of the condition is possible because capacity exists at that time). So they differ. And also because tadbir is a will (wasiyyah), and a will is a deputyship (khilafah) in the present like inheritance, and nullifying the cause is not permissible; and in selling and similar transactions, that (nullification) occurs. Translation: Then when he becomes a mudabbar, selling him, gifting him, or removing him from ownership in any way is not permissible, except by completely freeing him, just as in the case of a mukatab. The majority of scholars hold this. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is permissible to sell or gift a mudabbar because tadbir means suspending freedom on a condition, so just as in other suspensions, sale and gift are not prohibited; and it is a will, and a will does not prevent such actions. Our proof is the hadith 'the mudabbar is not sold nor gifted nor inherited...' and that tadbir is a cause of freedom; since freedom occurs after death, a cause must exist now; delaying the cause until after death is impossible because capacity ends. The difference from other ta'liqat is that those involve oaths where prevention is intended, and they can be delayed until the condition occurs. Further, tadbir is a will, and a will is like inheritance; nullifying its cause is invalid but sale/gift would nullify it. Commentary: Summary of scholars' views: The majority hold that a mudabbar cannot pass from one owner to another because the cause of freedom is present immediately. Imam al-Shafi'i cites the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold a mudabbar, but this is interpreted as the person had only intended tadbir, not actually done it. The majority view is stated in the book, and Imam Malik agrees.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling and the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the sale and gift of a mudabbar. The passage begins by stating the Hanafi position: a mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted, unless the master frees him immediately. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ that 'the mudabbar is not sold, nor gifted, nor inherited; he is free from one-third.' This is a dalil naqli. Additionally, the Hanafi reasoning is that tadbir is a cause (sabab) for freedom, and since freedom occurs after the master's death, the cause must be effective immediately; otherwise, there would be no cause at the time of death. Unlike other suspended conditions (ta'liqat) such as oaths, where the suspension itself prevents immediate effect and can be delayed until the condition is met, in tadbir the condition (death) is inevitable and the intention is to bring about freedom, so the cause must operate at the time of making the mudabbar. Thus, selling or gifting would nullify the cause, which is invalid. The passage then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's counterargument: tadbir is like a will, and a will does not prevent sale; he also cites the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet sold a mudabbar. The Hanafi response is that the person in the hadith had only intended tadbir without enacting it, so it was not a fully executed mudabbar; the majority of scholars, including Imam Malik, uphold the prohibition. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school gives priority to the clear hadith and the principle of preserving the cause of freedom.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death (tadbir).
تَدْبِير (tadbir): The act of making a slave a mudabbar by declaring freedom after death.
سَبَب (sabab): Cause; the legal cause that links an act to its ruling.
تَعْلِيق (ta'liq): Suspension; attaching a ruling to a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is selling a mudabbar prohibited?
A) Because the mudabbar is already free.
B) Because selling would nullify the cause of freedom.
C) Because the master has no ownership rights.
D) Because the slave has consented.

Key Takeaway
A mudabbar cannot be sold or gifted because tadbir creates a binding cause of freedom that cannot be nullified.

Master's Rights over a Mudabbar
Lists permissible actions of a master over a mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four permissible uses of a mudabbar and explain that ownership remains the basis.

Core Idea
A mudabbar is still owned until death — the master retains full usage rights.

This passage clarifies that tadbir (declaration of freedom upon death) does not extinguish ownership. The master may still employ, hire, and if female, have intercourse with or marry off the mudabbar. Understanding this prevents the misconception that a mudabbar is like a free person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage presents actions a master may perform with a mudabbar. The ruling is permissibility (mubah).
2
List the four permissible uses
Memorize: service, hiring, intercourse (if female), and marrying off (if female).
3
Understand the basis
The text states 'because ownership remains.' Tadbir does not cancel ownership; it only prohibits alienation (sale/gift).
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, the master can benefit from the slave's labor, rent out his services, or if female, take her as a concubine or give her in marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَسْتَخْدِمَهُ وَيُوَاجِرُهُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ أَمَةً وَطِيَهَا وَلَهُ أَنْ يُزَوِّجَهَا لِأَنَّ الْمِلْكَ فِيهِ ثَابِتٌ لَهُ وَبِهِ يُسْتَفَادُ وَلَايَةُ هَذِهِ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ
ترجمہ: اور مولی کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ اپنے مدبر غلام سے خدمت لے اور اسے کرایہ پر دے اور اگر وہ باندی ہو تو اس سے وطی کرے اور چاہے تو کسی دوسرے سے اس کا نکاح کر دے۔ یہ اس لئے کہ مدبر میں ابھی تک ملکیت قائم رہتی ہے اور ملک کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے ہی ان تصرفات کا اختیار رہتا ہے۔ تشریح: ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
He said: And the master has the right to employ his (mudabbar) services, and to hire him out, and if (the slave) is a female, he may have intercourse with her, and he has the right to marry her off, because ownership over him/her is established for him, and through it the authority for these actions is derived. Translation: The master has the option to take service from his mudabbar slave, and to rent him out, and if the slave is a female, to have intercourse with her, and if he wishes, to marry her to someone else. This is because ownership over the mudabbar remains, and due to the continuation of ownership, the authority for these actions remains. Commentary: The translation clarifies the meaning.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a short ruling from the matn: despite the tadbir, the master retains full ownership rights over the mudabbar until death. Therefore, he may use the slave's labor, hire him out, and if the slave is a female, he may have sexual relations with her (as his concubine) or marry her off to another. The basis is that tadbir does not cancel ownership; it only restricts the master from alienating the slave (selling/gifting) to protect the prospective freedom. All other rights of ownership remain intact. This is a straightforward ruling without dispute.

Key Terms
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): Slave whose master has declared freedom upon his death.
يَطَأ (yati’u): To have sexual intercourse with a slave woman (concubine) based on ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because the mudabbar is about to be free.
B) Yes, because ownership remains.
C) No, only service is allowed, not hiring.
D) Yes, but only if the slave agrees.

Key Takeaway
A mudabbar remains owned; the master retains all usage rights until death, except alienation.

intermediate
8 min
Mudabbar's Freedom: Ruling, One-Third Limit, and Debt Priority
Explains tadbir's effect as analogous to a will and the consequences for the mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mudabbar's freedom upon the master's death, explain why it is limited to one-third, and apply the rule when debts are present.

Core Idea
Tadbir is a will – the mudabbar is freed only from one-third of the estate; debts take priority.

This passage explains the crucial Hanafi principle that tadbir (a slave's promise of freedom after master's death) is treated as a will (wasiyyah). Therefore, like a bequest, it can only take effect from one-third of the master's estate. The passage also addresses what happens when the mudabbar is the only asset or when there are debts – showing how the master's obligations affect the slave's path to freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Analogy
The passage analogizes tadbir to a will (wasiyyah) because both are gratuitous acts (tabarru') that take effect after death.
This analogy is the basis for the one-third limit.
2
Apply the One-Third Rule
Upon the master's death, the mudabbar is freed from one-third of the master's net estate. The remaineder of his value must be paid by him through work.
This is based on the hadith: 'The mudabbar is free from one-third.'
3
Analyze Insufficient Assets
If the mudabbar is the only asset, he is freed from one-third and must work to pay two-thirds of his value to the heirs.
The mudabbar does not become fully free immediately.
4
Apply the Debt Priority Principle
Debts take precedence over wills. If the master had debts, the mudabbar must work to pay his full value to creditors; he remains a slave until the debt is cleared.
Emancipation cannot be undone, so the mudabbar must earn his freedom through work.

فَإِذَا مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَتَقَ الْمُدَبَّرُ مِنْ ثُلُثِ مَالِهِ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَلِأَنَّ التَّدْبِيرَ وَصِيَّةٌ لِأَنَّهُ تَبَرُّعٌ مُضَافٌ إِلَى وَقْتِ الْمَوْتِ وَالْحُكْمُ غَيْرُ ثَابِتٍ فِي الْحَالِ فَيَنْفُذُ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ حَتَّى لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَالٌ غَيْرُهُ يَسْعَى فِي ثُلُثَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَى الْمَوْلَى دَيْنٌ يَسْعَى فِي كُلِّ قِيمَتِهِ لِتَقَدُّمِ الدَّيْنِ عَلَى الْوَصِيَّةِ وَلَا يُمْكِنُ نَقْضُ الْعِتْقِ فَيَجِبُ رَدُّ قِيمَتِهِ وَوَلَدُ الْمُدَبَّرَةِ مُدَبَّرٌ وَعَلَى ذَلِكَ نُقِلَ إِجْمَاعُ الصَّحَابَةِ
ترجمہ: پھر جب یہ مولی مر جائے تو اس کے تہائی مال میں سے وہ مدبر آزاد ہو جائے گا اوپر بیان کی گئی حدیث کی وجہ سے اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ مدبر کرنا ایک وصیت ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ایک تبرع اور احسان ہوتا ہے جس کی اضافت موت کے وقت کی طرف ہوتی ہے۔ اس میں ابھی تک آزادی کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوا۔ اس بناء پر یہ وصیت اور تدبر موقوف ایک تہائی سے نافذ ہوتی ہے۔ اسی لئے اگر اس غلام کے علاوہ اس مولی کے پاس دوسرا مال نہ ہو تو وہ مدبر اپنی دو تہائی قیمت وارثوں کو ادا کرنے کے لئے کمائی کرے گا اور اگر مولی پر پہلے سے قرض باقی ہو تو پھر مدبر اپنی پوری قیمت کی ادائیگی کے لئے محنت کرے گا۔ یعنی فی الحال وہ کچھ بھی آزاد نہ ہوگا اور مکمل غلام رہے گا۔ کیونکہ قرض کی ادائیگی وصیت سے مقدم ہوا کرتی ہے۔ ساتھ ہی اس کی آزادی کو ختم کرنا بھی ممکن نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے یہ لازم اور واجب ہوا کہ اس سے اس کی قیمت ادا کرائی جائے۔
Then when the master dies, the mudabbar becomes free from one-third of his (the master's) wealth, due to what we narrated and because tadbir is a will (wasiyyah), since it is a gratuitous act (tabarru’) attached to the time of death and the ruling is not established in the present, so it takes effect from one-third. Thus, if the master has no property other than him (the mudabbar), he (the mudabbar) works to (pay) two-thirds of his value (to the heirs). And if the master had a debt, he (the mudabbar) works for his entire value because debt takes precedence over the will, and the emancipation cannot be revoked, so his value must be paid. And the child of a female mudabbar is also a mudabbar. Consensus of the Companions has been reported on this. Translation: Then when the master dies, that mudabbar is freed from one-third of his wealth due to the hadith mentioned above and because tadbir is a will. It is a gratuitous act attached to the time of death; the ruling of freedom is not established in the present. Therefore, it takes effect from one-third. So if the master has no other property besides this slave, the mudabbar will work to pay two-thirds of his value to the heirs. And if the master had a debt, then the mudabbar will work to pay his entire value, i.e., he will not be free at all and remain a full slave, because debt payment takes precedence over the will. At the same time, revoking his freedom is not possible, so it becomes necessary to make him pay his value.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage explains the outcome of tadbir upon the master's death. The mudabbar becomes free only from one-third of the master's net estate, because tadbir is treated like a will (wasiyyah) — it is a gratuitous transfer effective after death, and wills are limited to one-third of the estate. If the mudabbar is the only asset, he is freed from one-third and must work to pay two-thirds of his value to the heirs. Debts take priority over wills, so if the master had debts, the mudabbar must work to pay his full value to creditors; he remains a slave until the debt is paid (but becomes free afterward). The emancipation itself cannot be undone, so the mudabbar is not sold but must earn his freedom by work. The passage also states that the child of a female mudabbar is also a mudabbar (i.e., the child follows the mother's status), and this is reported as consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
وَصِيَّة (wasiyyah): A will or bequest; here, tadbir is analogized to a will because it is a gratuitous act effective after death.
يَسْعَى (yas'a): He works/tries to earn money (to pay off a debt or value); the mudabbar works to pay the heirs or creditors.
مُدَبَّر (mudabbar): A slave whom the master has promised freedom after the master's death (tadbir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master dies and the only asset is a mudabbar worth 300 dirhams, but the master had debts of 400 dirhams, what happens to the mudabbar?
A) He is freed immediately without payment.
B) He is freed from one-third (100 dirhams) and must work to pay the rest to the heirs.
C) He remains a slave and must work to pay his full value (300 dirhams) to the creditors.
D) He is sold to pay the debt.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir is a will: the mudabbar is freed only from one-third of the estate; debts take precedence, requiring the mudabbar to work to pay his full value if needed.

Child of Mudabbira is Mudabbar by Ijma
States the ruling and proof of ijma for child of mudabbira being mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the child of a mudabbira is mudabbar and explain how the consensus of the Companions (ijma) serves as its proof.

Core Idea
The child of a mudabbira shares her tadbir — the ruling is established by the silent consensus of the Companions.

In this passage from the Sharh of Hidayah, we encounter a specific ruling concerning tadbir: when a female slave is given tadbir (declared free upon the master's death), her children after that declaration also become mudabbar. The author cites the consensus of the Companions as proof. Let us examine how this consensus is established and what it means for the child's status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the main hukm: the child of a mudabbira is mudabbar. Note that this is a declaratory ruling establishing legal status.
The ruling applies to children born after the tadbir declaration.
2
Identify the dalil
The proof cited is 'ijma al-sahaba' (consensus of the Companions). Find the Arabic phrase: وَعَلَى ذَالِكَ نُقِلَ إِجْمَاعُ الصَّحَابَةِ.
Ijma is a primary source in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the nature of the ijma
The commentator explains that this is a silent consensus (ijma sukuti): the ruling is transmitted from several Companions and no opposing narration exists. This establishes ijma.
The narrators include 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, al-Zuhri, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
4
Distinguish absolute vs conditional tadbir
The passage ends by noting that this ruling applies to absolute tadbir (mutlaq). Conditional tadbir (muqayyad) will be discussed separately.
This transition avoids overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التدبير . ۳۸ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم قیمت کی مزدوری کرائی جائے اور مدبرہ باندی کی اولاد بھی مدبر ہوگی۔ اس مسئلہ پر تمام صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہم کا اجماع منقول ہے۔ تشريح وَعَلَى ذَالِكَ نُقِلَ إِجْمَاعُ الصَّحَابَةِ "مدیرہ کی اولاد کے بھی مدبر ہونے پر صحابہ کرام کا اجماع منقول ہے۔" فائدہ اس کے اجماع ہونے کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ عبدالرزاق نے حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہا اور امام زہری اور سعید بن المسیب رحمہم اللہ سے ور امام محمد نے امام ابراہیم نفی سے اس حکم کی روایت کی ہے اور صحابہ کرام میں سے کسی سے اس کے خلاف روایت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ دلیل ہے اس بات پر کہ سب نے اسی پر اتفاق کیا ہے۔ اگر چہ صریح روایت مجھے نہیں ملی ہے۔ یہ تفصیل مد بر مطلق کے بارے میں تھی اور اگر کسی نے قید کے ساتھ مدبر بنایا ہو تو اسے مدبر مقید کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس کا بیان سامنے آتا ہے۔
Chapter of Tadbir. 38. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Six. The price of hiring is given [as compensation], and the child of a mudabbira slave-girl is also mudabbar. The consensus of all the noble Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, is transmitted upon this ruling. Explanation: And upon that the consensus of the Companions is transmitted: "The consensus of the Companions is transmitted upon the child of a mudabbira also being mudabbar." Benefit: The detail of its being a consensus is that 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), Imam al-Zuhri, and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab (may Allah have mercy on them), and Imam Muhammad from Imam Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, this ruling. And from any of the Companions, no narration contrary to this is found. Therefore, this is evidence that all agreed upon it, even if I have not found an explicit transmission. This detail was concerning the absolute mudabbar. And if someone made a mudabbar with a condition, then he is called a conditional mudabbar. Its explanation comes forth.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh (commentary) of Hidayah. The primary ruling is that when a slave-girl (bāndī) is made a mudabbira (i.e., her master declares that she will be free upon his death), and she subsequently bears a child, that child also becomes mudabbar — that is, the child will be free upon the master's death as well. The proof cited is the consensus (ijmā') of the Companions. The commentator then elaborates on the nature of this consensus: it is based on the silence of other Companions on the matter, as the ruling is transmitted from several authorities (Ibn 'Umar, al-Zuhri, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, Ibrahīm al-Nakha'ī) by reliable narrators like 'Abd al-Razzaq and Imam Muhammad. Since no Companion opposed it, it is taken as agreed upon. This ruling applies to absolute tadbīr (tadbīr muṭlaq). The passage then transitions to conditional tadbīr (tadbīr muqayyad), which is distinguished from the absolute case.

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): The act of a master declaring that his slave will be free upon his death.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who has been granted tadbir by his master.
مدبرة (mudabbira): A female slave who has been granted tadbir.
إجماع (ijma): The consensus of the Companions, used here as a proof for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof cited for the ruling that the child of a mudabbira is mudabbar?
A) A hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him)
B) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions
C) Analogy (qiyas) to other forms of emancipation
D) Istihsan

Key Takeaway
The child of a mudabbira slave-girl is mudabbar by the silent consensus of the Companions, meaning the child follows the mother's tadbir status automatically.

Conditional Tadbir (Tadbir Muqayyad) and Its Ruling
Defines conditional tadbir and rules on sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define conditional tadbir, distinguish it from absolute tadbir, and state the Hanafi ruling regarding the permissibility of selling the slave.

Core Idea
A conditional tadbir on an uncertain condition does not make the slave a mudabbar and does not prevent sale.

In this passage, the commentator explains the difference between absolute tadbir (tadbir mutlaq) and conditional tadbir (tadbir muqayyad). While an absolute tadbir immediately restricts the master's ability to sell the slave because death is certain, a conditional tadbir tied to an uncertain event leaves the slave freely saleable. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rulings of tadbir in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
Read the examples of conditional tadbir: tying emancipation to a specific illness, a specific journey, or a time limit like 'within a year'. The slave is not a mudabbar in these cases.
The condition must be uncertain for this ruling.
2
Contrast with absolute tadbir
Note why absolute tadbir prevents sale: death is inevitable, so the cause (sabab) is established immediately. In conditional tadbir, the cause is not established due to uncertainty.
The phrase 'li taraddud fī tilka al-ṣifa' captures the reason.
3
Determine the ruling when condition is met
If the master dies under the specified condition, the slave becomes free from the one-third of the estate. Understand that tadbir takes effect at the last moment of life when the condition is actualized.
The one-third rule applies because it is akin to a will.
4
Handle the special case of an extremely long time
If the condition is a time limit so long that death is inevitable (e.g., 100 years), it is treated like absolute tadbir. The slave becomes a mudabbar immediately and sale is not allowed.
The threshold is when 'the like of him does not generally live to it'.
5
Note the authority
This ruling is from the riwayah of Hasan ibn Ziyad from Imam Muhammad, and it is also the well-known view of Imam Malik. 'Allama 'Ayni confirms it.
It is nawadir (rare) but agreed upon by later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تدبیر کوموت کے ساتھ معلق کرنے کا حکم وَإِنْ عَلَقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفَةٍ مِثْلُ أَنْ يَقُولَ إِنْ مِتْ مِنْ مَرَضِي هَذَا أَوْ سَفَرِي هَذَا أَوْ مِنْ مَرَضِ كَذَا فَلَيْسَ بِمُدَبَّرٍ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُهُ لِأَنَّ السَّبَبَ لَمْ يَنْعَقِدْ فِي الْحَالِ لِتَرَدُّدٍ فِي تِلْكَ الصِّفَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْمُدَبَّرِ الْمُطْلَقِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَلَّقَ عِتْقُهُ بِمُطْلَقِ الْمَوْتِ وَهُوَ كَائِنٌ لَا مَحَالَةَ فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى عَلَى الصِّفَةِ الَّتِي ذَكَرَهَا عَتَقَ كَمَا يَعْتِقُ الْمُدَبَّرُ مَعْنَاهُ مِنَ التَّلْثِ لِأَنَّهُ ثَبَتَ حُكْمُ التَّدْبِيرِ فِي آخِرِ جُزْءٍ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ حَيَاتِهِ لِتَحَقُّقِ تِلْكَ الصِّفَةِ فِيهِ فَلِهَذَا يُعْتَبَرُ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ وَمِنَ الْمُقَيَّدِ أَنْ يَقُولَ إِنْ مِتْ إِلَى سَنَةٍ أَوْ عَشَرَ سِنِينَ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ إِلَى مِائَةِ سَنَةٍ وَمِثْلُهُ لَا يَعِيشُ إِلَيْهِ فِي الْغَالِبِ لِأَنَّهُ كَالْكَائِنِ لَا مَحَالَةَ. فائدہ یہ روایت حسن سے منفی میں مذکور ہے اور امام مالک کا قول مشہور بھی یہی ہے۔ علامہ عینی نے ایسا ہی فرمایا ہے۔ تشريح .... وَإِنْ عَلَقَ التَّدْبِيرَ بِمَوْتِهِ عَلَى صِفة ... الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
The ruling of suspending tadbir upon his death with a condition. And if he suspends tadbir upon his death with a condition, such as he says: 'If I die from this illness of mine, or this journey of mine, or from such an illness,' then he is not a mudabbar, and selling him is permissible because the cause has not been established in the present due to uncertainty in that condition, unlike the absolute mudabbar, because his emancipation is suspended upon absolute death, and that is inevitable. Then if the master dies upon the condition he mentioned, he becomes free just as the mudabbar becomes free. Its meaning is from the one-third, because the ruling of tadbir is established in the last part of his life due to the actualization of that condition in him. Therefore, it is considered from the one-third. And from the conditional [tadbir] is that he say: 'If I die within a year or ten years,' for what we mentioned, unlike the case when he says: 'Within a hundred years,' and the like of him does not generally live to it, because it is like the inevitable. Benefit: This narration is mentioned in the riwayah of Hasan from Naf'i, and this is also the well-known saying of Imam Malik. 'Allama 'Ayni said likewise. Explanation: ... 'And if he suspends tadbir upon his death with a condition...' etc., the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and definition of conditional tadbir (tadbīr muqayyad). The commentator explains: If a master says, 'If I die from this specific illness' or 'on this journey', the slave does not become a mudabbar immediately; he can be sold because the condition is uncertain. This contrasts with absolute tadbir (tadbīr muṭlaq), where death is certain. If the master dies exactly under the specified condition, the slave becomes free from the one-third of the estate, because the tadbir is confirmed at the last moment of life when the condition is met. The same applies if the condition is a time limit, like 'if I die within a year', because death within that time is uncertain. However, if the time is unrealistically long, like a hundred years, it is treated as absolute tadbir because death is inevitable within that period. The faidah (benefit) notes that this ruling comes in the riwayah of Hasan ibn Ziyad, and it is also the famous view of Imam Malik. The taḥrīr (commentary) from 'Allama 'Ayni confirms this.

Key Terms
تدبير مقيد (tadbir muqayyad): A tadbir that is conditioned upon a specific death (e.g., from a particular illness or journey) or a specific time frame.
تدبير مطلق (tadbir mutlaq): An absolute tadbir that is not conditioned on any specific death or time; it takes effect upon the master's death inevitably.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a master says 'if I die within a year, you are free', is the slave considered mudabbar during the master's life?
A) Yes, because a year is a definite time.
B) No, because death within a year is uncertain.
C) Yes, because it is a conditional tadbir.
D) No, because the condition is not fulfilled yet.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a conditional tadbir on an uncertain event does not make the slave a mudabbar and does not prevent sale; only absolute or inevitably realized conditions do.

Umm Walad: Status and Rulings
Explains how a slave-girl becomes umm walad and the legal consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main consequences of a slave-girl becoming umm walad and explain the legal proofs (hadith and qiyas) that establish them.

Core Idea
An umm walad cannot be sold; she is freed upon her master's death.

This passage from the chapter on istīlād (umm walad) explains the moment a slave-girl becomes an umm walad and the immediate and deferred legal effects. The ruling is established through both a prophetic hadith and a rational analogy (qiyas) to the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationships. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the Hanafi position on the inviolability of the mother of one's child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a slave-girl giving birth to her master's child. The ruling is that she immediately becomes an umm walad, which carries two consequences: (1) she cannot be sold or given away, and (2) she will be freed upon the master's death.
2
Locate the dalil naqli
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Her child set her free.' This statement informs us that the child causes her freedom, and from that we derive the immediate prohibition of sale as a partial consequence.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (zanni al-thubut, qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'a'taqaha' (set her free) is informative; it establishes that the child brings about freedom. The prohibition of sale is a necessary implication because if she is destined for freedom, she cannot be sold.
This is an example of istidlal (inference) from the hadith.
4
Examine the qiyas analogy
The text presents a qiyas: the mixing of the master's and slave-girl's fluids through the child creates a partial ownership (juz'iyya), similar to the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationships (musahara). This partial ownership prohibits sale immediately but, being weak, defers full freedom until death.
The illa is the mixing of fluids to the point of indistinguishability.
5
Apply the ruling to edge cases
The passage concludes that the same ruling applies if the master owns only part of the slave-girl, because istilad is indivisible, being based on lineage (nasab) which is from the male side.

باب الاستيلاد ترجمہ: باب ام ولد ہونے کے بیان میں باندی ام ولد کب بنتی ہے اور اس کے متعلق احکام إِذَا وَلَدَتِ الْأَمَةُ مِنْ مَوْلَاهَا فَقَدْ صَارَتْ أُمَّ وَلَدٍ لَهُ لَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُهَا وَلَا تَمْلِيكُهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَعْتَقَهَا وَلَدُهَا أَخْبَرَ عَنْ إِعْتَاقِهَا فَيَثْبُتُ بَعْضُ مَوَاجِبِهِ وَهُوَ حُرْمَةُ البَيْعِ وَلِأَنَّ الْجُزْئِيَّةَ قَدْ حَصَلَتْ بَيْنَ الْوَاطِئِ وَالْمَوْطُوءَةِ بِوَاسِطَةِ الْوَلَدِ فَإِنَّ الْمَاءَيْنِ قَدِ اخْتَلَطَا بِحَيْثُ لَا يُمْكِنُ الْمَيْزُ بَيْنَهُمَا عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ فِي حُرْمَةِ الْمُصَاهَرَةِ إِلَّا أَنَّ بَعْدَ الْإِنْفِصَالِ تَبْقَى الْجُزْئِيَّةُ حُكْمًا لَا حَقِيقَةً فَضَعُفَ السَّبَبُ فَأَوْجَبَ حُكْمًا مُؤَجَّلًا إِلَى مَا بَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ وَبَقَاءُ الْجُزْئِيَّةِ حُكْمًا بِإِعْتِبَارِ النَّسَبِ وَهُوَ مِنْ جَانِبِ الرِّجَالِ فَكَذَا الْحُرِّيَّةُ تَثْبُتُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ لَا فِي حَقِّهِنَّ حَتَّى إِذَا مَلَكَتِ الْحُرَّةُ زَوْجَهَا وَقَدْ وَلَدَتْ مِنْهُ لَا يَعْتِقُ بِمَوْتِهَا وَثُبُوتُ عِلْقٍ مُؤَجَّلٍ يُثْبِتُ حَقَّ الْحُرِّيَّةِ فِي الْحَالِ فَيَمْتَنِعُ جَوَازَ الْبَيْعِ وَإِخْرَاجَهَا لَا إِلَى الْحُرِّيَّةِ فِي الْحَالِ وَيُوْجِبُ عِتْقَهَا بَعْدَ مَوْتِهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا كَانَ بَعْضُهَا مَمْلُوكًا لَهُ لِأَنَّ الْإِسْتِيْلَادَ لَا يَتَجَزَّى فَإِنَّهُ فَرْعُ النَّسَبِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ بِأَصْلِهِ
Chapter of Istilad. Translation: Chapter concerning the status of umm walad: when does a slave-girl become umm walad and the rulings related to it. When the slave-girl gives birth from her master, then she has become his umm walad. It is not permissible to sell her nor to give her into the ownership of another, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Her child set her free.' He informed about her emancipation, so some of its consequences are established, and that is the prohibition of sale. And because partial ownership (juz'iyya) has occurred between the coitus-performer and the one with whom coitus is performed through the child. For the two fluids have mixed such that differentiation is not possible between them, as is known in the prohibition of in-laws. However, after separation, the partial ownership remains as a ruling, not in reality, so the cause became weak, thus it necessitated a postponed ruling until after death. And the remaining of partial ownership as a ruling is by consideration of lineage, and it is from the side of males. Likewise, freedom is established concerning them, not concerning their females, such that if a free woman owns her husband, and she has given birth from him, he does not become free upon her death. And the establishment of a postponed connection establishes the right of freedom in the present, so the permissibility of sale and her removal from his ownership without immediate freedom becomes prohibited, and necessitates her emancipation after his death. And likewise if part of her is owned by him, because istilad does not divide; for it is a branch of lineage, so it is considered by its root.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on istīlād (umm walad). It defines umm walad: a slave-girl who bears a child from her master. The primary ruling is that she cannot be sold or gifted to another. The proof is the hadith: 'Her child set her free,' which indicates that the child causes her freedom, so the sale is prohibited as a partial consequence. A rational proof (qiyas) is also provided: the partial ownership (juz'iyya) between master and slave-girl through the child — since their fluids mix, they become as if partially owned by each other, analogous to the prohibition of marriage due to in-law relationship (muṣāhara). However, after the child is born, this partial ownership is only a legal construct, not real, so the effect is delayed until the master's death. The freedom from this partial ownership is established only from the male side (the husband/master), not from the female side. Hence, if a free woman owns her husband, he does not gain freedom upon her death because the lineage is established from the male side. The ruling that she cannot be sold applies immediately, while full freedom occurs after the master's death. If the master only owned a part of the slave-girl, the same ruling applies because istīlād is indivisible, being based on lineage.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who has borne a child to her master, thereby acquiring special status: she cannot be sold and will be freed upon her master's death.
استيلاد (istilad): The act of a slave-girl bearing a child from her master, making her umm walad.
جزئية (juz'iyya): The legal concept of partial ownership or connection between the master and slave-girl through the mixed fluids.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the child's lineage is established from the father, which is why the freedom effect is from the male side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the immediate legal effect when a slave-girl becomes umm walad?
A) She becomes free immediately
B) She cannot be sold or given away
C) She must be sold
D) She can be sold but not freed

Key Takeaway
The sale of an umm walad is haram because her child establishes a legal bond of partial ownership, resulting in delayed freedom upon the master's death.

Establishing Lineage of Umm Walad's Child: The Necessity of a Claim
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over necessity of claim for umm walad's child lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on establishing lineage of an umm walad's child and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the distinction in purpose of intercourse.

Core Idea
Lineage of an umm walad's child requires the master's claim; intention of pleasure, not procreation, differentiates from marriage.

This passage addresses a fundamental dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a master must explicitly claim a child born to his umm walad. The ruling hinges on the purpose of intercourse with a slave versus a free wife. Understanding this distinction clarifies not only the legal rule but the deeper objectives (maqasid) that shape family law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the lineage of an umm walad's child is not established unless the master claims the child. Only after acknowledging a first child does subsequent lineage become automatic.
This contrasts with free marriage where lineage is automatic.
2
Identify the opponent's view and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that lineage is established without a claim, analogizing to marriage: intercourse alone suffices, especially since the master has greater access to the slave.
Shafi'i uses qiyas (analogy) with marriage.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes the purpose: intercourse with a free wife is intended for procreation (nasl), whereas with a slave it is primarily for pleasure (shahwa). Additionally, bearing a child diminishes the slave's market value, creating an economic disincentive that makes a claim necessary.
The response highlights a difference in the illa (effective cause).
4
Determine the practical consequence
If the master dies without claiming the child, the child is not his heir and remains a slave (or free but not linked). In Shafi'i, the child is free and inherits.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

ترجمہ اور اس ام ولد کے بچہ کا نسب اس مولی سے اس وقت ثابت ہوگا جبکہ یہ خود بھی اس نسب کے ہونے کا دعویٰ کرے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اگر چہ وہ اس کا دعوی نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ جب صرف نکاح کر لینے سے ہی اس عورت کے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے تو وطی کے بعد بدرجہ اولی ثابت ہونا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ اس سے وطی کرنے کا زیادہ اختیار اور سہولت ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی کی وطی سے مقصود اپنی خواہش پوری کرنی ہوتی ہے۔ اولاد مقصود نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں کچھ رکاوٹیں بھی ہوتی ہیں یعنی اگر اس سے اولاد ہوگئی تو بازار میں اس کی قیمت یا تو بالکل ختم ورنہ کم تو ضرور ہو جائیگی۔ اس لئے اس سے نسب کا دعویٰ کرنا ضروری ہے جیسے اس باندی سے جو صرف ملکیت میں ہو اور اس سے وطی نہ کی گئی ہو۔ بخلاف عقد نکاح کے کہ اس سے اصل مقصود حصول اولاد ہے اس لئے منکوحہ کی اولاد کے لئے نسب کا دعویٰ کرنا ضروری نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر جب کسی باندی کے ایک بچہ کے نسب کا بھی اقرار کر لیا تو وہ ام الولد ہو چکی۔ اس کے بعد بچہ ہونے پر اس کے اقرار کے بغیر بھی بچہ کا اس سے نسب ثابت ہوتا رہے گا۔ یعنی مولیٰ نے جب پہلے بچہ کے نسب کا اس طرح اقرار کر لیا کہ یہ میرا بچہ ہے تو اس کے بعد جب بھی دوسرا بچہ ہو گا وہ اسی مولیٰ کے نسب سے ہوگا کیونکہ پہلے بچہ کا دعویٰ کرنے سے یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ باندی کو بستر پر لانے سے یہی مقصود تھا۔ اس لئے یہ باندی بھی دوسری منکوحہ کی طرح اس کی شریک بستر ہوگئی۔ تشريح وَ لَا يَنْبُتُ نَسَبُ وَلَدِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْتَرف به ... الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔

مولی ام ولد کے بچہ کی نفی کر دے تو کیا حکم ہوگا

إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا نَفَاهُ يَنْتَفِى بِقَوْلِهِ لِأَنَّ فِرَاشَهَا ضَعِيفٌ حَتَّى يَمْلِكُ نَقْلَهُ بِالتَّزْوِيجِ بِخِلَافِ الْمَنْكُوحَةِ حَيْثُ لَا يَنْتَفِي الْوَلَدُ بِنَفْيِهِ إِلَّا بِاللَّعَانِ لِتَأَكُّدِ الْفِرَاشِ حَتَّى لَا يَمْلِكُ إِبْطَالَهُ بِالتَّزْوِيجِ وَهَذَا الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَاهُ حُكْمٌ فَأَمَّا الدِّيَانَةُ فَإِنْ كَانَ وَطِئَهَا وَحَصَّنَهَا وَلَمْ يَعْزِلْ عَنْهَا يَلْزَمُهُ أَنْ يَعْتَرِفَ بِهِ وَيَدَّعِى لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ أَنَّ الْوَلَدَ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ عَزَلَ عَنْهَا أَوْ لَمْ يُحَصِّنْهَا جَازَ لَهُ أَنْ يَنْفِيَهُ لِأَنَّ هَذَا الظَّاهِرَ يُقَابِلُهُ ظَاهِرٌ آخَرُ هَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَفِيهِ رِوَايَتَانِ أُخْرَيَانِ عَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ وَعَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ ذَكَرْنَاهُمَا فِي كِفَايَةِ الْمُنْتَهِي

ترجمہ البتہ منکوحہ کے بچہ اور ام ولد کے بچہ میں یہ فرق ہوتا ہے کہ اگر مولیٰ نے ام ولد کے دوسرے بچہ کی نفی کر دی تو صرف زبانی انکار سے ہی نفی ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کا فراش ہونا کمزور ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ مولی کو یہ اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اپنے پاس سے علیحدہ کر کے کسی اجنبی مرد سے اس کا نکاح کر دے۔ بخلاف منکوحہ کے کہ اس کے بچہ کے نسب کی اس کے شوہر سے نفی نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ اگر نفی کرنا ہو تو اس کے لئے لعان کرنا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ بیوی ہونے اور بستر کے اعتبار سے اس کا حق مضبوط ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے کہ اپنی بیوی کا دوسرے مرد سے نکاح کر کے خود سے اس کو دور کر دے۔ پھر یہاں تک ہم نے جو کچھ ذکر کیا ہے وہ ظاہری حکم ہے۔ کیونکہ دیانت داری کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اگر اپنی باندی سے وطی کر لی اور باندی کو محفوظ رکھا۔ اور انزال کے بغیر اس سے جدا نہیں ہوتا رہا تو مولی پر یہ واجب ہوتا ہے کہ اس کے بچہ اور اس کے نسب کا اعتراف کرے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر بات یہی ہے کہ بچہ اسی کا ہے۔ البتہ اگر بغیر انزال اس سے جدا ہوتا رہا یا اس کو محفوظ نہیں رکھا تو بھی اس بچہ کے نسب سے انکار کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس ظاہر کے مقابلہ میں دوسرا ظاہر بھی موجود ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایسی ہی روایت پائی گئی ہے۔ اور اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو یوسف و محمد سے دوسری دو روایتیں منقول ہیں۔ جن کو ہم نے کفایت المنتہی میں ذکر کر دیا ہے۔ تشریح إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا نَفَاهُ یُنْتَفَى بِقَوْلِهِ لِأَنَّ فِرَاشَهَا ضَعِيفٌ ... الخ ترجمہ سے مطلب واضح ہے۔
Chapter of concubinage. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya volume six. His purpose from her, so no need for claim. If she comes after that with a child, his lineage is established without acknowledgment, meaning after his acknowledgment of the first child, because by the claim of the first child the child is determined as his purpose from her, so she becomes a bed (firash) like a married woman after marriage. Translation: The lineage of the child of this umm walad to this master will be established only when he himself claims that lineage. Imam al-Shafi'i said that his lineage will be established even if he does not claim it, because when by mere marriage the lineage of a woman's child is established, then after intercourse it should be established a fortiori, because there is more authority and ease of intercourse from him. And our proof is that from a slave-girl's intercourse with the master, the purpose is to fulfill his desire; progeny is not intended, because there are some obstacles in it, that is, if she bears a child, her market value will either be completely lost or at least reduced. Therefore, it is necessary to claim lineage from her, like the slave-girl who is purely owned and with whom no intercourse has occurred. Unlike the marriage contract, where the primary purpose is obtaining progeny; therefore, for the offspring of a married woman, claiming lineage is not necessary. Then, when he acknowledges the lineage of one child of a slave-girl, she becomes umm walad. After that, when she gives birth, the child's lineage from him is established without his acknowledgment. That is, when the master acknowledged the lineage of the first child in this manner that 'this is my child', then whenever a second child is born, it will be from the lineage of the same master, because by claiming the first child it became apparent that bringing the slave-girl to bed was for this purpose. Therefore, this slave-girl, like a second married woman, became his bed-partner. Commentary: 'And the lineage of her child is not established unless he acknowledges it...' etc. The meaning is clear from the translation. (Heading) What is the ruling if the master denies the child of his umm walad? Except that if he denies him, he is denied by his statement, because her bed (firash) is weak, to the extent that he has the power to transfer her by marriage, unlike the married woman, where the child is not denied by his denial except by li'an, due to the strength of the bed, to the extent that he does not have the power to annul it by marriage. And this that we have mentioned is the external ruling (hukm). As for religious duty (diyanatan), if he had intercourse with her and guarded her and did not practice coitus interruptus from her, it is obligatory upon him to acknowledge him and claim him, because the apparent circumstance is that the child is from him. And if he practiced coitus interruptus from her or did not guard her, it is permissible for him to deny him, because this apparent circumstance is counterbalanced by another apparent circumstance. Thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifah. And there are two other narrations from Abu Yusuf and from Muhammad; we have mentioned both in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Translation: However, there is this difference between the child of a married woman and the child of an umm walad: that if the master denies the second child of the umm walad, the denial is effected merely by his statement, because the bed (firash) of the umm walad is weak, to the extent that the master has the authority to separate her from himself and marry her to a stranger. Unlike the married woman, where the lineage of her child is not denied from her husband by his denial; rather, if he wants to deny, he must perform li'an, because her right as a wife and in terms of the bed is strong, to the extent that the husband does not have the authority to marry his wife to another man and thus remove her from himself. Then, what we have mentioned so far is the external ruling. Because the requirement of piety is that if he had intercourse with his slave-girl and kept her guarded and did not separate from her without ejaculation, then it is obligatory upon the master to acknowledge her child and his lineage, because the apparent circumstance is that the child is his. However, if he separated from her without ejaculation or did not guard her, then it is permissible for him to deny this child's lineage, because this apparent circumstance is counterbalanced by another apparent circumstance. This is the narration from Abu Hanifah. And regarding this issue, there are two other narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, which we have mentioned in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Commentary: 'Except that if he denies him, he is denied by his statement, because her bed is weak...' etc. The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya covers the rules of lineage (nasab) for children of an umm walad. It begins by stating the general principle: if the master acknowledges the first child, subsequent children are automatically attributed to him without a new claim, because the first claim establishes the purpose behind the relationship. The passage then presents a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i: Shafi'i holds that lineage is established automatically without a claim, drawing analogy from marriage where intercourse establishes lineage. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the purpose of intercourse with a slave is pleasure, not offspring; hence a claim is necessary unless the first child has already been acknowledged. Regarding denial of paternity, the passage explains that the master can deny a child by mere statement because the umm walad's status as a bed (firash) is weak—unlike a wife, where denial requires li'an. However, from a religious perspective (diyanatan), if the circumstances strongly suggest the child is his (e.g., consistent intercourse with protection), he must acknowledge it. Two additional narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are referenced but not detailed here.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, and the master has acknowledged the child. She becomes free upon the master's death.
فراش (firāsh): The legal 'bed' or marital relationship that attributes a child to a man. In this context, the firāsh of an umm walad is weak compared to a married woman.
نفي (nafy): Denial of paternity. For umm walad, nafy is effective by mere statement; for a wife, it requires li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must the master claim the first child of his umm walad for lineage to be established?
A) Because the master's intercourse with a slave is not considered lawful without a claim.
B) Because the primary purpose of intercourse with a slave is pleasure, not procreation, and the child would diminish her value.
C) Because the child of a slave is always a slave until freed by a judge.
D) Because the umm walad is considered a wife and therefore lineage is automatic.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a claim to establish lineage for the first child of an umm walad, distinguishing the purpose of intercourse from marriage, where lineage is automatic.

Denying Paternity of Umm Walad's Child: Weak Firash and Diyanatan Considerations
Ruling on denial of paternity for umm walad and distinction between external and diyanatan rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the master can deny paternity of an umm walad's child by mere statement, distinguish this from a wife's case requiring li'an, and state the diyanatan conditions that make acknowledgment wajib.

Core Idea
A master can deny paternity of his umm walad's child by mere statement because her firash is weak, unlike a wife who requires li'an.

This part of the passage explains the master's ability to deny paternity of an umm walad's child through mere statement, contrasting it with the strong firash of a married woman that necessitates li'an. It also distinguishes between the external ruling (hukm) and religious obligation (diyanatan), where circumstances may obligate the master to acknowledge the child even if he could legally deny.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on denial for umm walad
The master can deny the child of his umm walad simply by saying 'this is not my child.' The denial is effective immediately, without legal process.
This is because her firash is weak.
2
Contrast with married woman
For a wife, denial of paternity requires li'an (mutual imprecation), because her firash is strong.
The husband cannot simply deny by statement.
3
Explain the reason for weak firash
The firash of an umm walad is weak because the master has the authority to marry her to someone else, effectively removing her as his bed partner. This is not possible with a wife.
The ability to transfer indicates weak firash.
4
Examine the diyanatan ruling
Despite the external ruling, if the master had intercourse with the umm walad without using coitus interruptus and guarded her (i.e., no other man had access), then it is wajib upon him religiously to acknowledge the child, because the apparent circumstance is that the child is his.
This is based on the principle that the apparent (zahir) indicates paternity.
5
Note the exceptions
If he practiced coitus interruptus or did not guard her, then denial is permissible even diyanatan, because the appearance is counterbalanced by another appearance.
There are also two other narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
